1 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Calloway


No. 26204


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


207 W. Va. 43; 528 S.E.2d 490; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 206


November 3, 1999, Submitted  
December 16, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Concurring Opinion by Chief Justice Starcher Filed January 6, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Tod J. Kaufman, Judge. Case No. 95-F-341.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from conviction in the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) for sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of breaking into a woman's home and sexually assaulting her. On appeal, he contended that the trial court should have admitted DNA evidence showing that the woman had sex with someone else. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the rape shield law was properly applied because the victim's sexual conduct was irrelevant to whether defendant had assaulted her.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the rape shield law was properly applied to exclude irrelevant evidence of the victim's sexual conduct.

 

2 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Carvey v. West Virginia State Bd. of Educ.


No. 26217


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


206 W. Va. 720; 527 S.E.2d 831; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 201


October 5, 1999, Submitted  
December 15, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Irene C. Berger, Judge. Civil Action No. 97-C-2306.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, IN PART, AND REVERSED, IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public training center challenged the orders of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which held that W. Va. Code § 18A-3-2c(i), which governed mandatory training for school principals, was unconstitutional as applied; and that appellant, not the individual county boards of education, was responsible for paying a stipend to principals who attended the center outside of their contract periods of employment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant public training center challenged the circuit court's determination that W. Va. Code § 18A-3-2c(i), which governed mandatory training for school principals, unconstitutionally differentiated between principals with short and long term contracts; and that appellant, not the individual county boards of education, was responsible for paying a stipend to principals who attended the center outside of their contract periods of employment. The court held that the classification in § 18A-3-2c(i) was a rational one based on social, economic, historic, and geographic factors, bore a reasonable relationship to a proper governmental purpose, and that all persons within the classes were treated equally. In addition, the plain language of the code indicated that appellant, and not the individual county boards of education, was the entity responsible for paying a stipend to participants.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; appellant was responsible for paying a stipend to participants, and the classification of short and long term contractors did not violate constitutional guarantees of equal protection.

 

3 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. Ireland


No. 26440


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


207 W. Va. 1; 528 S.E.2d 197; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 202


November 3, 1999, Submitted  
December 15, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Paul Zakaib, Jr., Judge. Civil Action 98-C-1816.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) dismissing appellant's complaint regarding the calculation of his public employee pension benefits.


OVERVIEW: While appellant was a state employee, a statute was amended to change the method of calculation of pension benefits. The change reduced the amount of benefits appellant would have received. Appellant contended that he had been deprived of his contractual rights. The lower court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the change in the method of calculating public employee pension benefits could have unconstitutionally impaired appellant's contractual rights if appellant relied to his detriment upon promised benefits. The court further ruled that the statute of limitations for contract actions was applicable and that the complaint had been timely filed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, holding that a change in the method of calculating public employee pension benefits may unconstitutionally impair contractual rights if detrimental reliance has occurred, and that the complaint had been filed within the applicable statute of limitations for contract actions.

 

4 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Crispen v. West Virginia Secondary Schs. Activities Comm'n


No. 25958


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


206 W. Va. 486; 525 S.E.2d 677; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 178


October 6, 1999, Submitted  
December 9, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Mason County. Honorable Clarence L. Watt, Judge. Case No. 97-C-128.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pro se appellants, as natural guardians and next friends of their teenage son, sought review from an order of the Mason County Circuit Court (W. Va.) dismissing appellants' civil action against appellee defendants on the ground that venue for the case did not lie in the court's county of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant home-schooling parents requested and received permission for their son to play on the local high school's varsity soccer team. After one soccer season, appellee Secondary Schools Activities Commission (Commission) ruled appellants' son ineligible to participate in athletics. Appellants moved to another county, but son again was denied permission to play sports given the Commission's ruling. In their new county of residence, appellants, on behalf of their son, filed unlawful discrimination and defamation suit against Commission and other appellees that had no connection to the county of filing. Appellees moved to dismiss on ground that circuit court lacked venue to try the action. With appellant father and sons' approval, court dismissed action. As to appellant mother, court dismissed on lack of venue ground. Appellants challenged trial court's dismissal. Court affirmed, holding that appellants' residence, without more, was not a valid ground of venue under W. Va. Code § 56-1-1(b) (1986).


OUTCOME: Court affirmed circuit court's granting of appellees' motion to dismiss appellants' unlawful discrimination and defamation suit for lack of venue, holding that appellants' residence, without more, was not valid ground of venue in absence of statute or other principle of law authorizing it. Venue must exist by virtue of law.

 

5 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stephens


No. 25893


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


206 W. Va. 420; 525 S.E.2d 301; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 154


November 2, 1999, Submitted  
December 3, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissenting Opinion by Justice Maynard Filed December 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Nicholas County. Hon. Gary Johnson. Criminal Case No. 97-F-12.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Nicholas County (West Virginia), which in a jury trial denied appellant's motion for mistrial and convicted appellant on two charges: first-degree sexual assault, W. Va. Code § 61-8B-3 (1991), and sexual abuse by a custodian, W. Va. Code § 61-8D-5 (1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellant allegedly sexually molested a 4-year-old boy that appellant was babysitting. During the trial, the prosecutor, in the rebuttal portion of his closing argument, suggested to the jury that defense counsel believed that appellant was guilty. The trial court denied appellant's motion for a mistrial. Appellant was convicted of first-degree sexual assault and sexual abuse by a custodian. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction, because the trial court abused its discretion in not granting a mistrial. There was sufficient unfair prejudice in the prosecutor's argument to the jury, to the effect that defense counsel had failed to deny that appellant had committed the offenses charged.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed, because the trial court abused its discretion by denying appellant's motion for a mistrial after the prosecutor suggested to the jury that defense counsel believed that appellant was guilty.

 

6 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rygh


No. 26195


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


206 W. Va. 295; 524 S.E.2d 447; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 150


October 6, 1999, Submitted  
December 3, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Rygh v. McBride, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 21167 (4th Cir. W. Va., Sept. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Logan County. Hon. Roger Perry. Case No. 97-F-105-P.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Logan County (West Virginia), which allowed appellant's juvenile justice records to be obtained and used by the prosecution against appellant and convicted appellant of felony murder and of conspiracy to commit aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of two felony murder counts and of conspiracy to commit aggravated robbery. The prosecution used a copy of a juvenile petition from appellant's juvenile justice records in cross-examination of appellant's mother to demonstrate that despite her assertions that he was a "good kid," she had filed a petition for delinquency against him. The petition itself was apparently not introduced into evidence. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The trial court did not err by allowing appellant's juvenile justice records to be obtained and used by the prosecution against appellant, because the records were used for the purpose of impeachment during the cross-examination of a witness for appellant and were not used in the prosecution's "case-in-chief."


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, because juvenile justice records were used to impeach appellant's witness and were not used in the prosecution's "case-in-chief."

 

7 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


No. 25980


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


208 W. Va. 144; 539 S.E.2d 87; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 134


September 22, 1999, Submitted  
November 17, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Chief Justice Withdrew His Right to File a Concurring Opinion November 1, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wood County Honorable George W. Hill, Jr., Judge Criminal Action No. 98-F-5.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant challenged his convictions and sentences in the Circuit Court of Wood County (West Virginia) of multiple counts stemming from his flight to avoid arrest resulting in an aggregated sentence of over seven years in the county jail.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of multiple counts stemming from his flight to avoid arrest. After being sentenced to an aggregate term of over seven years in the county jail, he appealed. The court held that it could not consider the trial court's denial of appellant's proffered jury instruction because he had not properly objected at trial. The sentences were within statutory limits and not impermissible factors influenced the lower court's sentencing. Since simultaneous sentences were to be served consecutively by statute and the cases did not involve unlimited sentences or a life recidivist statute, proportionality principles were not applied. The court could not evaluate the merits of his claim of deprivation in the county jail absent information for comparison. The legislature intended to create two flight offenses; one with a vehicle and one without. Defendant's various instances of flight were separate and distinct occurrences. The convictions and sentences were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed because, inter alia, the denial of appellant's jury instruction was not considered since he had not objected at trial; the sentences were within statutory limits and no impermissible factors influenced sentencing; and sentence proportionality did not apply.

 

8 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Rist v. Underwood


Nos. 26653, No. 26654


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


206 W. Va. 258; 524 S.E.2d 179; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 127


October 20, 1999, Submitted  
November 3, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended November 15, 1999. Concurring Opinion by Starcher, C.J. Dated December 7, 1999. Justice Miller, sitting by temporary assignment, today withdrew his right to file a dissenting opinion in the above-captioned cases. As Corrected January 26, 2000.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, petitioners sought a writ of mandamus and/or prohibition requiring respondent governor to appoint an individual to the office of Supreme Court Justice who was not barred from the office by W. Va. Const. art. VI, § 15, rather than his selected appointee, a current legislator.


OVERVIEW: Respondent governor appointed a current legislator to the office of Supreme Court Justice, although during the appointee's term of office the legislature had approved an increase in salary for the justices. Petitioners filed suit seeking a writ of mandamus and/or prohibition requiring respondent governor to appoint an individual to that office who was not barred by the Emoluments Clause, W. Va. Const. art. VI, § 15. The court issued the writ, finding that the Emoluments Clause, with one exception, rendered a member of the legislature ineligible to be elected or appointed to a civil office for profit that had been created, or the emoluments of which had been increased, during the legislator's term of office. The sole exception operated to allow an otherwise ineligible legislator to gain public office through popular election. The provision in question would only apply to a legislator's current term of office.


OUTCOME: Petition was granted and a writ of mandamus was issued requiring respondent governor to discharge his duty by appointing a justice who was constitutionally qualified to hold the office.

 

9 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Canterbury v. Paul


No. 25890


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


205 W. Va. 665; 520 S.E.2d 662; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 97


June 1, 1999, Submitted  
July 14, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Concurring and Dissenting Opinion by Justice Starcher Filed October 15, 1999.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner jail authority sought a writ of prohibition alleging that respondent magistrate was wrongfully refusing to impose statutory court costs pursuant to W. Va. Code § 50-3-2 (1996).


OVERVIEW: Respondent magistrate informed the administrative director's office that he was troubled by certain court cost assessments and challenged the assessment of $ 55.00 in court costs in certain criminal cases as required by W. Va. Code § 50-3-2 (1996). Respondent would only impose the fee in cases where a criminal defendant was convicted after a trial, and not where the conviction was the result of a plea. The office informed respondent as well as others that they were to impose the fee in all criminal cases, whether by plea or by trial. Petitioner jail authority sought a writ of prohibition alleging that respondent exceeded the jurisdiction of the magistrate court by refusing to assess the fee in all criminal proceedings pursuant to section 50-3-2 thereby depriving the regional jail and prison development fund of its dedicated source of revenue. The court found that respondent's refusal to assess the statutory fee where a conviction was a result of a plea was erroneous as a matter of law because section 50-3-2 clearly evinced a legislative intent that magistrates were to collect court costs upon conviction in all criminal cases.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for writ of prohibition as moulded because respondent's refusal to impose the court costs ignored the legislative intent of the statute. The court ordered respondent to make a good faith effort to collect the court costs, which it previously failed to assess for convictions resulting from a plea, and to assess the $ 55.00 in court costs in all criminal cases resulting in a conviction, whether by plea or trial.

 

10 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Affiliated Constr. Trades Found. v. Vieweg


No. 26364


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


205 W. Va. 687; 520 S.E.2d 854; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 88


June 29, 1999, Submitted  
July 14, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner construction foundation requested a writ of prohibition or mandamus to prohibit respondent commissioner from dismissing civil actions instituted by the Workers' Compensation Division and having any further involvement in the actions. Further, petitioner sought to direct respondent commissioner and respondent council to promulgate rules and regulations governing the conduct of litigation commenced by respondent commissioner.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner construction foundation sought a writ prohibiting respondents, commissioner, bureau, and council, from dismissing civil actions instituted by the Workers' Compensation Division against certain corporate entities under theories of imputed liability for delinquent workers' compensation premiums, penalties, and interest. The court found that, in dismissing the actions at issue, respondent commissioner was performing a purely administrative function. Because the writ of prohibition never issues against administrative officials performing purely administrative acts, a remedy by prohibition was not available. Further, the court found that respondent commissioner had a fiduciary obligation to maintain the workers compensation fund. However, the possibility that the dismissal of the civil actions would impair the workers' compensation fund and render the fund unable to fulfill its purpose was purely speculative. Therefore, petitioner did not show that respondent commissioner violated his fiduciary duty to maintain the workers' compensation fund. Accordingly, the petition was denied.


OUTCOME: The writ of prohibition or mandamus was denied because the dismissal of lawsuits involved was within the discretion of the respondent commissioner. Further, respondent commissioner's dismissal of the civil actions was not arbitrary or capricious. There was no clear legal duty for respondents, commissioner, bureau, and council, to do the things, which petitioner construction foundation sought to compel.

 

11 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Guthrie


No. 25790


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


205 W. Va. 326; 518 S.E.2d 83; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 62


May 11, 1999, Submitted  
June 25, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Irene C. Berger, Judge. Criminal Action No. 96-F-364.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), for sexual assault of his spouse under W. Va. Code § 61-8B-6(b) (1997). Defendant claimed that DNA evidence was improperly excluded under West Virginia's rape shield statute, W. Va. Code § 61-8B-11(b) (1997), W. Va. R. Evid. 404 and 612, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV and W. Va. Const. art. III, § 14. Defendant also sought to exclude his custodial statements.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault of his wife, in violation of W. Va. Code § 61-8B-6(b) (1997). On appeal, the court rejected defendant's argument that he had the right to impeach the victim using DNA evidence that included sperm from at least two other men at the victim's medical exam after the alleged rape. The court held that the DNA evidence was properly excluded under West Virginia's rape shield statute, W. Va. Code § 61-8B-11(b) (1997), because the victim did not testify about her prior sexual conduct. The court also held that W. Va. R. Evid. 404 and 612 did not require admission of the DNA evidence and that defendant's due process rights were not violated. The court also rejected defendant's claim that his Miranda rights were violated by admission of statements made while being transported by police. The court concluded that Miranda warnings were not required after arrest until police interrogation began and specifically overruled West Virginia cases that held otherwise. The court held that the issue of whether the prosecutor engaged in misconduct in charging him with second degree sexual assault under W. Va. Code § 61-8B-4 (1997) was not properly preserved at trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for sexual assault of his spouse was affirmed. The court held that DNA evidence was properly excluded under the West Virginia rape shield statute because the victim did not make her previous sexual conduct an issue at trial. The court also held that West Virginia rules of evidence did not require admission of the DNA evidence and that defendant's constitutional right to due process was not violated.

 

12 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 25815


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


205 W. Va. 552; 519 S.E.2d 835; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 44


May 5, 1999, Submitted  
June 15, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fayette County. Honorable John W. Hatcher, Jr., Judge. Civil Action No. 97-F-117.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Fayette County (West Virginia) that sentenced her to 50 years upon her voluntary plea conviction of attempted aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was involved in an attempt to rob a victim that resulted in his death. Pursuant to a plea agreement with the state, appellant pled guilty to attempted aggravated robbery in exchange for the state dismissing the murder charge pending against her. Sentencing was left to the court and she was sentenced to 50 years in the state penitentiary. On appeal, she claimed that the circuit court violated W. Va. Const. art. III, § 5 by sentencing her to a term of 50 years for attempted aggravated robbery. She contended that the 50-year sentence was unconstitutionally excessive and disproportionate to the character and degree of the offense she committed. The court concluded that although appellant did not personally shoot the victim, she was responsible for setting the chain of events in motion that led to his death. The sentence imposed did not shock the conscience of the court and society, and the circuit court considered the violent and dangerous nature of the crime committed by appellant. Appellant's sentence was appropriate and not constitutionally disproportionate. The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court that sentenced appellant to 50 years for a conviction of attempted aggravated robbery was affirmed because appellant's sentence was appropriate and not constitutionally disproportionate.

 

13 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mann


No. 25767


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


205 W. Va. 303; 518 S.E.2d 60; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 40


May 4, 1999, Submitted  
June 11, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Mingo County. Honorable Elliott E. Maynard, Judge. Indictment No. J95-F2.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order entered by the Circuit Court of Mingo County (West Virginia), which sentenced defendant to 30 years of imprisonment after the jury found him guilty of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was being treated for back pains and discomfort caused by ingesting cocaine and drinking beer, the attending nurse observed a gun in defendant's jacket. Defendant left the hospital before police arrived. Before defendant returned to pick up a friend, a nearby store was robbed by a man wearing clothing reportedly identical to that worn by defendant. An eyewitness also observed the license plate number of the vehicle that defendant was driving that night. The jury found defendant guilty of aggravated robbery, and the trial court sentenced him to 30 years imprisonment. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the circumstantial evidence was sufficient to support the jury verdict. The prosecution's late disclosure of photographs depicting the license plate number was not prejudicial because such evidence was redundant. Defendant's direct testimony invited cross- examination into his cocaine addiction. No prejudice or manifest injustice arose from the prosecution's opening and closing remarks. Under the subjective test for proportionality, defendant's sentence within the statutory limits did not shock the conscience of the court and society.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery because circumstantial evidence that defendant's clothing matched that worn by the robber and an eyewitness' observation of the license plate number of the car reportedly driven by defendant was sufficient evidence of defendant's guilt. Defendant's sentence was not subject to appellate review because it was within statutory limits and not based on any impermissible factor.

 

14 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Morgan v. City of Wheeling


No. 25420


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


205 W. Va. 34; 516 S.E.2d 48; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 36


February 16, 1999, Submitted  
June 4, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ohio County. Honorable Ronald E. Wilson, Judge. Civil Action No. 96-C-440.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city police officer sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Ohio County (West Virginia), which granted summary judgment to appellees, a city and its police department, and which also declared that W.Va. Code § 8-5-11 (1969) permitted municipalities to establish residency requirements for municipal employees. The court found that a city residency ordinance was valid in appellant's action seeking declaratory relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a police officer employed by appellee city. Appellant filed a request with appellee police department to relocate outside of city limits. His request was denied pursuant to the residency requirements of Wheeling City, W. Va., Ordinance 9046, which required all city employees to be residents of either the city of Wheeling or Ohio County. Appellant filed suit and sought declaratory relief, challenging the validity of Ordinance 9046 on several grounds. Appellees filed a motion for summary judgment, which the trial court granted. The decision of the lower court was affirmed on appeal. The appellate court determined that the residency requirement at issue was rationally related to the legitimate government purposes for which it was enacted. The appellate court held that the ordinance, enacted pursuant to W. Va. Code § 8-5-11 (1969), did not penalize the fundamental right to travel; did not burden the privileges and immunities protected by the Privileges and Immunities Clause; and did not violate the right of equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV or W. Va. Const. art. III, § 10.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court granting appellees' summary judgment and declaring appellee city's police residency ordinance valid was affirmed. The court found that the residency requirement was not irrational, did not penalize the fundamental right to travel, did not burden appellant's privileges and immunities rights, and did not violate his equal protection rights.

 

15 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. ACF Indus., Inc. v. Vieweg


No. 25142


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


204 W. Va. 525; 514 S.E.2d 176; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 3


September 8, 1998, Submitted  
February 5, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employers sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent commissioner of workers' compensation to apply statutory amendments, which governed the eligibility and benefit amounts of permanent total disability awards, to employees' claims filed after the amendments' effective date.


OVERVIEW: The West Virginia Legislature enacted a comprehensive revision of the West Virginia workers' compensation law. The amendments included a requirement that an employee have a distinct minimum threshold level of medical impairment before he or she could request a permanent total disability (PTD) award. The amendment also reduced the amount and duration of PTD awards. Petitioner employers wanted these amendments to apply to their employees' claims that were filed after the amendments became effective. However, respondent commissioner of workers' compensation took the position that the case law and statutes in existence on the date of injury or date of last exposure applied to all workers' compensation claims with injury or last exposure dates prior to the amendments' effective date. Petitioners filed for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent to apply the amendments to claims that had a date of injury or last exposure prior to amendments' effective date. The court found that petitioners had no right to the requested relief because respondent did not have a legal duty to apply the amendments in the manner propounded by petitioners.


OUTCOME: Writ of mandamus to compel respondent commissioner of workers' compensation to apply statutory amendments to employees' permanent total disability claims was denied because the court accorded deference to respondent's interpretation of the statute in the absence of legislative guidance.

 

16 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reed


No. 25356


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


204 W. Va. 520; 514 S.E.2d 171; 1999 W. Va. LEXIS 2


January 12, 1999, Submitted  
January 29, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prosecuting attorney filed for a writ of prohibition to prevent the dismissal by the Circuit Court of Wood County, West Virginia of sexual assault charges against respondent criminal defendant. The dismissal was based on the fact that a variance existed between the dates of the offenses contained in the indictment and the dates proven at trial.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner prosecuting attorney filed for a writ of prohibition to prevent the dismissal of sexual assault charges against respondent accused. The trial court granted respondent's motion for judgment of acquittal after the evidence at trial proved the dates of the offenses were different than those in the indictment. The court granted the writ of prohibition, finding that the mere discrepancies in the dates was not sufficient to grant acquittal where time was not of the essence of the offense. The court determined that time was not an element of the sexual assault offenses and that petitioner was under no obligation to prove that the sexual assaults occurred on the specific dates listed in the indictment. The court did conclude that a variance between the indictment and the proof would be considered material if the variance misled respondent in presenting his defense to the charges and exposed him to the danger of being put in jeopardy again for the same offense. However, the court determined that respondent did not provide any specifics in how the discrepancies in the dates prejudiced his defense.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of prohibition preventing the dismissal of the sexual assault charges against respondent accused, finding that a variance between the indictment dates and the proof of the dates adduced at trial was not prejudicial to the respondent because time was not of the essence for the crimes charged.

 

17 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Chevy Chase Bank v. McCamant


No. 25049


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


204 W. Va. 295; 512 S.E.2d 217; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 216


October 27, 1998, Submitted  
December 14, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Christopher C. Wilkes, Judge. Civil Action No. 96-C-102.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (West Virginia), which denied appellant's motion for a new trial or, in the alternative, to alter or amend the judgment. Appellee creditor bank sought to collect unpaid credit card charges from appellant.


OVERVIEW: After appellant debtor's credit card account became chronically delinquent, appellee creditor bank filed suit to collect from appellant $ 5,115.28 plus interest in unpaid credit card charges. Appellant answered the complaint with a general denial and served a 10 count amended counterclaim alleging various violations of the West Virginia Consumer Credit and Protection Act (WVCCPA), W.Va. Code § 46A-1-101 et seq. The circuit court found that appellee was entitled to $ 5,115.28 plus prejudgment interest and statutory interest subsequent. Finding that appellee violated the WVCCPA by telephoning appellant's neighbor and falsely stating that there was a banking emergency, the circuit court imposed the statutory penalty of $ 1000.00 against appellee for its violation of the WVCCPA. After its motion for a new trial or, in the alternative, to alter or amend judgment was denied, appellant sought review of the judge's decision. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment, holding that the WVCCPA was not preempted by federal law from regulating appellee's debt collection practices because there was no express or implied preemption in the federal laws or regulations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment, which denied appellant debtor's motion for a new trial or, in the alternative, to alter or amend the judgment entered against him in an action by appellee creditor bank to collect unpaid credit card charges. The court held that the West Virginia Consumer Credit and Protection Act was not preempted by federal law.

 

18 of 754 DOCUMENTS


University of West Virginia Bd. of Trustees ex rel. West Virginia Univ. v. Graf


No. 24972


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


205 W. Va. 118; 516 S.E.2d 741; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 218


September 15, 1998, Submitted  
December 14, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Dissenting Opinion by Justice McGraw filed July 21, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Irene C. Berger, Judge. Civil Action No. 94-AA-163.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the University of West Virginia Board of Trustees on behalf of West Virginia University, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which granted appellee faculty member attorney fees and lost wages in excess of one million dollars in a case arising from appellee's grievance that he was not permitted to pursue outside employment as an emergency room physician.


OVERVIEW: Appellee faculty member filed a grievance with the West Virginia Education and Employees Grievance Board (board) regarding the fact that he was not permitted to pursue outside employment as an emergency room physician. An administrative law judge ruled in favor of appellee finding that he had the right to continue outside employment. The circuit court subsequently upheld an award of lost wages to appellee in excess of $ 1,000.000.00 and awarded appellee attorney fees. Appellant sought review of the decision after its motion to amend the judgment was denied. The court found that because West Virginia University would be responsible for any award of attorney fees to appellee and public funds would be involved, constitutional immunity applied. However, because appellee sought attorney fees accumulated in litigating a tort action, the court held that appellee's claim fell under the exception to constitutional immunity which allowed suits seeking recovery under and up to the limits of the state's liability insurance coverage. The court reversed the circuit court's award of attorney fees which were in excess of the state's $ 1,000.000.00 liability insurance coverage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment granting appellee faculty member an award of lost wages in excess of $ 1,000,000 pursuant to his grievance that he was not permitted to pursue outside employment. The court reversed the circuit court's judgment granting appellee attorney fees, holding that to do so would place appellee's recovery in excess of the state's liability coverage and was barred by the state's constitutional immunity.

 

19 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Rice v. Underwood


No. 25166


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


205 W. Va. 274; 517 S.E.2d 751; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 222


October 7, 1998, Submitted  
December 11, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable A. Andrew MacQueen, Judge. Civil Action No. 97-MISC-424.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commissioner sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which denied his requests for a writ of mandamus and injunctive relief in an action seeking an order prohibiting appellee governor from removing appellant from his appointed position as a member of the West Virginia Racing Commission before the expiration of his term, and declaring the appointment of a successor null and void.


OVERVIEW: Appellant commissioner was an appointed member of the West Virginia Racing Commission; however, after being elected, appellee governor removed appellant from that position, pursuant to W.Va. Code § 6-6-4, and named a successor. Appellant filed suit seeking a writ of mandamus and injunctive relief to prohibit appellee from removing appellant before the expiration of his term and to declare the appointment of the successor null and void. Appellant sought review of the lower court's decision after it denied the requested relief. The court affirmed the trial court's decision and found that the members of the commission had no special status based on their quasi-judicial functions, either through statutory or common law, granting them protection from § 6-6-4 which allowed the removal of appointed officials at a governor's will and pleasure. Furthermore the court found that § 6-6-4 was constitutional and did not violate separation of powers. The court also held that § 6-6-4 did not conflict with W.Va. Code § 19-23-4(b), providing for the appointment and term of members of the commission and when the two statutes were read together appellee had the power to remove appellant at will.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying appellant commissioner a writ of mandamus and injunctive relief, because the quasi-judicial functions of the racing commission did not exempt its members from the general removal law that allowed appellee governor to remove appellant at his will. The court found that the statute was constitutional and that it did not conflict with the statute regarding the appointment of the commission's members.

21 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bull


No. 25179


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


204 W. Va. 255; 512 S.E.2d 177; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 179


November 10, 1998, Submitted  
December 4, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tucker County. Hon. C. Reeves Taylor, Judge. Hon. Andrew N. Frye, Jr., Judge. Criminal Actions Nos. 95-F-11 and -12.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, husband and wife, appealed from their conviction by the Circuit Court of Tucker County, West Virginia, for creating an emergency situation for an incapacitated adult by means of intentional neglect, a violation of W.Va. Code § 9-6-15(b) (1984).


OVERVIEW: Defendants intentionally left the wife's father, a substantially disabled and incapacitated person, alone in their home during a period of extremely hot weather with no arrangements for him to be fed or cared for. Defendants contended on appeal that the language of W.Va. Code § 9-6-15(b) was unconstitutionally vague, that the indictments lacked specificity, and that the evidence of their intent was insufficient to sustain a conviction. The appellate court found that the trial court did not err in denying defendants' motion to grant a judgment of acquittal. The statutory language would have clearly alerted a reasonable person to the undesirable, even reprehensible, conduct that was subject to criminal prosecution and penalty. The language was also not so broad as to arguably include, chill, or penalize socially desirable or protected conduct. Defendants were apprised of the charges against them by indictments which tracked the statutory language of the charged offense and by a bill of particulars that set forth the details. Finally, there was strong evidence from which a jury could have inferred intentional neglect and a pattern of neglect over a substantial period of time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court .

State v. Shelton


No. 25019


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


204 W. Va. 311; 512 S.E.2d 568; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 186


September 9, 1998, Submitted  
December 3, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Christopher W. Wilkes, Judge. Civil Action No. 97-P-48.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Jefferson County, West Virginia, which rejected his petition for home incarceration, despite his fitness for an alternative sentence, upon the grounds that he was unable to pay the mandatory home incarceration costs made mandatory by W.Va. Code § 62-11B-5(7) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to violating W.Va. Code § 17C-5-2, by driving a tractor with a blood alcohol concentration at nearly double the level which gave rise to a statutory presumption of intoxication. He was sentenced to an eight week term of incarceration, and granted a stay of enforcement of the incarceration order to allow him to petition the circuit court for an alternative sentence of home incarceration. The supreme court held that it was inappropriate for the circuit court to have used defendant's ability to pay the costs of home incarceration as a pre-sentencing standard. It held that mandating imprisonment in a jail or correctional facility for indigents, who would otherwise be granted home incarceration, was unconstitutional. Defendant's ability to pay should have been one of the factors which the circuit court used to set the fee for home incarceration, but his economic misfortune should not have been the criteria upon which incarceration was imposed instead of home confinement.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the circuit court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

23 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Anstey v. Davis


No. 25155, No. 25156, No. 25157, No. 25158


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


203 W. Va. 538; 509 S.E.2d 579; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 173


September 8, 1998, Submitted  
November 20, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fayette County. Honorable John W. Hatcher, Jr., Judge. Civil Action No. 97-C-408 (H).



DISPOSITION: No. 25155 - Writ denied.

No. 25156 - Writ denied.

No. 25157 - Writ denied.

No. 25158 - Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, petitioner prisoners sought writs of habeas corpus against respondent prison officials for depriving them of personal property without due process of law and for retaliation for filing litigation. Appellant prisoner challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Fayette County (West Virginia), which dismissed his petition for a writ on the same basis.


OVERVIEW: The inmates argued that the prison officials deprived them of their personal computers without due process of law and in retaliation for litigation by "jailhouse lawyers." The court held that prison inmates had no constitutional right to possess personal computers in their cells. No laws or regulations granted the inmates a property interest in the possession of computers. The prison's policies were insufficient to create a property interest, and thus due process of law was not necessary. The right of meaningful access to the courts did not include the right of inmates to possess computers in their prison cells because prohibiting the possession of personal computers in inmates' cells was a reasonable restriction. The inmates did not have a claim under contract law for detrimental reliance on the prison's policy allowing computers because the relationship between prison administrators and the inmates under their charge was not a contractual one. The inmates failed to state claims for retaliation because each inmate failed to allege that he exercised a fundamental right for which he suffered the removal of his computer.


OUTCOME: The inmates' petition for habeas corpus and appeal were denied.

 

24 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Duncan


No. 24485


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


204 W. Va. 411; 513 S.E.2d 459; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 171


September 15, 1998, Submitted  
November 18, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Hon. Herman G. Canady, Judge. Case Nos. 95-F-34 and 95-F-35.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order entered in the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which dismissed indictments charging defendants with criminal fraud under both W.Va. Code § 5A-3-30 (1990) and W. Va. Code § 61-3-24 (1994).


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that the indictments were fatally flawed on the ground that both the State and a contractor were listed as victims under W. Va. Code § 5A-3-30 (1990), which penalized only criminal fraud committed directly against the State, and W. Va. Code § 61-3-24 (1994), which penalized only criminal fraud committed against parties other than the State. Reversing the order dismissing the indictments, the court ruled that charging defendants with a violation of W. Va. Code § 61-3-24 (1994) was not improper because, though the statute did not specifically provide for the State being a potential victim, the statute did not preclude the State from being a member of the group that the legislature sought to protect. The court agreed that the State was the only intended victim under W. Va. Code § 5A-3-30 (1990), but that the erroneous listing of the contractor as a victim did not render the indictments sufficiently flawed to warrant their dismissal. Noting that W.Va. R. Crim. P. 7(e) authorized amendment of indictments, the court concluded that the trial court should have permitted the State to amend the indictments because defendants would not have been prejudiced.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the indictments against defendants. The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to reinstate the indictments and to permit amendment of the indictments.

State ex rel. West Virginia Deputy Sheriffs' Ass'n v. Sims


No. 25212


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


204 W. Va. 442; 513 S.E.2d 669; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 169


September 8, 1998, Submitted  
November 16, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sheriffs' association filed an application for a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, Executive Secretary of the State of West Virginia Consolidated Public Retirement Board (board) and its members, to comply with provisions of the West Virginia Deputy Sheriff Retirement System Act (Act), W. Va. Code § 7-14D-1 to -30 (1998).


OVERVIEW: The Act provided for the transfer of retirement fund assets from the public employees retirement system (PERS) to the deputy sheriff fund (Fund). The board refused to permit the transfer of assets for those employed prior to the statutory date, and also refused to allow those individuals hired before July 1, 1998 to enroll in the Fund. The court granted the writ of mandamus. Section 7-14D-8(d) of the Act required the board to seek a judicial determination by writ of mandamus of issues regarding the transfer of assets. The court held that such a statutory "test case" amounted to an advisory opinion. Although courts could not give advisory opinions, the court decided to cautiously address the substantive issues raised by the association. The court held that the board had a fiduciary duty to monitor funds and assets and take all actions necessary to protect those funds. Despite a remote possibility that the transfer of assets from PERS to the Fund could impair the fiscal solvency of PERS, the transfer of assets was not barred because an impairment could be prevented if the board properly performed its fiduciary duty.


OUTCOME: The court granted the association's petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the board and its members to comply with the provisions of the West Virginia Deputy Sheriff Retirement System Act.

Charleston Urban Renewal Auth. v. Courtland Co.


No. 25015


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


203 W. Va. 528; 509 S.E.2d 569; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 155


September 16, 1998, Submitted  
October 30, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Hon. Herman Canady, Judge. Civil Action No. 97-MISC-76.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which held that appellee redevelopment authority acted within its legitimate power when it exercised its power of eminent domain over appellant's property.


OVERVIEW: Appellee redevelopment authority (authority) exercised its power of eminent domain pursuant to W. Va. Code § 16-18-2, to acquire land owned by appellant company following the authority's determination that the property was wholly located with an area that was designated as a slum or blighted area by the city council. The trial court upheld the authority's findings and the company challenged the decision. The company contended the authority improperly exercised its power of eminent domain, the authority had not stated a legitimate intended public use for the property acquired, and the trial court erred in failing to make factual findings with respect to permitting the eminent domain proceeding to go forward. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. First, the court held that it was within the authority's purview in accordance with § 16-18-2 to exercise its power of eminent domain. Secondly, the court held the authority adequately stated a legitimate intended public use for the property acquired through eminent domain. Lastly, the court held the trial court was not required to make factual findings with respect to the authority's power to exercise the use of eminent domain.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment holding that appellee redevelopment authority properly exercised its eminent domain power of appellant company's property.

Kessel v. Leavitt

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother, maternal grandparents, uncle appealed a judgment, upon a jury verdict, for plaintiff father from the Circuit Court of Cabell County (West Virginia) on the issues of fraud and tortious interference with the father's parental or custodial relationship.


OVERVIEW: Following the Canadian adoption of the mother's and father's biological child without the father's knowledge or consent, the father brought an action alleging that the mother, the maternal grandparents, the uncle, and the mother's attorney acted fraudulently and tortiously interfered with the father's parental rights. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the father sufficiently stated a cause of action for fraud by averring that the mother, maternal grandparents, uncle, and the mother's attorney intentionally, purposefully, and maliciously prevented the father from obtaining any pertinent information regarding the child's birth or subsequent pre-adoptive placement and that they continued a scheme to impair and frustrate the father's efforts to ascertain the whereabouts of his son; and (2) the father sufficiently stated a cause of action that the maternal grandparents, uncle, and the mother's attorney tortiously interfered with his parental or custodial relationship with his minor child but that such a claim could not be maintained against the mother because both parents were equally entitled to establish or maintain a parental or custodial relationship with their child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State ex rel. Stull v. Davis


Nos. 24459, 24460, 24461, 24462, 24463, 24464, 24465, 24466, 24467, 24468, 24469, 24470, 24472


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


203 W. Va. 405; 508 S.E.2d 122; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 138


March 24, 1998, Submitted  
July 17, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Justice McCuskey's concurring/dissenting opinion Filed September 23, 1998.



DISPOSITION: WRITS GRANTED AS MOULDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a writ of mandamus proceeding, petitioner inmates sought a prompt transfer from their holding facilities in the regional and county jails to the West Virginia Division of Corrections (division). The inmates contended that they were sentenced to terms of confinement in the division facilities and their holding in the jails by respondent corrections department was unlawful and denied them the rehabilitative programs to which they were entitled.


OVERVIEW: The inmates were lodged in regional and county jails in the state while awaiting transfers to the division. Substantial delays in the transfers occurred because of alleged overcrowding of the division's facilities. The inmates asserted that their continued incarceration in regional and county jails was unlawful and resulted in a denial of the rehabilitative programs to which they were entitled. The inmates sought prompt transfer to the division facilities or release from confinement. The court held that relief in mandamus was warranted and that the inmates were entitled to prompt transfer to the division facilities. The court directed the commissioner of the division to submit to the court within 60 days a full and complete plan for the immediate transfer to the division facilities of at least half of all inmates currently lodged in the jails who were awaiting such transfer. In addition, the court directed the commissioner to submit to the court, as soon as practicable, a full and complete long-range plan for the transfer of such inmates to the division facilities. The special master was ordered to review the plans and promptly submit reports as to their adequacy.


OUTCOME: The court granted mandamus relief ruling that the inmates were entitled to prompt transfer to the division facilities and requiring submission of plans for such transfers.

State ex rel. W. Va. Reg'l Jail & Corr. Facility Auth. v. W. Va. Inv. Mgmt. Bd.


No. 25134


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


203 W. Va. 413; 508 S.E.2d 130; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 134


June 3, 1998, Submitted  
July 17, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] WRIT GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator correctional facility authority petitioned for a writ of mandamus to evaluate the constitutionality of H.R. 4702, 1998 Leg., (W. Va. 1998), directing respondent management board to invest pension funds in the correctional facility for the completion of statewide facility construction and renovation.


OVERVIEW: H.R. 4702, 1998 Leg., (W. Va. 1998) directed a management board to invest $ 150,000,000 of the pension system funds in a correctional facility authority for the completion of statewide construction and renovation of facilities. When the board refused on the ground that H.R. 4702 violated constitutional prohibitions against state impairment of contracts, the facility authority sought a writ of mandamus, which the court granted. The court held that H.R. 4702 did not unconstitutionally impair the contract between the state and the members and beneficiaries of the state retirement system because H.R. 4702 did not affect the sufficiency of funds provided under the plan or the promised pensions. The court found that H.R. 4702 was simply another modification made by the legislature to the statutorily prescribed investment vehicles available to the management board in its management of pension funds and that nothing in the state constitution prohibited such action.


OUTCOME: The court granted a correctional facility authority's writ of mandamus as to a management board's refusal to comply with a legislative bill requiring investment in the authority's statewide construction and renovation project and found that the bill did not substantially impair the contract rights between the pension members and the state.

Pendleton Citizens for Community Schs. v. Marockie


No. 25138, No. 25139


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


203 W. Va. 310; 507 S.E.2d 673; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 132


June 9, 1998, Submitted  
July 14, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Hon. Tod J. Kaufman, Judge. Civil Action No. 96-C-507.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, West Virginia Superintendent of Schools, West Virginia Board of Education (state board), West Virginia School Building Authority (SBA), a director, and a county board of education, sought review of an order by the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which ruled that the closing of a high school violated both statutory law and the state constitutional right to education in West Virginia.


OVERVIEW: Appellants contended that even if the SBA and the state board policies did drive consolidation, any such bias toward consolidation was not contrary to any statute nor a violation of the constitutional right to education for appellees, students, parents, and an organization. The court stated that W. Va. Code § 18-9D-16 (1993) did not prohibit the SBA from exercising discretion in weighing and applying the factors listed in § 18-9D-16, in order to prioritize requests for funding. Thus, appellees' statutorily-based attack on the SBA's weighing of the "economies of scale" factor must have failed. The court did not concur with the trial court's conclusion that the SBA and the state board's approach to funding school construction and salaries, and the allegedly resulting closing of the high school, was not a narrowly tailored, least restrictive method necessary to advance a compelling state interest. The court held that the trial court erred in issuing the declaratory judgment and injunction order appealed from in the case. Hence, the court reversed the order ruling that the closing of the high school violated both statutory law and the state constitutional right to education.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order holding that the closing of the high school violated both statutory law and the state constitutional right to education in West Virginia.

State ex rel. Farley v. Spaulding


No. 24965


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


203 W. Va. 275; 507 S.E.2d 376; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 123


April 28, 1998, Submitted  
July 14, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Concurring Opinion by Justice Workman Filed July 20, 1998. Justice Starcher's Concurring Opinion Filed November 9, 1998. Dissenting Opinion by Chief Justice Davis filed July 22, 1998.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED, IN PART, AND DENIED, IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sheriff sought a writ of prohibition to prevent respondent circuit court judge from enforcing two administrative orders designating individuals hired by respondent county commission as civilian court marshals. The sheriff alleged that the administrative orders were unconstitutional and an impermissible usurpation of his statutory power under W. Va. Code § 51-3-5 (1923).


OVERVIEW: The court granted the writ of prohibition in part and denied it in part. In so holding, the court concluded: (1) the county commission's hiring of court security personnel was within its constitutional power to superintend and administer the internal police and fiscal affairs of the county under W. Va. Const. art. IX, § 11 and the commission had the implied authority to employ them under W. Va. Code §§ 7-1-3m, 7-3-2 (1989); (2) the county commission's employment of these personnel did not impair or supplant the power and duty of the county sheriff under W. Va. Code § 51-3-5 (1923) and W. Va. Trial Ct. R. VII (1960); and (3) although the circuit court judge had the inherent power to provide adequate court security, which was essential to the safe and orderly administration of justice, he improperly usurped the power and responsibility of the sheriff to furnish deputy sheriffs to serve as court bailiffs for the county's courts under W. Va. Code § 51-3-5 (1923) and W. Va. Trial Ct. R. VII. Under the separation of powers doctrine, this usurpatory portion of the judge's order were not permitted to stand.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of prohibition in part, prohibiting the enforcement of the grants of authority to court marshals to perform the courtroom services of bailiff and to escort prisoners to and from court proceedings. The court denied the writ of prohibition as to the remainder of the circuit court judge's order.

 

32 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Stuckey v. Trent


No. 24528


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


202 W. Va. 498; 505 S.E.2d 417; 1998 W. Va. LEXIS 80


June 2, 1998, Submitted  
July 2, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. Honorable Fred L. Fox, II, Judge. Civil Action No. 94-P-95.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant felon sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Marion County (West Virginia), which denied his petition against respondent warden for habeas corpus relief, claiming that the state's failure to elect to try him on either a premeditated murder theory or a felony-murder theory rendered the trial unfair and violated his due process rights under U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV and W.Va. Const. art. III, § 10.


OVERVIEW: The felon was tried for premeditated murder and felony-murder, but he was not charged with the arson. After conviction, he sought habeas corpus relief. The trial court denied his habeas petition and on appeal he again claimed that the state's failure to elect to try him on either a premeditated murder theory or a felony-murder theory rendered the trial unfair and violated his due process rights. The court affirmed the judgment below, ruling that the state was authorized to present its case on both theories. The two theories were distinguished for the jury in the trial court's charge. Further, because the felon's alibi defense was the same under both murder theories he was not prejudiced by the state's advancement of both theories. In the absence of an arson charge, the jury was not required to distinguish the state's theories of murder in the first degree in its verdict. The court held that premeditated murder and felony-murder were alternative means under W.Va. Code § 61-2-1 (1987) of committing murder in the first degree. The state's reliance on both theories at trial did not, per se, offend due process because they were distinguished for the jury in the instructions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the felon's petition for habeas corpus relief.

McCoy v. Vankirk


No. 24019


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


201 W. Va. 718; 500 S.E.2d 534; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 291


October 8, 1997, Submitted  
December 16, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Judge Paul Zakaib, Jr. Civil Action No. 96-C-419.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant abutting landowner sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which held that W.Va. Code § 17- 2A-19 (1994), which allowed appellee Commissioner of West Virginia Division of Highways to dispose of certain unneeded highways real estate, was unconstitutional and ordered the commissioner to convey property to appellee company that was the highest bidder on the property.


OVERVIEW: The landowner and the commissioner negotiated an agreed order that allowed the sale by public auction of land that abutted the landowner's property, subject to a right of first refusal in any abutting property owners. The commissioner then held a public auction and offered to sell the property to the landowner according to his right of first refusal; however, the commissioner determined the fair market value of the property to be the winning auction bid. The landowner exercised his right to purchase, but filed a motion for determination of fair market value with the circuit court. The company that had made the winning bid filed a motion to intervene. The circuit court ordered the commissioner to convey the property to the company. On appeal, the court reversed and held, inter alia, that: (1) the commissioner was required to offer the landowner, an abutting landowner, the right of first refusal to purchase the property at fair market value; (2) the preferences granted to abutting landowners under § 17-2A-19 were rationally related to legitimate state interests; and (3) § 17-2A-19 was constitutional under the equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's decision, which ordered the commissioner to convey the property to the company, and remanded the case for a determination of the fair market value of the property.

State v. Murrell


No. 23808


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


201 W. Va. 648; 499 S.E.2d 870; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 283


October 8, 1997, Submitted  
December 16, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Monroe County. Honorable Robert A. Irons, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-F-10.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, IN PART; REVERSED, IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Monroe County (West Virginia), which sentenced him to prison and imposed a fine of $ 20,000 on his plea of guilty to two counts of third degree sexual assault, on the grounds that the fines were excessive and that he had no ability to repay them.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion for a reduction of the fines was denied and the court granted leave to appeal both the imposition of costs and fines. On appeal, the court affirmed holding that pursuant to W. Va. Code § 29-21- 16(g)(3), orders requiring repayment of attorney fees were not enforceable during a period of incarceration, unless the court found, at the time of sentencing, that the person had sufficient assets to pay the amounts ordered or found sufficient likelihood that the person would acquire the necessary assets in the foreseeable future. Upon his release, defendant was entitled to a hearing on his ability to pay the assessed attorney fees, in accordance with W. Va. Code § 29-21-16(g). The court held that it was not a violation of defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. VIII or W. Va. Const. art. III, § 5 because those sections applied to instances where there were no maximum fines imposed or to where there was a life recidivist sentence. The court held that there was nothing to indicate that the fines were excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for third degree sexual assault and the fines imposed.

Hartwell v. Marquez


No. 24124


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


201 W. Va. 433; 498 S.E.2d 1; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 250


September 10, 1997, Submitted  
November 21, 1997, Filed As Modified


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] November 21, 1997, Rehearing Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Mercer County. Honorable David W. Knight, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-CV-64-K.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company sought review from a decision of the Circuit Court of Mercer County (West Virginia), which denied its W. Va. R. Civ. P. 60(b) motion to set aside a default judgment and a resulting monetary judgment entered against defendant below and in favor of plaintiff below. The underlying personal injury action arose from an automobile accident wherein plaintiff below was struck by a vehicle driven by defendant below.


OVERVIEW: The underlying personal injury action arose from an automobile accident wherein plaintiff below was struck by a vehicle driven by defendant below. The trial court denied appellant insurance company's motion to set aside a default judgment and a resulting monetary judgment entered against defendant below and in favor of plaintiff below. On appeal, the court held that the provisions of W. Va. Code § 56-3-31 (1990) permitting substituted service upon a nonresident motorist's insurer referred to an insurer providing coverage at the time of an accident alleged in a complaint. Further, the court stated that due process did not require that the method of service absolutely provide a defendant with notice. It was sufficient if it was reasonably calculated to provide such notice. The court held that the provisions of W. Va. Code § 56-3-31 (1990) that permitted substituted service of process on a nonresident motorist's liability insurer after all statutory conditions were met were constitutional and did not violate the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff below.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Robert K. McL.


No. 23951


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


201 W. Va. 317; 496 S.E.2d 887; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 220


September 17, 1997, Submitted  
October 24, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fayette County. Hon. John W. Hatcher, Jr., Judge. Case No. 96-JD-5.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Fayette County (West Virginia), which transferred the juvenile to the adult criminal jurisdiction of the court. The juvenile argued that the "automatic transfer" provisions of the juvenile transfer statute, W. Va. Code § 49-5-10(d) (1995), violated his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court ordered that the juvenile be transferred to the criminal jurisdiction of the circuit court to stand trial as an adult. On appeal, the juvenile contended that the "automatic transfer" provisions of W. Va. Code § 49-5-10(d) (1995) violated the guarantees of equal protection and due process contained in W. Va. Const. art. III, § 10 and the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution. The court considered whether the statute at issue, which divested and deprived a circuit court of the ability to consider personal and other factors going to the suitability and amenability of a juvenile, ran afoul of the constitutional guarantees of equal protection and due process. The court concluded that the "automatic transfer" provisions of the statute at issue, when read in pari materia with the provisions of W. Va. Code § 49-5-13 (1995), did not unconstitutionally divest and deprive a circuit court of the ability to consider personal factors going to the amenability of a juvenile for the rehabilitative purposes of the court's juvenile jurisdiction and to, in its discretion, return a child to juvenile jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court, which transferred the juvenile to the adult criminal jurisdiction of the court.

 

38 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Hartwell v. Marquez


No. 24124


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


1997 W. Va. LEXIS 211


September 10, 1997, Submitted  
October 3, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Mercer County. Honorable David W. Knight, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-CV-64-K.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Mercer County (West Virginia), which entered summary judgment against defendant below (defendant), a nonresident and the insurer's alleged insured, and in favor of plaintiff below (plaintiff).


OVERVIEW: The insurer failed to answer the complaint filed by plaintiff below. A default judgment was entered against the insurer and it filed a motion to set aside the default judgment, which was denied. The insurer argued that at the time that it received substituted service of process, it did not insure either defendant or the owner of the vehicle, which defendant was driving at the time of the accident. The court reviewed the record and determined that prior to the service of process, the insurer was the insurance carrier for the owner of the vehicle and that defendant was named as an insured under that policy. The court ruled that because the insurer had a contract of insurance that covered defendant at the time of the accident, the insurer had a duty to defend defendant with regard to the accident. As to the insurer's constitutional challenge to W. Va. Code § 56-3-31, the court ruled that the procedures for service upon a nonresident driver complied with the due process requirements of the Fourteenth Amendment. The procedures for notifying defendant by registered or certified mail were met before substituted service on the insurer was attempted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's grant of summary judgment in favor of plaintiff.

State ex rel. Hechler v. Christian Action Network


No. 23573


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


201 W. Va. 71; 491 S.E.2d 618; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 184


January 22, 1997, Submitted  
July 16, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Lyne Ranson, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-C-2089.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, IN PART, AND REVERSED, IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nonprofit corporation challenged the order of the Circuit Court, Kanawha County (West Virginia) enjoining it from soliciting funds until it complied with the Solicitation of Charitable Funds Act, W. Va. Code Ann. § 29-19-1 et seq., and sent a copy of public mailings to appellee Secretary of State. It alleged that it was not a "charitable organization" and that the statute violated U.S Const. amend. I and W. Va. Const. art. III, § 7.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Secretary of State filed a petition to enjoin appellant nonprofit corporation from soliciting funds until it complied with the Solicitation of Charitable Funds Act (Act), W. Va. Code Ann. § 29-19-1 et seq. The trial court granted the petition and appellant sought review, asserting that it was not a "charitable organization" under the Act and that the statute violated U.S. Const. amend. I and W. Va. Const. art. 10, § 7. The court affirmed, in part, ruling that appellant was a "charitable organization" as that term was defined in W. Va. Code Ann. § 29-19-2(1) (1992). Appellant's self-description in its articles of incorporation included it within the definition of "charitable organization" found in § 29-19-2(1) and thus, it was subject to the requirements of that Act. Appellant was required to print the mandated statement of § 29-19-8 on its written solicitations. The requirement that a charitable organization "conspicuously display" the mandated statement "on a prominent part of the solicitation materials" was not unconstitutionally vague. The court reversed, in part, holding that § 29-19-8 did not require appellant to provide appellee with a copy of its public mailings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, the order enjoining appellant nonprofit corporation from soliciting funds until it complied with a charitable funds act. Appellant was a "charitable organization" under the act and thus, was required print a mandated statement on all of its solicitation materials. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court reversed the order to send appellee Secretary of State a copy of solicitation materials.

Cottrill v. Ranson


No. 23374


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


200 W. Va. 691; 490 S.E.2d 778; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 168


January 28, 1997, Submitted  
July 15, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Putnam County. Honorable Clarence L. Watt, Circuit Judge. Civil Action No. 91-C-906.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant original owner challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Putnam County (West Virginia), which affirmed a prior summary judgment in favor of the sale and purchase of a piece of property between appellees, the Board of Education of Putnam County (board) and spouses.


OVERVIEW: The original owner contended that he should have been given the right to repurchase the former school property as an original grantor of the property to the board and as the heir of the other grantor, his brother. The court held that the spouses, who had owned the parent tracts for the past 30 years, were properly granted the sole right of repurchase the property because the spouses were the assignees of the parent tracts and neither the original owner nor his brother preserved their rights to repurchase the former school property in their respective assignments of those tracts. According to the court, the spouses were the "assigns" within the meaning and contract of W. Va. Code § 18-5-7 and were entitled to repurchase the former school property pursuant to that statute. The court held that the spouses were not unjustly by the order of the trial court. Rather, the court held that the spouses were the only ones who possessed the right to repurchase the former school property because the right to repurchase followed the land from which it was annexed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which affirmed a prior summary judgment in favor of the sale and purchase of a piece of property between the board and the spouses.
