State v. Wade


No. 23559


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


200 W. Va. 637; 490 S.E.2d 724; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 161


January 14, 1997, Submitted  
July 11, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied December 1, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7204.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ohio County. Honorable Martin J. Gaughan, Judge. Criminal Action No. 95-F-33.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Ohio County (West Virginia) that convicted him of first-degree felony-murder with mercy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree felony-murder with mercy. On appeal, he contended that the circuit court erred in refusing to instruct the jury regarding self-defense, provocation, and certain lesser-included offenses. In addition, he contended there was insufficient evidence upon which to convict him of felony-murder, and that the trial court erred in allowing the testimony of the victim's father, and in refusing to excuse, for cause, two jurors. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the trial court committed no prejudicial error. The self-defense and provocation instructions were not available in response to a charge of felony-murder because the predicate felony was the delivery of a controlled substance. The court held that, as a matter of law, second-degree murder, voluntary manslaughter, and involuntary manslaughter were not lesser included offenses of felony-murder, so the trial court did not err in refusing his proposed instructions. Moreover, the evidence supported the verdict, and although the victim's father's testimony was admitted in error, it was harmless. The court found no error in refusing to strike the challenged jurors for cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of first-degree felony-murder with mercy.

Atkinson v. County Comm'n


No. 23880


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


200 W. Va. 380; 489 S.E.2d 762; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 134


April 22, 1997, Submitted  
July 3, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wood County. Honorable George W. Hill, Circuit Judge. Civil Action No. 96-P-73.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former magistrate challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Wood County (West Virginia) that denied his petition for a writ of mandamus requiring respondent county commission to reimburse him under the Governmental Tort Claims and Insurance Reform Act (Tort Claims Act), W. Va. Code §§ 29-12A-1 to -18 (1992), for attorneys' fees incurred in defending against criminal charges brought against him while in office.


OVERVIEW: The magistrate's petition for a writ of mandamus requiring the commission to reimburse him for attorneys' fees incurred in defending against criminal charges brought against him while in office was denied. The court affirmed, finding that the magistrate was not a county employee and the Tort Claims Act did not apply where the defense costs were incurred in connection with criminal charges. The magistrate had none of the indicia of a county officer or employee where the state paid his salary, trained and supervised him, limited his jurisdiction, and set qualifications for his office. The inclusion of magistrates within W. Va. Code § 6-6-7 (1993), affecting removal of county officers, had no bearing on his employment status because it only gave the commission power to file a complaint, not to remove him from office. Although the magistrate was not entitled to reimbursement of attorneys' fees under the Tort Claims Act, he was free to pursue a common law indemnification claim against a state agency if the acts giving rise to the criminal charges were performed in good faith and within the scope of his official duties, and he avoided the constitutional bar against suing a state agency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying the magistrate's petition for a writ of mandamus requiring the commission to reimburse him under the Tort Claims Act for attorneys' fees incurred in defending against criminal charges brought against him while in office.

Cathe A. v. Doddridge County Bd. of Educ.


No. 23350


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


200 W. Va. 521; 490 S.E.2d 340; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 129


September 25, 1996, Submitted; February 25, 1997, Resubmitted  
July 3, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Concurring in part and Dissenting in part Opinion Filed July 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Doddridge County. Honorable Joseph Troisi, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-P-17.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Board of Education appealed a decision from Circuit Court of Doddridge County (West Virginia), which issued an order to compel it either to readmit plaintiff parents' student son to regular school classes or alternatively to provide him with other state-funded educational services after he had been expelled for possession of a knife on school property.


OVERVIEW: The board had ordered that student be expelled from school for a period of 12 months. At trial it stipulated that it was willing to provide a home instruction teacher for four hours per week, provided parents agreed to pay for the teacher's time. The court agreed to consider the questions raised because of their importance, even though the issues were technically moot. The court found that a child could be constitutionally removed from a classroom when he engaged in disruptive conduct. Under the "no weapon" policy, the school could remove student for a substantial period of time. The Productive and Safe School Act, W. Va. Code § 18A-5-1a(g) (1995), was facially constitutional because it was reasonably necessary and narrowly tailored method to provide a safe school environment. However, because the state was constitutionally required to provide a free public education, the board could not condition an instructional program upon parent's reimbursing the board for the cost of the program. On parents' cross appeal that they were wrongfully denied attorney fees, the court found the trial court had failed to consider where extraordinary circumstances existed to allow such fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which held that student could be removed from school for a period of up to 12 months and that parents could not be required to pay for an instructional program. It remanded the matter of attorney fees for further consideration.

State ex rel. Watson v. Hill


No. 23849


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


200 W. Va. 201; 488 S.E.2d 476; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 101


February 25, 1997, Submitted  
June 10, 1997, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed for a writ of mandamus and/or prohibition seeking to compel the judge of the Circuit Court of Wood County (West Virginia) to consider and decide petitioner's post-conviction habeas corpus petition on its merits.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner had been found guilty of malicious assault and, based on prior convictions, was sentenced to life in prison. Petitioner sought to compel the trial court to hear her post-conviction habeas corpus petition on its merits. The court agreed that he was entitled to a hearing on the merits of his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. W. Va. Code § 53-4A-7(c) (1994) required the trial court denying or granting relief in a habeas corpus proceeding to make specific findings of fact and conclusions of law relating to each contention advanced by petitioner, and to state the grounds upon which the matter was determined. Here the judge simply noted that the allegations were entirely without merit and that good cause for the filing and appointment of counsel was not shown. The court agreed that this order was insufficient. The court directed the trial court to hold a habeas corpus hearing on the merits of petitioner's ineffective assistance claim and to issue an order that included findings of fact and conclusions of law as required by § 53-4A-7(c).


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner's writ of mandamus and directed the trial court to hold a habeas corpus hearing on the merits of the ineffective assistance claim and to issue an order that included findings of fact and conclusions of law relating to each contention.

State ex rel. Ring v. Boober


No. 23676


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


200 W. Va. 66; 488 S.E.2d 66; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 85


May 6, 1997, Submitted  
May 30, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. Honorable David H. Sanders, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-P-164.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Jefferson Count (West Virginia), which denied his petition for a writ of prohibition to preclude respondent magistrate from denying his demand for a jury trial because the demand was not timely according to W.Va. Code § 50-5-8(b) (1994) and Rule 5(c) of the West Virginia Rules of Criminal Procedure for Magistrate Courts.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's petition to prohibit the magistrates from denying him a jury trial. The trial court found that W.Va. Code § 50-5-8(b) was constitutional, and that the defendant's constitutional right to a jury trial was knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently waived pursuant to Rule 5(c) of the West Virginia Rules of Criminal Procedure for Magistrate Courts. On review, the court agreed. The signed rights statement and defendant's subsequent failure to demand a jury trial within the prescribed time period constituted an intentional, knowing, and voluntary waiver. The statement clearly informed defendant of his right to demand a jury trial, the necessity of demanding a jury trial no later than 20 days from the date of this initial appearance or the appointment of counsel, and the consequences of failing to demand a jury trial within this time period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the writ of prohibition and held that defendant's right to a jury trial was knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently waived.

State ex rel. W. Va. Fire & Cas. Co. v. Karl


No. 23944, 23986


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


199 W. Va. 678; 487 S.E.2d 336; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 71


March 25, 1997, Submitted  
May 29, 1997, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, insurance companies for insureds, who had injured a child, paid money to the child's parents and obtained the parents' signatures on settlement releases without obtaining court approval. The insurance companies sought writs of prohibition from the state supreme court concerning the conclusion by the Circuit Court of Marshall County (West Virginia) that W. Va. Code § 44-10-14 (1929) required court approval of all such settlements.


OVERVIEW: In two consolidated lawsuits, the complaints alleged violations of W. Va. Code § 33-11-4(9) (1985), the unfair claims settlement practices, the tort of outrage, and fraud. The parents and infant contended that the insurance companies paid money to and obtained settlement releases from them, where there was no litigation pending, to settle tort claims against the insurance companies' insureds in "infant settlements," in a fashion that was wrongful, illegal, and actionable. The circuit court stated that W. Va. Code § 44-10-14 (1929) required an infant settlement proceeding where a minor was injured in his person or property. The issue was whether § 44-10-14 required court approval of all infant settlements. The court held that the statutory language plainly contemplated that both parties to an infant settlement, the guardian and the tort-feasor, could elect not to proceed under the provisions of the statutory section in question. Section 44-10-14 did not require court approval of all claims where a guardian executed a settlement agreement on behalf of a minor who had been injured in his or her person or property.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of prohibition as molded.

The court held that the issue as to waiver of counsel was exclusively for the courts of the demanding state, South Carolina, to determine in the first instance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the habeas corpus relief granted to the convict and remanded with directions that the circuit court allow the extradition of the convict to proceed.

Shannondale, Inc. v. Jefferson County Planning & Zoning Comm'n


No. 23453


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


199 W. Va. 494; 485 S.E.2d 438; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 52


February 4, 1997, Submitted  
April 11, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Christopher C. Wilkes, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-P-2.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, IN PART, REVERSED, IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Jefferson County Planning and Zoning Commission's found that the subdivision standards of Jefferson County, W. Va., Subdivision Ordinance § 4.8.a applied to an access road and denied appellant developer a variance. The developer challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (West Virginia), which affirmed the Commission's decisions and found that the Ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The developer sought to construct single family residences. The Ordinance provided that a road accessing subdivision had to meet the standards required for rights-of-way and roads and required a developer who used an existing access road to upgrade it to the Ordinance's asphalt standards. The developer sought a variance and offered to upgrade the access road, but not to the subdivision standards. The Commission denied the variance. The court held that the Commission did not err in interpreting the Ordinance, but it did err in failing to set forth the factual basis for its denial of the variance. The circuit court correctly concluded that Jefferson County, W. Va., Subdivision Ordinance §§ 4.8 and 8.2 were applicable to the proposed subdivision roads and to the access road. All sections of the Ordinance had to be applied to the access road. The Ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague because it provided a reasonable notice of the important issues to those seeking a variance. The Commission's minutes did not reflect the reasons why it denied the variance. Findings of fact were necessary for a proper review by both the court and the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order upholding the Commission's decision that the subdivision standards of the Ordinance applied to the access road and finding that the Ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague. The court reversed the order affirming the Commission's decision to deny the developer a variance and remanded the case to the Commission to conduct a reconsideration or a hearing and make specific findings of fact and conclusions of law.

State v. Phillips


No. 23535


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


199 W. Va. 507; 485 S.E.2d 676; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 51


January 15, 1997, Submitted  
April 10, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wood County. Honorable George W. Hill, Judge. Criminal Action No. 94-F-34.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by a jury in the Circuit Court of Wood County (West Virginia) for two counts of aggravated robbery and one count of kidnapping. He argued that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on the lesser included offense of nonaggravated robbery, and that the 140-year sentence he received was excessive.


OVERVIEW: The evidence at trial showed that defendant entered two restaurants, pointed a gun at the employees, and told them that he would kill them if they did not cooperate in giving him money. He kidnapped one of the employees while leaving the restaurant, and after being spotted by the police, drove in excess of 125 miles per hour with the employee in the car. Defendant argued that because he used an air pistol to commit the robberies, he was entitled to an instruction on the lesser included offense of nonaggravated robbery. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence. The court held that the only element that differed from aggravated robbery was the violence or threat of violence to the victims. The court ruled that because the presence of a firearm was not required for a conviction of aggravated robbery, and the evidence showed that defendant threatened the victims with a weapon, which they believed was real, defendant was not entitled to an instruction on nonaggravated robbery. The court further determined that defendant's sentence was constitutionally proportionate to the character and degree of the offenses of which he was convicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for two counts of armed robbery and one count of kidnapping. The court also affirmed defendant's sentence.

West Virginia Trust Fund v. Bailey


No. 23939


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


199 W. Va. 463; 485 S.E.2d 407; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 46


February 25, 1997, Submitted  
March 28, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Lyne Ranson, Judge. Civil Action Nos. 96-Misc-221, 96-Misc-225, 96-C-1347, and 96-C-1405.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee pension fund appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which ruled that W. Va. Code § 12-6-9(j), which created petitioner, was unconstitutional under W. Va. Const. art. X, § 6, and which issued a writ of quo warranto dissolving petitioner as an illegal corporation.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee pension fund (the fund) was created under W. Va. Code § 12-6-9(j). Four suits, which claimed that the fund violated the state constitution, were consolidated. After the circuit court ruled that the enabling act was unconstitutional under W. Va. Const. art. X, § 6, which prohibited the state from becoming an owner or stockholder in a company or association, and issued a writ of quo warranto dissolving the fund as an illegal corporation, the fund appealed. The court affirmed the finding that the West Virginia Trust Fund Act, W. Va. Code §§ 44-6B-1 to -12 (1996), was unconstitutional. The fund was to a significant degree a state actor and instrumentality of the state. The fund allowed the state to invest employee pension, the workers' compensation, and coal workers' pneumoconiosis funds to become a joint owner or stockholder in companies and associations. The court reversed in part. The court disagreed with the finding that the act interfered with the duties of the state treasurer. The fund's purpose was to benefit the public fisc by reducing the need for legislative appropriations to fund pension plans.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the act was unconstitutional because petitioner was a state actor and instrumentality of the state so that petitioner violated the unconditional constitutional proscription against the state becoming a joint owner or stockholder in any corporation or association.

 

52 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Bush v. Richardson


No. 23702


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


199 W. Va. 374; 484 S.E.2d 490; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 43


January 15, 1997, Submitted  
March 21, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wood County. Honorable Jeffrey B. Reed, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-C-222.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Wood County (West Virginia), which held in a declaratory judgment action that the employee need not be fully compensated for her injuries by the moneys received from a third-party tortfeasor before the appellee workers' compensation commissioner (commissioner) could enforce a statutory subrogation lien.


OVERVIEW: An employee was involved in a car accident while within the scope of her employment. She filed a workers' compensation claim as well as a personal injury claim against the tortfeasor. The commissioner notified the employee of a statutory lien against any moneys recovered from the tortfeasor or his insurance company under W. Va. Code § 23-2A-1 (1990). The employee filed a declaratory judgment action in which she maintained that the commissioner was not entitled to recover any money because the maximum amount of money that she could recover would not fully compensate her for her personal injury claim. The trial court concluded that the commissioner was entitled to subrogation. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision because the made-whole rule was inapplicable to the commissioner's claim. The court held that the legislature expressly modified the usual, ordinary meaning of subrogation as it was used in § 23-2A-1 by mandating that the commissioner in a subrogation claim was be limited to recovering only the medical benefits paid as of the date of recovery, and could not collect more than fifty percent of the amount received from the third party as a result of the employee's claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment declaring that the made-whole rule did not apply to the commissioner's subrogation claim against the employee.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Logan County (West Virginia), which convicted her of first-degree murder and shooting at a person in a public street, which involved the shooting death of defendant's estranged boyfriend.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first-degree murder and shooting at a person in a public street, which involved the shooting death of her alleged boyfriend who had severed their relationship. State ex rel. West Virginia Div. of Natural Resources v. Cline


No. 23840


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


200 W. Va. 101; 488 S.E.2d 376; 1997 W. Va. LEXIS 2


January 14, 1997, Submitted  
February 20, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended March 17, 1997.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state filed a writ requesting vacation of an order of the Circuit Court of Braxton County (West Virginia), which ruled that W. Va. Code § 20-2-5(10), prohibiting the carrying of loaded firearms in or on any vehicle, was an unreasonable restriction of the rights contained in W. Va. Const., art. III, § 22. The state further requested the prohibition of respondent officials from refusing to enforce violations of W. Va. Code § 20-2-5(10).


OVERVIEW: The court granted the writ. W. Va. Const., art. III, § 22 permitted a person to keep and bear arms for lawful hunting and recreational use. The court found that applying § 22 to W. Va. Code § 20-2-5(10) demonstrated that there was no conflict between the two provisions because transportation of a loaded firearm was not a lawful method of hunting with firearms. The court determined that, as an unlawful manner of hunting, the transportation of a loaded firearm was not subject to constitutional protection. The court also found that a review of § 20-2-5(10) indicated that it was a reasonable and narrow restriction of a person's right to bear arms. The court determined that the state had a legitimate police power interest in protecting its citizens from the dangers of transporting loaded firearms. The court concluded that the restriction was reasonable because it did not infringe upon a sportsperson's right to keep and bear arms for hunting purposes, but rather, it merely regulated the manner in which such weapons could be transported.


OUTCOME: The writ for vacation of the order ruling that the statutory provision was an unreasonable restriction of a constitutional right was granted.

State v. Rahman


No. 23329


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


199 W. Va. 144; 483 S.E.2d 273; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 258


September 24, 1996, Submitted  
December 20, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Lyne Ranson, Circuit Judge. Criminal Action No. 95-F-159.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which convicted him of four felony counts of possession of heroin with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment and held: (1) the trial court did not err by denying a motion to exclude heroin found inside defendant's pocket because the police had probable cause to make an arrest without a warrant and had the authority to make a full search incident to his arrest; (2) the trial court was not required to declare a mistrial after the prosecutor asked defendant during cross-examination whether he had ever sold heroin before, which was not permissible under W. Va. R. Evid. 404(b), as the error was harmless because the question did not have a prejudicial effect on the jury; (3) separation of the charges into four counts did not violate the Double Jeopardy Clause of the United States Constitution or the West Virginia Constitution because each count required proof of separate facts; (4) defense counsel was not permitted to impeach a co-defendant with a prior misdemeanor conviction for shoplifting because the conviction did not involve dishonesty or a false statement, and (5) the case was remanded because the state failed to explain why it did not challenge a similarly situated juror in the face of defendant's Batson challenge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, but remanded the case for a hearing on the validity of the peremptory strike.

State v. Smith


No. 23312


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


198 W. Va. 702; 482 S.E.2d 687; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 262


September 24, 1996, Submitted  
December 19, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Monroe County. Honorable Robert A. Irons, Circuit Judge. Criminal Action No. 94-F-31.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Monroe County (West Virginia), which found defendant not guilty of second-degree murder by reason of mental illness after continuing defendant's charges until an amended version of W.Va. Code §§ 27-6A-3 and 27-6A-4 (1992 & Supp. 1996) took effect. The trial court applied the amendments to §§ 27-6A-3 and 27-6A-4 in ordering defendant's hospitalization.


OVERVIEW: For several years before defendant shot and killed her husband, she suffered from varying degrees of mental illness. Following her arrest, the trial court ordered her to undergo hospitalization. After six months of evaluation, defendant was found to suffer from bipolar affective disorder with psychotic features and was found competent to stand trial. However, the evaluation showed that she did not form the criminal intent necessary for a conviction at the time of the murder. At a hearing, defendant was found guilty by reason of insanity and hospitalized. Considering defendant's mental state, the court held that §§ 27-6A-3 and 27-6A-4 provided the trial court with flexibility in exercising and retaining its jurisdiction up to the maximum sentence period. The court further held that the trial court's implementation of the amended version of § 27-6A-3 did not violate ex post facto principles.

State ex rel. School Bldg. Auth. v. Marockie


No. 23675


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


198 W. Va. 424; 481 S.E.2d 730; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 229


November 19, 1996, Submitted  
December 13, 1996, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ Granted as Moulded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator School Building Authority of West Virginia (SBA) sought a writ of mandamus compelling respondent SBA president to issue refunding bonds to discharge previously issued bonds in order to generate cash for new school improvement projects.


OVERVIEW: In order to generate cash for new school improvement projects, the SBA sought to issue refunding bonds for a principal amount greater than bonds previously issued and use the cash generated for the projects. The SBA president objected and the SBA filed a writ of mandamus with the court. The court granted the writ, but restricted its scope. The court held that the SBA was permitted to issue revenue bonds in a principal amount greater than the principal amount of the bonds to be refunded in order to establish an escrow account for the repayment of those preexisting obligations that were not presently due and payable. But the court held that the SBA was permitted to issue refunding bonds only in that additional amount required to establish and maintain the escrow account. The court further held that the SBA was not permitted to issue bonds alleged to be refunding bonds for the redemption of the previous obligations, which had the practical effect of generating cash at closing in order to make immediately available to the SBA the anticipated debt service savings from the so-called refunding bonds.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus, but only to the extent that the SBA could establish an escrow account for the repayment of the preexisting bond obligations.

Phillip Leon M. v. Greenbrier County Bd. of Educ.


No. 23349


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


199 W. Va. 400; 484 S.E.2d 909; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 226


September 25, 1996, Submitted  
December 13, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Greenbrier County. Honorable George M. Scott, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-C-75.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of education challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Greenbrier County (West Virginia), which required it to provide some form of alternative education to appellee student who had been expelled after bringing a firearm to school.


OVERVIEW: Appellee student was expelled for two semesters from a junior high school after he was found on school property with a firearm. Subsequently, appellee petitioned for a writ of mandamus seeking some form of education from appellant board of education. The trial court granted the writ, holding that while appellee forfeited his right to attend the junior high school by bringing a firearm to school, he had not forfeited his right to an education. On appeal, the court affirmed. Because education was a fundamental, constitutional right in West Virginia, appellant had to demonstrate a compelling state interest to justify its refusal to provide alternative education to appellee. The court held that the lack of financial resources, standing alone, was not a compelling state interest to justify appellant's denial of appellee's constitutional right to an education. Because appellant knowingly and deliberately refused to provide appellee an alternative education as required by the constitution, the trial court properly awarded appellee attorney fees and costs.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because appellant board of education failed to present a compelling state interest justifying its refusal to provide appellee student with an alternative education following his expulsion.

State ex rel. Charleston Bldg. Comm'n v. Dial


No. 23582


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


198 W. Va. 185; 479 S.E.2d 695; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 203


October 1, 1996, Submitted  
December 11, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified December 11, 1996.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator building commission petitioned for a writ of mandamus to challenge its authority to acquire property, issue bonds to finance the acquisition, and lease the acquired property to the state pursuant to a lease-purchase agreement. Respondent chairman pro tem of the commission (chairman) argued that he had no authority to execute a financial agreement for the project.


OVERVIEW: The building commission purchased and renovated a building for the state to use as an office building. The state entered into a lease-purchase agreement with the building commission. Following objections from the chairman, the building commission contended that its actions neither exceeded the statutory authority of a municipal building commission grant in W. Va. Code § 8-33-1 et seq. (1975), nor violated the W. Va. Const. art. X, §§ 4, 6, 8. The court first held that mandamus was the appropriate remedy because the building commission demonstrated a clear legal right to relief and because there was no other adequate remedy. The building commission had authority under W. Va. Code § 8-33-4 (1984) to appoint the chairman and to do all things reasonable and necessary to construct or acquire the municipal building. The court also held that the lease-purchase agreement was a proper method of conducting the project and that the issuance of revenue bonds was constitutional under the W. Va. Const. art. X. Under W. Va. Code § 8-16-7(d) (1981), a municipality could issue municipal revenue bonds necessary to pay the cost of a municipal public works.


OUTCOME: The court granted the building commission's writ of mandamus and held that the building commission had the authority to acquire, renovate, and lease, pursuant to a lease-purchase agreement, property to the state to be used solely for municipal purposes.

Wheeling Park Comm'n v. Hotel & Restaurant Emples., Int'l Union


No. 23448


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


198 W. Va. 215; 479 S.E.2d 876; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 180


September 11, 1996, Submitted  
November 18, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ohio County. Honorable W. Craig Broadwater, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-C-455 Br.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant union sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Ohio County (West Virginia) that granted a preliminary injunction restricting its organizing activities after plaintiff park commission brought an action seeking to prohibit the union's activities at one of its recreation complexes.


OVERVIEW: The union argued that the preliminary injunction violated its right to free speech found in the First Amendment of the United States Constitution and W. Va. Const. art. III, § 7. The court reversed the preliminary injunction concluding that the lower court did not apply the appropriate legal principles when granting it. The court held that when evaluating whether an injunction's content-neutral restrictions on speech in a public forum was constitutional, the reviewing court had to ensure that the content-neutral restrictions in the injunction burden no more speech than necessary to serve a significant government interest. The court explained that injunctions carried greater risks of censorship and discriminatory application than ordinances. Further, the court noted that an injunction represented a remedy imposed for a violation while an ordinance represented a legislative choice. For these reasons, the court concluded that the standard time, place, and manner analysis used to determine the constitutionality of an ordinance was not sufficiently rigorous for examining the constitutionality of an injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the preliminary injunction and remanded the case.

Hardy v. Richardson


No. 23388


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


198 W. Va. 11; 479 S.E.2d 310; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 182


September 24, 1996, Submitted  
November 15, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Robert K. Smith, Judge. Civil Action No. 93-C-5679.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which denied his prayer for a declaratory judgment that the provisions of W.Va. Code § 23-4-22 (1993) were unconstitutional and which refused to require appellee Commissioner of the Division of Workers' Compensation, Bureau of Employment Programs (commissioner) to evaluate claimant's entitlement to permanent partial disability.


OVERVIEW: The claimant suffered a leg injury and filed a worker's compensation claim. The injury was ruled compensable on a no lost time basis. No permanent partial evaluation was made and the commissioner did not file an order closing the claim. The state legislature subsequently passed § 23-4-22. The day before its effective date, the claimant's counsel requested permanent partial disability evaluations for all claims being handled by counsel's law firm which could have been affected by the bill. The request was denied. The commissioner later denied a specific request for an evaluation of the claimant. The claimant filed a declaratory judgment action. The circuit court denied relief. The court reversed and remanded. The court found that § 23-4-22 was inapplicable to the claimant's situation because the statute, on its face, applied only to cases closed on a no lost time basis. The court determined that the commissioner acted only through his orders, and as no order closing the case had been issued, the claimant's case was still open. The court concluded that the claimant's request for a permanent disability evaluation was effective on the date his counsel made a request for his evaluation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded with directions that the circuit court enter an order consistent with the court's opinion with respect to the claimant's rights under W.Va. Code § 23-4-22 (1993) relative to his request for a permanent disability evaluation.

Hutchison v. City of Huntington


No. 23332


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


198 W. Va. 139; 479 S.E.2d 649; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 190



November 15, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF CABELL COUNTY. HONORABLE ALFRED E. FERGUSON, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 94-C-238.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipality sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cabell County (West Virginia), which entered an award of damages to plaintiff property owner due to defendant's delay in giving plaintiff a requested building permit. Defendant contended that it was error to deny its motion to dismiss the state claim, that the evidence was insufficient, and that his due process rights were violated.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owner filed an action against defendant municipality, alleging that a delay by defendant in issuing a requested building permit caused damages, including additional costs for having to build during the winter. The trial court entered judgment for plaintiff based upon a jury verdict, and defendant sought review. The court reversed, holding that liability under state law claims was barred by the West Virginia Immunity Statute, W. Va. Code § 29-12A-5(a), because absolute immunity applied. The court held that defendant could be held liable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 as an entity when the plaintiff's injury resulted from a municipal policy or custom, and it found that actions of the planning supervisor and planning commission constituted official policy of defendant. However, the court held that plaintiff had received a process which was due, pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and that the four-month delay did not violate his due process rights, in that he did not show that the procedures were unfair or otherwise deficient. Accordingly, the court dismissed the action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of plaintiff property owner and dismissed the action against defendant municipality, which sought to impose liability on defendant for damages caused by a delay in issuing a building permit. The court held that absolute immunity shielded defendant from state law claims, and that there was no actionable violation of plaintiff's Fourteenth Amendment due process rights.

State v. One 1994 Dodge Truck Auto.


No. 23376


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 665; 478 S.E.2d 118; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 162


September 18, 1996, Submitted

OVERVIEW: The owner was indicted for two counts of delivery of a controlled substance within 1,000 feet of a school and one count of delivery of a controlled substance. At the time the indictment was returned, the state filed a petition for forfeiture of the owner's truck pursuant to the provisions of W.Va. 65 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Phelps


No. 23254


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 713; 478 S.E.2d 563; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 155


September 18, 1996, Submitted  
October 11, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF FAYETTE COUNTY. HONORABLE JOHN W. HATCHER, JR., JUDGE. NO. 93-F-83.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Fayette County (West Virginia), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment without possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of first-degree murder, and he was sentenced to life imprisonment without possibility of parole. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The trial court balanced the propriety of allowing testimony of outstanding charges against defendant, as opposed to merely allowing testimony that defendant was actively being sought by authorities for other felony charges, and it concluded that the former was too prejudicial but that the probative value of the latter was not outweighed by its prejudicial effect. It was not an abuse of discretion for the trial court to reject defendant's instruction because the matter was covered in the trial court's charge. The testimony of police concerning their conversations with others was not hearsay because it was not presented to prove the truth of the matter asserted. Assuming the officers' testimony was not relevant, the error was harmless. Other evidence that was objected to by defendant was relevant, and the probative value of the evidence outweighed any prejudice that could have been associated with the introduction of the evidence. The trial court's decision to deny bifurcation was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State ex rel. Browne v. Hechler


No. 23637


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 612; 476 S.E.2d 559; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 149


August 13, 1996, Submitted  
August 22, 1996, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ Granted


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a political party and two political candidates, sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent, the Secretary of State for West Virginia, to accept the candidates' certificates and filing fees to place the candidates on a general election ballot as third-party presidential and vice-presidential candidates.


OVERVIEW: The political party filed a petition of its intention to place the candidates on the general election ballot, submitted over 20,000 signatures endorsing the petition, and filed the filing fee. The Secretary refused the application because he claimed that the July 2 deadline as calculated under W. Va. Code § 3-5-23(a) (1986) had expired. The Secretary argued that the declarations of candidacy and the fees were due at least 30 days prior to the filing of the certificate provided by W. Va. In granting the writ of mandamus, the court noted that § 3-5-7(f) applied only to primary elections and not general elections. Further, the proviso in W. Va. Code § 3-5-23(a) (1986) provided that the deadline for filing the certificate and fees for seeking ballot access as candidates for president or vice president could be filed no later than the first day of August preceding the general election. The language of the proviso was clear and unambiguous, and petitioners timely submitted their certificate and filing fees.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ.

State v. McKenzie


No. 22976


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 429; 475 S.E.2d 521; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 147


January 16, 1996, Submitted  
July 18, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied December 2, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 7304.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wood County. Honorable Jeffrey Reed, Judge. Criminal Action No. 93-F-128.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Wood County (West Virginia) convicted defendant of second degree murder and sentenced him to from five to eighteen years in prison. Defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court committed reversible error by failing to suppress and exclude his confession. The court found that defendant's attempt to invoke his Miranda right to counsel, if invoked at all, was ineffective because it was invoked weeks before his subsequent contact with police. The trial court properly concluded that defendant's friend was not an agent of the state; therefore his right to counsel was not violated by his friends questioning of him. The court also concluded that the trial court properly admitted the murder weapon into evidence. The trial court's record indicated no negligence or bad faith on the part of the state in the preservation of evidence. The court also found no error in the trial court's jury instructions. Furthermore, the court found no reversible error in defendant's remaining arguments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

68 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Blankenship v. Richardson


No. 23119


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 726; 474 S.E.2d 906; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 117


March 5, 1996, Submitted  
July 17, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of Mandamus.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner workers' compensation claimants filed a writ of mandamus invoking the court's original jurisdiction pursuant to W. Va. Const. art. VIII, § 3 and W. Va. Code § 51-1-3 (1923). Claimants sought a writ of mandamus against respondent, Commissioner of the Division of Workers' Compensation, Bureau of Employment Programs, challenging the constitutionality of certain provisions of Senate Bill 250, which amended the Workers' Compensation Act.


OVERVIEW: Workers' compensation claimants filed a writ of mandamus against the Commissioner of the Division of Workers' Compensation, Bureau of Employment Programs, challenging the constitutionality of certain provisions of Senate Bill 250, which amended the West Virginia Workers' Compensation Act. The court determined that only one claimant was sufficiently affected by one of the provisions of Senate Bill 250. That claimant had filed a petition to reopen his work-related injury for consideration for permanent total disability three days after the effective date of Senate Bill 250, and his request was denied on the ground that he did not meet the requirements of W. Va. Code § 23-4-6(n)(1) (1995) in that he had received a total 32 percent whole man impairment. The court determined that the denial of claimant's request to reopen his claim because he did not suffer a medical impairment of 50 percent was not unconstitutional as a denial of equal protection under W. Va. Const. art. III, § 10. The court, however, concluded the statute, as applied to the claimant, violated principles of fundamental fairness embodied in the due process provisions of W. Va. Const. art. III, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus only as to one of the claimants who was sufficiently affected by one of the provisions of Senate Bill 250. The court concluded that the requirement in the statute that a claimant was not eligible for permanent total disability benefits unless he had been awarded 50 percent permanent partial disability did not violate equal protection because there was a rational basis for the requirement.

 

69 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. County Comm'n v. Cooke


No. 23375


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 391; 475 S.E.2d 483; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 115


May 28, 1996, Submitted  
July 17, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Mandamus.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner commission sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent clerk to publish notice of a public hearing under the Tax Increment Financing Act (Act), W. Va. Code § 7-11B-1 et seq. (1995), regarding the issuance of bonds to finance a water project.


OVERVIEW: Claiming that the Act was unconstitutional, the clerk refused to publish a notice of a public hearing under the Act for the issuance of the bonds to finance a county water project. The commission sought a writ of mandamus to compel the clerk to publish a notice of a hearing. The court denied the writ. When the bonds were issued under the Act, a debt was created. Such a debt could only have been issued under W. Va. Const. art. X, § 8, which stated that a county, city, or municipal corporation could not incur a debt unless it provided for the collection of a direct annual tax on all taxable property therein. If a county increased its current debt or created a new debt, it had to adjust its taxes to pay the debt. The Act provided that the increased ad valorem taxes generated as a result of the development project would pay the bonds. The Act used tax revenues derived from existing regular levies, making the Act unconstitutional. The bonds issued under the Act violated W. Va. Const. art. X, § 8. Thus, the county commission did not have a legal right to continue the process to fund the water project.


OUTCOME: The court denied the commission's petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the clerk to publish notice of a public hearing for the issuance of the bonds.

 

70 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. White v. Todt


No. 23271


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 334; 475 S.E.2d 426; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 84


May 2, 1996, Submitted  
July 8, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lewis County. Honorable Thomas H. Keadle, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-C-62.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mental patient sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Lewis County (West Virginia), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The circuit court ordered that the patient continue to be detained in a West Virginia state mental hospital until the demanding agent from Nebraska appeared to take custody of the patient pursuant to the Interstate Compact on Mental Health (Compact), W. Va. Code § 27-14-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The patient left a Nebraska psychiatric facility without permission while under involuntary civil commitment. In response to information provided by Nebraska officials, appellee Interstate Compact Administrator (administrator) issued an order authorizing the police to apprehend the patient and to take him to the West Virginia state mental hospital. In his petition, the patient challenged the procedure used to return an escaped dangerous or potentially dangerous patient, which was set forth in the Compact. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that the patient was not denied procedural due process. The court found that the patient was informed of the reason he was being detained, was afforded a hearing to determine identification, and was afforded the opportunity to have the representation of counsel at the hearing. The court rejected the patient's contention that due process required that a mental hygiene commissioner, magistrate, or judge issue the order to detain a mental patient, rather than the administrator. The court also held that the Compact was not unconstitutionally vague and was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative powers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that denied the mental patient's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

71 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Stone v. United Eng'g


No. 23101


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 347; 475 S.E.2d 439; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 86


April 24, 1996, Submitted  
July 8, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Tod J. Kaufman, Judge. Civil Action No. 93-C-490.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, IN PART; REVERSED, IN PART, AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed an action against defendant employer and equipment designer (designer) for injuries sustained by the employee during his employment. The jury returned a verdict in favor of the employee, and the designer filed a motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or, in the alternative, a new trial. The Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) denied the designer's motion, and the designer challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The designer owned the aluminum fabrication facility and designed the facility's hotline. Two years before the employee's accident the designer sold the facility to the employer. The designer alleged that the employee's claim of negligent design was barred under W. Va. Code § 55-2-6a (1983), the statute of repose. The court disagreed and held that § 55-2-6a was not intended to extend repose to a defendant such as the designer, which not only designed, but also owned, the equipment. The court determined that the statutory language contemplated that someone other than the owner of the real property had performed the enumerated activities or services and, therefore, would have had the benefit of repose. The court also held that the hotline equipment in question was real property. Finally, the court held that the measure of damages for the employee's past wages was adequately supported, but the testimony regarding the damages for future lost wages was highly speculative and could not have been sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment except as to the amount of damages. The court reversed the portion of the judgment with respect to the damages awarded for future lost wages and remanded the matter back to the trial court to enter a remittitur order.

State ex rel. Chadwell v. Duncil


No. 23280


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 643; 474 S.E.2d 573; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 87


June 25, 1996, Submitted  
July 3, 1996, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the denial of his writ of habeas corpus from the Circuit Court Of Upshur County (West Virginia) contending that the use of a felony third offense shoplifting conviction as a prior felony under W.Va. Code § 61-11-18 to impose a five-year recidivist sentence as a habitual offender was improper.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed for a writ of habeas corpus contending that use of a third offense misdemeanor shoplifting conviction, enhanced for sentencing purposes to be a felony was improper in applying the recidivist statute, W.Va. Code § 61-11-18 (1994), to impose a five-year sentence. The lower court denied his petition and he challenged that denial. On appeal, the court held that the legislative intent of similar statutes, applying enhancement of multiple DUI convictions under W.Va. Code § 61-11-18 (1994) to felony status did not violate the disproportionality provisions of W.Va. Const. art. III, § 5, and that because third offense shoplifting was a felony within the scope of the recidivist statute, W.Va. Code § 61-11-18 (1994), given the plain and unambiguous language of the statute the lower court's denial, was proper. The court, therefore, affirmed the lower court's denial of petitioner's writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's denial of petitioner's writ of habeas corpus challenging the use of an enhanced misdemeanor for recidivist sentencing purposes.

State v. Berrill


No. 23050


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 578; 474 S.E.2d 508; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 56


February 27, 1996, Submitted  
June 14, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Calhoun County. Honorable Charles E. McCarty, Judge. Criminal Action No. 94-APM-4.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Calhoun County (West Virginia), which denied his petition appealing magistrate court jury convictions for disrupting a public meeting in violation of the anti-disruption statute, W. Va. Code § 61-6-19, and wearing a mask in public in violation of the anti-mask statute, W. Va. Code § 61-6-22.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged after entering a school board meeting dressed in a devil costume in an effort to convince the school board to change the high school red devil mascot. Defendant challenged his conviction on the grounds that it violated his right to petition for a redress of grievances and his right to freedom of speech as provided under the First Amendment to the U.S. Constitution, and W. Va. Const. art. III, §§ 7, 16. Defendant also argued that he was denied the right to allocution. The court found that W. Va. Code §§ 61-6-19, 61-6-22 were constitutionally applied to defendant, and thus, affirmed the convictions. Because W. Va. Code § 61-6-19 created an offense without reference to speech, or the content thereof, the court held that it was a time, place, or manner restriction on the right to petition and freedom of speech, a restriction which was neutral with respect to the content of the restricted speech. However, the court agreed that defendant was denied his right to allocution and reversed and remanded the cause to the circuit court, with directions to resentence defendant after first according him his right of allocution and considering any allocution offered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court insofar as it affirmed the convictions of defendant before the magistrate court. The court, however, reversed the circuit court's judgment of sentence. The court remanded the matter to the circuit court with instructions to resentence defendant after affording him the right of allocution.

State v. Ivey


No. 23079


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 571; 474 S.E.2d 501; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 71


February 27, 1996, Submitted  
June 14, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fayette County. Honorable John W. Hatcher, Judge. Misdemeanor Appeal No. 95-M-AP-3.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Fayette County (West Virginia), which convicted defendant, upon his conditional plea of guilty, of one count of negligent shooting, wounding, or killing of human being or livestock while hunting, a misdemeanor under W. Va. Code § 20-2-57 (1991). The trial court also denied defendant's motions to dismiss and to declare § 20-2-57 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Following a denial of defendant's motion to dismiss and motion to declare W. Va. Code § 20-2-57 (1991) unconstitutional, defendant entered a conditional guilty plea pursuant to W. Va. R. Crim. P. 11(a)(2) to one count of negligent shooting, wounding, or killing of human being or livestock while hunting. Defendant challenged the judgment of conviction and its denial of his motions. On appeal, defendant contended that the State was required, but failed, to show that defendant was grossly negligent in order to be convicted under § 20-2-57. Defendant also contended that the procedural requirements of § 20-2-57 violated his constitutional right against self-incrimination under the Fifth Amendment to the United States Constitution and article III, § 5 of the West Virginia Constitution. The court held that it was only necessary that defendant had acted with ordinary negligence or carelessness to support a conviction under § 20-2-57. The court held that defendant voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently waived his constitutional right against self-incrimination prior to making a statement regarding the shooting incident that led to his arrest and conviction under § 20-2-57.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State ex rel. Roy Allen S. v. Stone


No. 23355


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 624; 474 S.E.2d 554; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 72


April 23, 1996, Submitted  
June 14, 1996, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator ex-husband sought a writ of prohibition to prevent enforcement of the judgment of respondent judge directing that a blood sample be taken from a minor child for the purpose of determining her paternity.


OVERVIEW: A minor child was born during a separation in the marriage of the ex-husband and the mother, and the putative biological father maintained a relationship with the child. After the divorce of the ex-husband and the mother, the mother had custody of the child and married the putative biological father, allowing him to further maintain a relationship with the child. The ex-husband received custody of the child, and the putative biological father sought to establish paternity. The court found that (1) a father who established a relationship with a child had a liberty interest in that relationship, regardless of the mother's marital status, (2) the historical rationales for preventing a putative biological father from claiming paternity over a child born to another's wife could no longer sustain the intrusion on the biological father's liberty interest, and (3) W. Va. Code § 48A-6-1 was unconstitutional in part, as it violated the due process clause, but the Due Process Clause of the West Virginia Constitution required courts to hear and decide, under certain guidelines, paternity actions brought by a putative biological father of a child born to a married woman who was not his wife.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of prohibition and remanded the case to permit the paternity action to proceed as directed by the court.

State v. Martin


No. 23083


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 376; 472 S.E.2d 822; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 59


May 28, 1996, Submitted  
June 14, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. Honorable Rodney B. Merrifield, Judge. Civil Action No. 93-F-5 and 93-F-181.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Marion County (West Virginia), which denied his motion to reconsider the revocation of his probation.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was sentenced to a prison term of not less than two nor more than 10 years for the felony offense of malicious assault. The trial court suspended the sentence and placed him on probation. The prisoner's probation was suspended when he plead guilty to aggravated robbery. The trial court again suspended the sentences and placed him on probation. However, his probation was again revoked when it was found that he consumed alcohol and left his home confinement. The trial court denied the prisoner's motion to reconsider the revocation. On appeal, the court affirmed. The prisoner's "probation sentence" terminated upon the revocation of his probation. He was then resentenced pursuant to W. Va. Code § 25-4-6, which provided that in the case of revocation, the offender was to be given the sentence he would have originally received. Thus, the prisoner again received consecutive sentences upon the malicious assault and aggravated robbery convictions. His resentencing to not less that two years nor more than 10 years, with regard to the malicious assault conviction, and 10 years, with regard to the aggravated robbery conviction, did not violate proportionality principles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Todd Andrew H.


No. 23186


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 615; 474 S.E.2d 545; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 55


May 28, 1996, Submitted  
June 14, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY. HONORABLE DAVID H. SANDERS, JUDGE. NO. 95-J-45.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (West Virginia), which denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence and adjudged him a juvenile delinquent.


OVERVIEW: A police officer saw defendant standing on the street. The officer believed that defendant had failed to appear for a traffic citation and that he had a runaway petition filed against him. Defendant accompanied the officer to the station and he was placed under arrest. Defendant was searched and crack cocaine was discovered on his person. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress and adjudged him a delinquent. The court reversed and remanded the case. The court determined that there was no warrant for defendant's arrest for a failure to appear. The court found that, pursuant to W. Va. Code § 49-5-8(b)(3), a juvenile could be taken into custody without a warrant or court order if the officer had reasonable grounds to believe that the juvenile was a runaway and that the health, safety, and welfare of the child was endangered. The court noted that a records check indicated that a runaway petition had been filed against defendant. However, there was no evidence that defendant's health, safety, or welfare was endangered. Therefore, since no lawful custodial arrest existed, the search of defendant was invalid and the crack cocaine should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress and his adjudication of delinquency. The case was remanded to the trial court.

State v. Miller


No. 23155


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 588; 476 S.E.2d 535; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 69


April 30, 1996, Submitted  
June 14, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Miller v. Nohe, 2015 W. Va. LEXIS 555 (W. Va., Apr. 13, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF WYOMING COUNTY. HONORABLE JOHN S. HRKO, JUDGE. NO. 94-F-18.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Wyoming County (West Virginia), which denied defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of first degree murder and was sentenced to life. Defendant filed a motion for new trial that asserted various errors at trial. The trial court denied the motion. The court affirmed and held that: (1) the indictment was not defective and the inclusion of the words "first degree murder" was not prejudicial because the trial court properly instructed the jury on all the elements of the crime including the requirement of premeditation; (2) in the absence of a contemporaneous objection, a defendant forfeited on appeal the right to complain that the circuit clerk asked questions of the jury; (3) the defendant failed to demonstrate her entitlement to a new trial because the defendant failed to object to either the procedure used or to the omission of certain questions; (4) the trial court did not err where it decided two prospective jurors with underlying prejudice towards homosexuals were not unduly biased or prejudiced; and (5) merely telling a jury it may infer malice if the state proved beyond a reasonable doubt that the defendant, without lawful justification, excuse, or provocation fired a deadly weapon was not error of a constitutional dimension.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial.

State v. Johnson


No. 22954


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 575; 476 S.E.2d 522; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 37


January 16, 1996, Submitted  
May 21, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Upshur County. Criminal Action No. 93-F-65. Honorable Thomas H. Keadle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Upshur County (West Virginia), convicting him of first offense driving under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first offense driving under the influence of alcohol. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in refusing to quash the indictment on the grounds that the indictment charged an offense which the state could not possibly prove. The court ruled that a valid indictment or presentment could be made only by a grand jury, and that no court could make an indictment in the first instance or alter or amend the substance of an indictment returned by a grand jury. Further, the court held that a variation that had the effect of actually or constructively amending the indictment required reversal, whereas one that added nothing to the indictment could constitute harmless error. Also, the court found that the fact that the proof at trial differed from the allegations in the indictment was not reversible error. The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant, concluding that the factual allegations for first offense driving under the influence of alcohol were set forth in the indictment.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was affirmed.

Gribben v. Kirk


No. 23292, No. 23293


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 20; 475 S.E.2d 20; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 48


March 5, 1996, Submitted  
May 21, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Robert K. Smith, Special Judge. Civil Action No. 94-Misc-160.



DISPOSITION: No. 23292 - REVERSED AND REMANDED. No. 23293 - WRIT GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Superintendent (superintendent) of the Division of Public Safety (division), sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which directed the payment of a judgment in favor of appellee police officers by January 31, 1996. Petitioner superintendent also sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, state auditor and state treasurer, not to pay the judgment out of the division's account.


OVERVIEW: Police officers obtained a judgment for unpaid overtime. The circuit court ordered the judgment paid by January 31, 1996. The superintendent claimed that the state police would run out of money by April, 1996 if the judgment was paid from the division's current budget. The superintendent sought review of the circuit court's order and petitioned for a writ of mandamus to compel the treasurer and auditor not to pay the judgment out of the division's current budget. The court reversed the circuit court's order because the executive department and the legislature had several options in order to discharge the judgment, a previous liability of the State of West Virginia (state). Further, it was not for a court to choose among the alternatives. However, the legislature's mandate, that it was in its discretion as to whether it would pay judgment interest, violated the Due Process Clauses of the United States and West Virginia Constitutions because interest was a valid obligation of the state, pursuant to W. Va. Code § 56-6-31 (1981). Finally, the writ of mandamus was granted because the superintendent had the clear right not to have the judgment paid from the division's current budget.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus compelling the state auditor and the state treasurer not to pay the judgment in favor of the police officers out of the division's 1995-1996 account. The court reversed the order directing the payment of the judgment by January 31, 1996. The case was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

West Virginia Health Care Cost Review Auth. v. Boone Mem. Hosp.


No. 23035


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 326; 472 S.E.2d 411; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 49


April 24, 1996, Submitted  
May 17, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF KANAWHA COUNTY. HONORABLE CHARLES E. KING, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 94-AA-133.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which held that it's proposed stationary computerized tomography service was subject to a Certificate of Need review, because appellee West Virginia Health Care Cost Review Authority's (Authority) statutory regulations required it.


OVERVIEW: The hospital provided computerized tomography (CT) service to its patients by having a third party outside the hospital perform the service. After the third party's contract expired with the hospital, the hospital transported patients requiring CT service to another hospital far away. The hospital then attempted to purchase its own CT service machine. The Authority required that before the hospital could purchase the machine, it had to undergo a Certificate of Need (CON) review. The hospital filed suit, claiming that it did not have to have a CON. The court upheld the CON order and the hospital challenged the ruling. The court held that under state law, the hospital was required to undergo a CON review if it was providing new service. The court stated that the legislation was ambiguous in this instance, since it was unknown whether the law applied to a hospital that had a CT service provided by a third party. The court concluded that because the legislation was unclear, the Authority was acting within its administrative authority in requiring the CON. The court upheld the lower court, and dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, holding that the hospital was required to undergo a Certificate of Need review before it could purchase a computerized tomography machine.
