McComas v. Board of Educ.


No. 23291


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


197 W. Va. 188; 475 S.E.2d 280; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 47


March 5, 1996, Submitted  
May 17, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF FAYETTE COUNTY. HONORABLE CHARLES VICKERS, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 95-C-0050.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Education of Fayette County sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Fayette County (West Virginia), which granted a writ of mandamus to appellee taxpayers in action concerning appellant's closure and consolidation of public schools.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Board of Education of Fayette County implemented a plan to close and consolidate public schools. Appellee taxpayers initiated action against the plan. The trial court granted a writ of mandamus to appellees, and appellant sought review. The court held that, pursuant to W. Va. Code § 53-1-2 (1933), mandamus was the appropriate remedy when there were no other adequate means for respondents to obtain the desired relief and there was a legal duty on the part of appellant to do that which respondents sought. The court determined that, although appellant had the authority to close and consolidate schools, a writ of mandamus was appropriate when appellant overstepped its legal duties. Pursuant to W. Va. Code § 6-9A-3 (1987), all meetings of any government bodies must have been open to the public. The court held that § 6-9A-3 applied to the meetings concerning appellant's school closure/consolidation plan and that appellant failed to comply with such laws. The court affirmed an order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court, which granted a writ of mandamus to appellee taxpayers against appellant Board of Education of Fayette County concerning appellant's implementation of school closure/consolidation plan. The court held that, although appellant had authority to implement such plan, a writ of mandamus was appropriate when appellant overstepped its legal duties.

 

83 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Broughton


No. 22944


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 281; 470 S.E.2d 413; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 33


January 17, 1996, Submitted  
April 8, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Thomas W. Steptoe, Circuit Judge. Civil Action No. 93-F-44.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed orders from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (West Virginia), which convicted him for the delivery of cocaine, the delivery of marijuana, and conspiracy to deliver marijuana. Defendant challenged the trial court's order that imposed consecutive imprisonment sentences on him, 1 to 15 years for each of the delivery convictions and one to five years for the conspiracy conviction.


OVERVIEW: The police apprehended a buyer of cocaine and marijuana. In exchange for the buyer's participation in their investigation, he was not prosecuted. The buyer bought more drugs with marked money and returned to the police. The buyer asserted that defendant had sold the drugs to him. The police apprehended defendant when he fled. A drug-sniffing dog located the marked money a short distance from defendant's apprehension point. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's contention that the marked money was erroneously admitted for lack of a proper foundation and relevance. Trial testimony adequately established a nexus between the money and defendant. Defendant was not entitled to directed verdicts on any of the charges because there was sufficient evidence for the jury to return guilty verdicts. Defendant's right to be free from double jeopardy was not violated by the consecutive sentences for the separate offenses of marijuana and cocaine because the delivery of each substance was a separate violation of the law. Defendant was not entitled to the abbreviated sentencing consideration under W. Va. Code § 60A-4-401(a) because he was simultaneously convicted of more serious offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentences for delivery of cocaine, delivery of marijuana, and conspiracy to deliver marijuana. The court reversed defendant's conviction for delivery of marijuana on the State's concession that the sentence was statutorily improper. The court remanded for resentencing but affirmed defendant's sentences for the other crimes.

 

84 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. LaRock


No. 22979


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 294; 470 S.E.2d 613; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 25


February 27, 1996, Submitted  
March 20, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF FAYETTE COUNTY. HONORABLE CHARLES M. VICKERS, JUDGE. NO. 93-F-38.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the denial of his motion for an acquittal or a new trial by the Circuit Court of Fayette County (West Virginia) upon his conviction for the first-degree murder of his 19-month-old son. Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to show the requisite premeditation and intent to convict him of murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: In a murder trial, defendant argued that he suffered from "diminished capacity." The court held that: (1) defendant's intolerant and hostile relationship and behavior towards his son showed that he acted with deliberation and premeditation; (2) a defense expert's excluded testimony provided no factual basis from which to infer that defendant could not intend the consequences of his actions; (3) there was likewise no evidence to support a jury charge that defendant suffered from a specific mental defect that rendered him incapable of forming a specific intent to kill; (4) historical evidence of uncharged prior acts was admissible because it was inextricably intertwined with the charged crime and the continued pattern of physical and mental abuse defendant inflicted on his son was also relevant to show intent, motive, malice, and the absence of accident; (5) trial courts had discretionary authority to bifurcate trials under W. Va. Code § 62-3-15 when the jury was required to make a mercy finding, but this new statutory interpretation was not retroactively applied to defendant; and (6) the rulings made on unpreserved assignments of error would be affirmed under any standard of review.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and the sentence of life imprisonment without mercy were affirmed because the numerous assignments of error raised by the defendant had no merit.

State by & Through McGraw v. Imperial Mktg.


No. 22809


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 346; 472 S.E.2d 792; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 27


September 20, 1995, Submitted  
March 20, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Herman G. Canady, Jr., Judge. Civil Action No. 94-C-243.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, AS MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State sought a preliminary injunction to enjoin defendant corporation from soliciting consumers in a deceptive manner in violation of the West Virginia Prizes and Gifts Act, W. Va. Code §§ 46A-6D-1 to 10 (1992). The Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) found that there was reasonable cause to believe that the corporation engaged in deceptive or misleading conduct and granted the preliminary relief. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation argued that there was not a specific finding that any of the direct mail solicitations amounted to material misrepresentations and that the solicitations in their totality contained nothing more than standard puffing, which was an acceptable and lawful practice when attempting to sell a product. The corporation also argued that its solicitations were protected as commercial speech. The court rejected the corporation's arguments. The court found that the State only had to prove by minimal evidence that the corporation was engaging in conduct that violated West Virginia Prizes and Gifts Act, W. Va. Code §§ 46A-6D-1 to 10 (1992). There was sufficient evidence that the solicitations were ambiguous and did not represent a clear and meaningful disclosure. The granting of temporary relief under W. Va. Code § 46A-7-110 (1974) for a violation of the West Virginia Prize and Gifts Act was more narrow than the typical motion for a preliminary injunction. The court applied a four-part test when it determined that the corporation's deceptive solicitations were not protected as commercial speech. The court objected to the absence of any time constraints within the injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment but modified the temporary injunction by limiting its duration.

 

86 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Cooper v. Caperton


No. 23059


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 208; 470 S.E.2d 162; 1996 W. Va. LEXIS 13


November 28, 1995, Submitted  
February 29, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF KANAWHA COUNTY. HONORABLE HERMAN G. CANADY, JR., JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 95-MISC-290.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant council sought a final determination of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) that ordered it to certify to appellee development authority the marketing and sale of general obligation bonds. Appellant taxpayer challenged that judgment, which denied his petition for writ of mandamus in which he challenged a constitutional amendment that authorized issuance and sale of the bonds.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer claimed that the publishing of the proposed constitutional amendment in summary form in every county but one violated W.Va. Const. art. XIV, § 2 and, therefore was unconstitutional. The court however, affirmed the constitutionality of the amendment. In doing so, the court applied de novo review because the circuit court interpreted a provision of the constitution. The court held that the publication in summary form was proper because it substantially complied with a procedural requirement within art. XIV, § 2. The court reasoned that under this "substantial compliance" test there was no mechanical formula to have been applied, but rather the court had to determine whether in this particular case did the deviation from the procedural requirement of full text publication prevent a true expression of the voters' will. The amendment was valid because it was endorsed by two-thirds of the legislature, a majority of the voters approved it, the legislatively approved summary was published in a timely fashion in all but one county, and the it was more clear then the full text and excluded no material terms. However, the court cautioned against such further deviations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied the taxpayer's petition for writ of mandamus and upheld the validity of a constitutional amendment that authorized the issuance and sale of general obligation bonds.

RANDOLPH COUNTY BD. OF EDUC. v. ADAMS


No. 22902


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


196 W. Va. 9; 467 S.E.2d 150; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 265


September 26, 1995, Submitted  
December 14, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF RANDOLPH COUNTY. HONORABLE JOHN HENNING, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 94-C-69.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a county board of education (board), challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Randolph County (West Virginia), which granted defendant parents' motion to dismiss the board's declaratory judgment action and found that it was unconstitutional for the board to charge parents of non-needy school children a book user fee for school books and materials necessary for the completion of the required school curriculum.


OVERVIEW: After losing a levy at the polls, the board established a book user fee for non-needy school children, whom it defined as those children not participating in the free or reduced school lunch program. When parents refused to pay the fee on the grounds that it violated the "free schools" clause, W. Va. Const. art. XII, § 1, the board filed an action for declaratory judgment to direct that payment. The trial court agreed with the parents that the fee was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that whatever items were deemed necessary to accomplish the goals of a school system and were in fact an integral fundamental part of the elementary and secondary education had to be provided free of charge to all students in order to comply with the constitutional mandate of a "free school" system. The court determined that the textbooks in this case were such an integral fundamental part of education, holding that hindering access to necessary materials would make the educational process nearly meaningless. The court rejected the board's claim of financial hardship, ruling that it was no defense to a violation of the "free school" guarantee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Gribben v. Kirk


No. 22910


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


195 W. Va. 488; 466 S.E.2d 147; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 241


September 19, 1995, Submitted  
December 8, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF KANAWHA COUNTY. HONORABLE PAUL ZAKAIB, JR., JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 94-MISC-160.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state employer, auditor, and treasurer, sought review of judgment in favor of appellee employees in a mandamus proceeding for unpaid wages under the West Virginia Wage and Hour Law, W. Va. Code § 21-5C-1 et seq., in the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia).


OVERVIEW: Appellants, state employer, auditor, and treasurer, sought review of judgment in favor of appellee employees in a mandamus proceeding for unpaid wages under West Virginia Wage and Hour Law, W. Va. Code § 21-5C-1 et seq., an overtime exemption to wage laws for state troopers that was declared unconstitutional. The court rejected appellants' argument that sovereign immunity and separation of powers precluded the lower court from ordering the payment of a monetary award from the state treasury general funds. The court explained that appellees' claim for back overtime pay was not barred by the immunity provision of W. Va. Const. art. VI, § 35 because a state official, not the state, was sued in the mandamus proceeding to require the performance of a nondiscretionary function of paying appellees according to certain terms as the legislature had required. The court further observed the award of overtime was prospective relief only, and the constitutional bar to retroactive relief was not an issue that had to be confronted because the lower court's order of prospective relief acquired preclusive effect against appellants, who were in privity with litigants in the wage exemption case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment in favor of appellee employees in a mandamus proceeding against appellants, state employer, auditor, and treasurer, because sovereign immunity principles did not preclude an order requiring payment of back pay when such relief was prospective only, and mandamus was not directed at the state but instead at state officials in their official capacity to compel the performance of a nondiscretionary duty required by law.

Appalachian Power Co. v. State Tax Dep't


No. 22795


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


195 W. Va. 573; 466 S.E.2d 424; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 235


September 20, 1995, Submitted  
December 8, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION NO. 90-C-1213. HONORABLE PAUL ZAKAIB, JR., JUDGE. APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF KANAWHA COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff power companies (companies) appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which found that a legislative regulation, 110 W. Va. Code St. R. 13 § 1a.2.11 (1990), was a valid and enforceable regulation properly interpreting W. Va. Code § 11-13-2n(a)(1) (1990). In reaching its decision, the circuit court found there was no express or implied deduction for company use or line loss provided in § 11-13-2n(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: The companies argued that § 11-13-2n(a)(1) was clear and unambiguous in excluding company use and line loss from the calculation of net generation of electricity available for sale and violated equal protection principles by excluding manufacturers that generated electric power for their own use without providing similar exclusions for the companies, which generated electricity for sale. Defendant state tax department (department) argued that production taxes were traditionally based on quantities produced for sale and not on quantities actually delivered to the retail market and the department's interpretation was entitled to great weight. The court held that the department's interpretation excluding line loss and company use deductions was a well-reasoned and rational decision that comported with the language of the statute. When a court reached the same reading of a statute as a practical construction given it by the enforcing agency, that was a powerful weight supporting such reading. The statute did not violate equal protection because the differences in the rights and duties of a public utility and a nonutility justified the separate classification in which each was included.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the department's interpretation of the statute that there was no express or implied deduction for company use or line loss.

Philyaw v. Gatson


No. 22866

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable A. Andrew MacQueen, Judge. Civil Action No. 92-AA-308.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) reversed the decision of appellee Board of Review of the West Virginia Department of Employment Security (Board), which ruled that appellee claimant was not eligible to receive unemployment compensation benefits after she resigned from her position as a magistrate court clerk in order to run for a non-judicial public office. Appellant court administrator appealed the reversal.

The claimant contended that she was improperly forced to resign her position as a condition to the exercise of her right to seek public office, consequently she did not leave work voluntarily without good cause involving fault on the part of the employer within the meaning of W.Va. Code § 21A-6-3(1) (1990).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and held that the claimant was not eligible to receive unemployment compensation benefits.

SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA

DISPOSITION: No. 22886 - Writ denied.

No. 22847 - Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator 1 challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Marion County (West Virginia), which denied his petition for habeas corpus. Relator 2 filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Both relators filed their petitions for writs of habeas corpus to challenge their convictions of sexual assault in the first degree a violation of W. Va. Code § 61-8B-3(a)(1991).


OVERVIEW: Both relators were convicted of violations of W. Va. Code § 61-8B-3(a) (1991), which provided, in relevant part, that a person was guilty of sexual assault in the first degree when such person, being 14 years old or more, engaged in sexual intercourse with another person who was 11 years old or less. According to the relators, the State failed to prove the victims were 11 years old or less. The victims in both cases were approximately 11 years and 8 months. The realtors asserted that under the statutory language a crime was only committed if the victim was 11 years old or less. Consequently, the relators argued that once a person reached his or her 11th birthday, he or she had already lived 11 years and any time after the 11th birthday made such a person beyond the age of 11. The State countered with the argument that the common meaning of being 11 years of age encompassed those months until the person reached their 12th birthday. The court held that W. Va. Code § 61-8B-3(a) (1991) applied to a person who were 11 years old, but who had not reached his or her 12th birthday.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of trial court with respect to relator 1 and denied relator 2's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

In re Dailey


No. 22964


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


195 W. Va. 330; 465 S.E.2d 601; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 206


September 12, 1995, Submitted  
November 16, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Concurring Opinion Dated December 4, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certified Question from the Circuit Court of Cabell County Honorable L. D. Egnor, Judge. Civil Action No. 95-P-262.



DISPOSITION: CERTIFIED QUESTION ANSWERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cabell County (West Virginia) submitted a certified question challenging the constitutionality of W. Va. Code § 61-7-4 (1995), the statute that empowered West Virginia circuit courts with the authority to issue a license to carry a concealed deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: The licensee applicant applied to the circuit court for a license to carry a concealed deadly weapon under § 61-7-4. The circuit court denied the license, holding that issuance of such a license was an exercise of the state's police power and therefore it lacked jurisdiction to issue the license. The circuit court certified the question to the court. The court answered the question and held that § 61-7-4 was unconstitutional. The court held that § 61-7-4 was an unlawful delegation of legislative power to the circuit courts in violation of W. Va. Const. art. V, § 1, the separation of powers doctrine. The regulation of the right to carry a concealed deadly weapon was exclusively a legislative function because it involved no case or controversy as the circuit court had no discretion to deny the license if the applicant met § 61-7-4's requirements. The court ordered that its ruling be applied prospectively.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question and held that the concealed deadly weapons statute was unconstitutional.

Sheila L. ex rel. Ronald M.M. v. Ronald P.M.


No. 22794


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


195 W. Va. 210; 465 S.E.2d 210; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 194


September 12, 1995, Submitted  
October 27, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF WETZEL COUNTY. HONORABLE JOHN T. MADDEN, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 93-P-13M.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Wetzel County (West Virginia), which dismissed her petition for custody of her child on the ground that it was required to give full faith and credit to a final order of an Ohio court that assumed jurisdiction and awarded custody of the child to respondent father.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner mother and respondent father resided together, unmarried, in Ohio when their child was born. The child resided with the mother, who moved to West Virginia. The child went to Ohio for a visit and the father obtained custody in the Ohio court. The mother filed an application for custody in West Virginia, and the trial court denied the application based on full faith and credit, and the mother appealed. The court held that: (1) the Parental Kidnapping Prevention Act of 1980 (PKPA), 28 U.S.C.S. § 1738A, preempted the Uniform Child Custody Jurisdiction Act, enacted in W. Va. Code § 48-10-1 et seq., and in Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3109.21 et seq., where they were in conflict; (2) it need not accept the assertions of the judgment if the Ohio court lacked jurisdiction and did not fully and fairly litigate the issues; (3) West Virginia was the child's home state under the PKPA, codified at 28 U.S.C.S. § 1738A(b)(4), and did not did not decline to exercise jurisdiction; (4) Ohio had not entered a decree on which it could assert continuing jurisdiction under the PKPA, codified at 28 U.S.C § 1738A(d); and (5) the Ohio order was based on unsubstantiated and self-serving assertions.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court, which denied petitioner mother's application for custody of the child on the ground that the order of an Ohio court that granted custody to respondent father was entitled to full faith and credit, was reversed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

State ex rel. Brewer v. Starcher


No. 22966


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


195 W. Va. 185; 465 S.E.2d 185; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 183


September 12, 1995, Submitted  
October 27, 1995, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ Granted as Moulded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator filed an original proceeding seeking a writ of prohibition to prevent respondent trial judge of the Circuit Court of Monongalia County (West Virginia) from adding terms to a plea agreement negotiated under W. Va. R. Crim. P. 11(e)(1)(C).


OVERVIEW: The relator sought to prohibit the trial judge from adding additional terms to a binding plea agreement that had been negotiated under W. Va. R. Crim. P. 11(e)(1)(C). The relator had pleaded guilty to wanton endangerment involving a firearm. The court granted the relator's petition for a writ of prohibition because the trial judge's unjustified unilateral modification of a specific and judicially accepted plea agreement violated Rule 11. A circuit court has no authority on its own to vacate or modify a validly accepted guilty plea under Rule 11(e)(1)(C) because of subsequent events that do not impugn the validity of the original plea agreement, absent a showing of fraud. The trial judge's attempt to modify the sentencing decision, and impose new conditions on the relator, constituted a clear violation of the prohibition against judicial involvement in plea bargaining under Rule 11.


OUTCOME: The court granted as moulded the relator's petition for a writ of prohibition to prevent the trial judge from adding additional terms to a binding plea agreement, under the terms of which the relator had pleaded guilty to wanton endangerment involving a firearm.

TSGP P'ship v. Dep't of Tax & Revenue


No. 22814


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


195 W. Va. 405; 465 S.E.2d 862; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 178


September 20, 1995, Submitted  
October 13, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Civil Action No. 93-AA-166. Honorable Paul Zakaib, Jr., Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant revenue department appealed from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which ruled adversely to it in ordering release of a large sum plus accrued interest to appellee taxpayer, even though it affirmed an administrative law judge's ruling that alternative minimum tax (AMT) was constitutional. The revenue department challenged the ruling that AMT could not be applied on a pro rata basis.


OVERVIEW: Because the Legislature could have provided for repeal of AMT to relate back to the beginning of the year, and because the repealing statute expressly provided that it would not take effect for 90 days from passage of House Bill 2587, the Legislature expressly intended to permit utilizing AMT until July 7, 1989. There was no error in pro rata assessment. Although AMT was not assessed against the taxpayer on July 6, AMT and liability to pay the tax on assessment already accrued before reenactment of West Virginia Code § 19-23-9(b)(3) minus AMT. The Legislature expressly provided for using pro rata accounting for a shortened racing year. The legislative omission of repeal as a specific instance warranting pro rata assessment of AMT tax did not prevent such assessment. Rather, the express delineation of conditions warranting pro rata application of the AMT tax supported assessing it on a pro rata basis due to the tax's mid-year repeal. The pari-mutuel AMT, previously in West Virginia Code § 19-23-9(b)(3) (1987), but repealed through House Bill 2587, was properly utilized to assess on a pro rata basis the amount of pari-mutuel wagering taxes owed by the state's dog track licensees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Circuit Court.

Bradley v. Williams


No. 22766


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


195 W. Va. 180; 465 S.E.2d 180; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 181


September 13, 1995, Submitted  
October 13, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Justice Recht withdraws his right to file a concurrence, December 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cabell County. Honorable L. D. Egnor, Circuit Judge. Civil Action No. 91-C-1750.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Tax Commissioner of the State of West Virginia (commissioner), sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cabell County (West Virginia), which reversed the commissioner's decision and that ordered tax refunds be paid to appellee taxpayers, husband and wife, for the years 1978 to 1984.


OVERVIEW: In 1978, the taxpayers excluded federal civil service retirement income from their state income tax. In 1979, the commissioner informed the taxpayers that the income was not deductible until the taxpayer husband reached age 65, in 1985. The taxpayers did not appeal or challenge the determination. In 1990, following a United States Supreme Court decision, the taxpayers filed a petition for a tax refund for the years 1978 to 1984. Applying the applicable statute of limitations, the commissioner denied the petition. The circuit court reversed the commissioner's decision based upon the doctrine of equitable estoppel. The court reversed and remanded the circuit court's decision and held that the taxpayers failed to timely challenge the commissioner's decision under W. Va. Code § 11-10-14(d) (1995). The taxpayers did not file a refund claim within the limitation period of W. Va. Code § 11-10-14(1) (1995). The doctrine of equitable estoppel was inapplicable because the commissioner's 1979 response was an accurate statement of West Virginia law. Nothing in the commissioner's response constituted an affirmative act that induced the taxpayers to refrain from challenging his decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court that reversed the commissioner's decision that the taxpayers were not entitled to a tax refund for the years 1978-1984. The case was remanded with directions for the reinstatement of the commissioner's decision.

State ex rel. Hill v. Zakaib


No. 22881


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


194 W. Va. 688; 461 S.E.2d 194; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 173


June 27, 1995, Submitted  
July 19, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Circuit Court Action No. 92-F-161.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner brought a motion for a writ of habeas corpus to release him from custody, arguing he completed his term of incarceration and was being illegally detained.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was fifteen when he shot and killed another young man. He was originally sentenced to an indeterminate term of not less than five nor more than 18 years in the penitentiary. When he turned 18, he was returned to the trial court to permit reconsideration and modification of his sentence. At that time the judge ordered his confinement in youthful offender center for six months or longer, but no more than two years. The prisoner sought release after he had successfully completed the youthful offender program. On appeal, the court granted the writ, and ordered the prisoner released. The court found that although sentencing the prisoner under the youthful offender statute was technically improper in light of his age at the time he committed the crime, in that he was too young, this particular infirmity did not render the sentence illegal or void ab initio. The court reasoned that a sentence which was technically infirm, but generally and substantially complied with the spirit and purpose of the law, was not void, but merely voidable. The court then found that the State waived the objection by its failure to object when the youthful offender sentence was imposed.


OUTCOME: The court granted the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

STATE ex rel. MEADOWS v. HECHLER


No. 22875


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


195 W. Va. 11; 462 S.E.2d 586; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 176


June 27, 1995, Submitted  
July 19, 1995, Decided  
July 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of Mandamus.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner personal care home residents sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent state officials to file agency regulations pertaining to personal care homes. The residents alleged that W. Va. Code § 29A-3-12(b) (Supp. 1994) of the West Virginia Administrative Procedures Act (APA), W. Va. Code §§ 29A-3-1 to -17 (1993 & Supp. 1994), was unconstitutional in that it violated W. Va. Const. art. V, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The legislature had subjected the regulations to a legislative veto under W. Va. Code § 29A-3-12(b) (Supp. 1994), which permitted proposed administrative regulations to "die" if the legislature failed to take action on them. The personal care home residents contended that § 29A-3-12(b) violated the separation of powers requirement of W. Va. Const. art. V, § 1. The state officials argued that the executive branch and the attendant concerns of separation of powers were not introduced into the rulemaking equation until the legislature actually approved proposed agency rules. The court granted the writ. The court noted that the rulemaking function came under the executive department's bailiwick upon the delegation of the duty to propose rules for promulgation. The court determined that the legislative veto contained within the APA was unconstitutional, and that W. Va. Code § 29A-3-12(b) violated the separation of powers requirement of W. Va. Const. art. V, § 1 in that the legislative veto impermissibly encroached upon the executive branch's obligation to enforce the law.


OUTCOME: The court granted the personal care home residents a writ of mandamus against the state officials. The court determined that the legislative veto scheme was unconstitutional, and directed the legislature to promptly draft legislation to replace the unconstitutional section and to consider passage of additional legislation.

WETZEL CTY. SOLID WASTE AUTH. v. WEST VIRGINIA DIV. OF NATURAL RESOURCES


No. 22778


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


195 W. Va. 1; 462 S.E.2d 349; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 153


May 10, 1995, Submitted  
July 14, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certified Question from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable James O. Holliday, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: CERTIFIED QUESTION ANSWERED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) certified the following question to the court: whether W. Va. Code § 7-5-22 (1990) violated W. Va. Const. art. V, § 1, by impermissibly delegating taxing authority, violated W. Va. Const. art. X, § 1, requiring taxation to be equal and uniform throughout the state, and violated W. Va. Const. art. III, § 10, requiring substantive due process and the equal protection of the laws.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to W. Va. Code § 7-5-22, the solid waste authority enacted an assessment fee on each ton of solid waste in the county. The authority filed a mandamus action to compel enforcement of tonnage caps at a solid waste facility owned and operated by a transport company and to enforce the collection of all required fees and taxes. The circuit court judge issued a writ of mandamus, which a new judge vacated. The circuit court judge ruled that § 7-5-22 did not violate W. Va. Const. art. V, § 1; art. X, § 1; or art. III, § 10. The court accepted the appeal on certified question of whether W. Va. Code § 7-5-22 was unconstitutional. The court found § 7-5-22 constitutional and held that the solid waste assessment fee authorized by § 7-5-22 was a regulatory fee rather than a tax, and, therefore, § 7-5-22 did not violate W. Va. Const. art. V, § 1 or W. Va. Const. art. X, § 1. The solid waste assessment fee imposed by W. Va. Code § 7-5-22 was rationally related to the legitimate governmental purpose of defraying the administrative costs of the regional and county solid waste authorities and their solid waste programs. The imposition of the fee was not arbitrary and unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question and held that the disputed statute, which authorized solid waste authorities to impose a solid waste assessment fee, did not violate the state constitution. The court also remanded the case to the circuit court for further proceedings.

 

100 of 754 DOCUMENTS


In re City of Beckley


No. 22596


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


194 W. Va. 423; 460 S.E.2d 669; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 159


May 16, 1995, Submitted  
July 11, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Raleigh County. Honorable Robert A. Burnside, Judge. Case No. 93-AD-410-B.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Raleigh County (West Virginia) that rejected its petition for a minor boundary adjustment, which had been approved by the County Commission of Raleigh County. Two volunteer fire departments had challenged the annexation by writ of certiorari. The circuit court held that the boundary adjustment was invalid and allowed relief through a writ of prohibition.


OVERVIEW: The city sought and obtained an annexation by a minor boundary adjustment under W. Va. Code § 8-6-5 (1989) of property along W. Va. Route 3 and three adjacent parcels. There was no opposition to the annexation by the freeholders at the commission's public hearing. The city claimed that the fire departments, as non-freeholders, had no standing to challenge the annexation and that the circuit court erred in holding that the annexation was invalid. On appeal, the court agreed with the city and ordered the annexation affirmed. Although the circuit court was correct that the fire departments lacked standing to bring a writ of certiorari, it erred by granting a writ of prohibition because prohibition could only be directed against judicial officials. Moreover, the circuit court erred in determining that the annexation was not a proper boundary adjustment because the property was sufficiently contiguous to the city limits. Finally, noting that annexation was essentially a legislative matter and that the commission enjoyed broad discretion, the court held that the judiciary should not have intruded upon the commission unless the process was unconstitutional or invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the case with directions to affirm the commission's order granting the city's petition for annexation.

 

101 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Collins v. Bedell


No. 22781, No. 22783


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


194 W. Va. 390; 460 S.E.2d 636; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 122


April 4, 1995, Submitted  
June 19, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Justice Cleckley withdraws his right to file a concurring opinion.



DISPOSITION: No. 22781 - WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED. No. 22783 - WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners criminal and driver sought separate writs of prohibition against respondent judges, seeking to prohibit a trial judge from denying a jury trial de novo in the circuit court on appeal from a criminal conviction in a magistrate court. The cases were consolidated and pertained to amendments to W. Va. Code §§ 50-5-13, 50-5-8, which dealt with appeals of a criminal conviction in a magistrate court to the circuit court.


OVERVIEW: The criminal was charged sexual abuse and waived his right to a jury trial in the magistrate court. After trial, the criminal was convicted. The criminal appealed to the circuit court for a trial de novo, but the request was denied. The driver was arrested for driving under the influence and did not demand a jury trial in magistrate court. The driver was convicted, and the circuit court denied his request for a jury trial. The criminal and the driver filed petitions seeking to prohibit a trial judge from denying a jury trial de novo in the circuit court on appeal from a criminal conviction in a magistrate court. The court granted the criminal's petition and denied the driver's petition. The court held that the procedural amendments eliminating the right to a trial by jury on appeal from the magistrate court criminal proceeding did not violate state or federal constitutions. However, because the record failed to reflect whether the criminal was given the opportunity to voluntarily waive his right to a trial by jury under the amended statute, the criminal was entitled to that opportunity. As to the driver, the court held that there was no showing of a constitutional error.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant criminal a writ of prohibition and denied defendant driver a writ of prohibition in their consolidated actions seeking to prohibit a trial judge from denying a jury trial de novo in the circuit court on appeal from a criminal conviction in a magistrate court.

 

102 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Gainer v. West Virginia Bd. of Invs.


No. 22574


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


194 W. Va. 143; 459 S.E.2d 531; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 96


January 18, 1995, Submitted  
May 31, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Concurring and Dissenting Opinion Filed June 12, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Robert K. Smith, Special Judge. Civil Action No. 94-C-840.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state auditor challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which denied his request for injunctive and declaratory relief to prohibit appellee West Virginia Board of Investments (board) from investing certain monies from the consolidated pension fund in corporate stocks.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general stated that the board's investment of consolidated pension funds of the Public Employees Retirement System in corporate stocks pursuant to W. Va. Code § 12-6-9(j) (1991) violated W. Va. Const. art. X, § 6 and fiduciary principles. The state auditor sought a temporary injunction and declaratory judgment consistent with the opinion issued by the attorney general. The circuit court concluded that W. Va. Code § 12-6-9(j) (1991) did not violate W. Va. Const. art. X, § 6. The court found that the lower court erred and reversed the decision below. The constitutional language could not be read as proscribing only those type of historical credit for stock transactions, which served as the impetus for the enactment of art. X, § 6. Instead, the clearly-stated proscription against the state becoming an owner of corporate stock was read in accordance with its clear and plainly-stated terms. The court concluded that W. Va. Code § 12-6-9(j) (1991) was invalid and unenforceable because it violated the all-encompassing proscription found in W. Va. Const. art. X, § 6 against the state becoming a stockholder in any company or association.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that denied the state auditor's petition for injunctive and declaratory relief. The court held that the statute, which authorized the board's investment of pension funds in corporate stock violated the constitutional provision against the state being a stockholder in any company.

 

103 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Billings v. City of Point Pleasant


No. 22837


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


194 W. Va. 301; 460 S.E.2d 436; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 83


April 5, 1995, Submitted  
May 18, 1995, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ Denied


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator city council candidate filed an original action seeking a writ of mandamus against respondents, a city and its city clerk, its mayor, and the members of its city council. The candidate challenged the constitutionality of W. Va. Code, 3-5-7(b)(6) (1991), asserting that the requirement that he not have been registered as a member of another political party within 60 days of his filing for election was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The candidate changed his political party affiliation and filed his certificate of announcement to run as a candidate for the office of councilman-at-large in the city. He changed his political party affiliation less than 60 days prior to the filing of his certificate of announcement, which was contrary to W. Va. Code, 3-5-7(b)(6) (1991). A complaint was filed with the city clerk seeking to remove the candidate from the ballot. The candidate then filed his mandamus action seeking a ruling that the 60 day durational affiliation requirement in W. Va. Code, 3-5-7(b)(6) was unconstitutional. The court found that the requirement was constitutional and denied the requested writ of mandamus. A restriction on the right to run for public office was to be upheld only if the restriction advanced a state interest of compelling importance and the state did not have a less restrictive means of satisfying that legitimate state goal. The court held that the state's interest in the stability of its political system was compelling, as was the state's interests in preserving the integrity of the political process and in preventing party raiding and voter confusion.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of mandamus.

State v. Bradshaw


No. 22302, No. 22553


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


193 W. Va. 519; 457 S.E.2d 456; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 61


March 7, 1995, Submitted  
March 27, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wayne County. Honorable Robert G. Chafin, Judge. No. 92-F-30.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her judgment of conviction entered by the Circuit Court of Wayne County (West Virginia) for first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sought review. The court affirmed, holding that defendant was not deprived of her Fifth Amendment right to counsel or right to remain silent. Defendant's statements when attempting to invoke those rights were equivocal and ambiguous. The record supported the trial court's conclusion that defendant's confession was voluntary. The trial court committed harmless error by admitting the testimony of defendant's spouse in violation of the spousal testimony privilege contained in W. Va. Code § 53-3-3. Also, defendant was properly cross-examined, because defendant voluntarily testified at trial. Finally, the trial court did not improperly instruct the jury, because the jury instructions conformed to the requirements of state law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for first degree murder.

State v. Sugg


No. 22486


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


193 W. Va. 388; 456 S.E.2d 469; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 40


January 18, 1995, Submitted  
March 10, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County Honorable John Hey, Judge. No. 93-F-274



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which convicted him of aggravated robbery with the use of a firearm. Defendant contended that (1) his statement to police on the night of arrest should have been excluded at trial; (2) evidence regarding coin wrappers was improperly admitted at trial; and (3) the 45-year sentence was disproportionate to the crime and was imposed for retaliatory reasons.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a minor, was arrested, signed a waiver of Miranda rights, and made a statement to police which was later admitted at trial. Defendant was convicted and appealed. The court affirmed conviction. It held, inter alia, that: (1) defendant asked to talk to the police before there was an opportunity to present him to the magistrate, and, thus, any violation of the prompt presentment requirements of W. Va. Code § 49-5-8(d) (1982) was attributable to defendant; (2) if a juvenile affirmatively requested that his parents not be notified until after he talked to the police, and this request was not coerced or suggested by the police, the juvenile could not use the period of time that it took to conduct the interview to claim a delay in parental notification; (3) the trial court did not err in failing to hold an additional in camera hearing to determine the admissibility of coin wrappers found in defendant's pockets at the time of his arrest; (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in ruling that testimony about the wrappers was admissible; and (5) there was insufficient evidence in the record for the court to review defendant's claim of retaliatory sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of aggravated robbery and sentenced him to 45 years in prison.

 

106 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Stephen L.H. v. Sherry L.H.


No. 22084


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


195 W. Va. 384; 465 S.E.2d 841; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 39


January 18, 1995, Submitted  
March 6, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County Honorable John Hey, Judge. Civil Action No. 88-C-3301.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) that overturned a family law master's findings that appellee father had sexually molested one of the parties' two daughters and had "probably" molested the other daughter in the mother's action for modification of visitation.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother divorced. The mother was granted custody of their two daughters, and the father was granted visitation rights. Based on allegations of the father's sexual molestation of the children, the mother petitioned for modification of visitation. After hearing evidence presented by the parties, the family master found that the father had sexually molested one of the daughters and had "probably" molested the other. The master recommended that visitation be terminated until the father's completion of psychological treatment and that he pay the costs and attorney fees. The circuit court rejected the master's findings and issued its own. On appeal, the court considered whether the circuit court violated W. Va. Code § 48A-4-20(c) (1993) when it conducted a de novo review of the findings of fact made by the family law master. The court held that the standard of review for a circuit court was controlled by the § 48A-4-20(c) and that a circuit court should review findings of fact made by a family law master only under a "clearly erroneous" standard and that it should review the application of law to the facts under an "abuse of discretion" standard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's decision and remanded the case with instructions to reinstate the family law master's findings of fact and her recommended decision. The court found that the family law master's findings were supported by substantial evidence in the record and that the circuit court erred in overturning each and every finding of fact of the master when such findings were substantially supported by record evidence.

 

107 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Abshire v. Cline


No. 22229


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


193 W. Va. 180; 455 S.E.2d 549; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 12


January 24, 1995, Submitted  
February 17, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Berkeley County. Honorable David H. Sanders, Judge. Civil Action No. 92-C-383.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver appealed a judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Berkeley County (West Virginia), affirming an administrative order issued by respondent, the Commissioner of the Department of Motor Vehicles (DMV), revoking his driver's license. After the driver was arrested for his second offense of driving under the influence of alcohol, he had requested and received an administrative hearing under W. Va. Code, 17C-5A-2 (1986).


OVERVIEW: The driver's hearing was twice continued at the Commissioner's request. The DMV mailed petitioner's counsel a letter on April 24, 1990, stating that the hearing had been rescheduled for May 3. By letter dated April 26, counsel replied to the notice via certified mail, return receipt requested, asking for a continuance because counsel already had two court hearings scheduled on May 3. The letter arrived at the post office on Friday, April 27, but the DMV did not pick up its mail until Monday, April 30. The DMV refused petitioner's request for a continuance because it was not received at least five days prior to the scheduled hearing date, as required by a DMV rule. The driver appeared at the hearing without counsel, and his license was revoked. On appeal, the court held that the DMV violated the driver's due process rights under the federal and state constitutions. Petitioner's counsel demonstrated "good cause" for the continuance and made a reasonable effort to meet the five-day rule by using certified mail, return receipt requested; he was not required to use overnight mail service. Although facially reasonable, the rule was unreasonably applied under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new administrative hearing.

 

108 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Adams


No. 22398, No. 22397


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


193 W. Va. 277; 456 S.E.2d 4; 1995 W. Va. LEXIS 20


January 17, 1995, Submitted  
February 17, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Putnam County. Honorable Clarence L. Watt, Judge. Criminal No. 92-F-115.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. Petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Putnam County (West Virginia), which convicted him of concealing stolen property and of transferring stolen property. On appeal defendant argued that the trial court erred in granting the state's pretrial motion to amend the indictment in order to reflect the correct name of the owner of the stolen goods.


OVERVIEW: The grand jury returned an indictment charging defendant, inter alia, with concealing stolen property and transferring stolen property. The indictment named the owner of the stolen goods. Before trial, the state discovered that the stolen property actually belonged to relative of the person named as the owner and filed a motion to amend the indictment. The trial court granted the motion and defendant was convicted. On appeal, he argued that the court's decision in McGraw v. State, 85 S.E.2d 849 (1955), required reversal of his conviction. The court noted that in McGraw it had held that changing the name of the owner of stolen property rendered an indictment invalid. The court reconsidered its holding in McGraw and modified it to the extent that it stood for the proposition that any change to an indictment required resubmission to the jury. The court announced a new rule that an indictment could be amended by the trial court provided the amendment was not substantial, was sufficiently definite and certain, did not take defendant by surprise and so long as any evidence defendant had before the amendment was equally available after amendment. The court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant after reconsidering and modifying its prior holding that changing the name of the owner of stolen goods rendered the indictment invalid. The court announced a new rule that an indictment could be amended if the change was not substantial, was sufficiently definite and certain, did not take defendant by surprise and defendant had the same evidence equally available before and after the amendment.

Mills v. Van Kirk


No. 22270


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 695; 453 S.E.2d 678; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 270


September 28, 1994, Submitted  
December 21, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County Honorable Lyne Ranson, Judge. Civil Action No. 92-C-2820.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant abutting landowners filed an appeal from the order of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee prospective buyer in his action for a declaratory judgment and an injunction to prevent appellee highway commissioner from subdividing or otherwise disposing of certain property other than in its entirety at a public auction pursuant to W. Va. Code § 17-2A-19 (1988).


OVERVIEW: The highway commissioner determined that certain property was not needed for the present or foreseeable future and could thus be sold pursuant to § 17-2A-19. The abutting landowners accepted the highway commissioner's offer to purchase the northern part of the property, but the prospective buyer claimed that he would purchase the entire property if it were sold at a public auction. The abutting landowners and the highway commissioner argued that § 17-2A-19 required that the abutting landowners be given a right of first refusal of the property at fair market value (FMV). However, the prospective buyer argued, and the circuit court found, that § 17-2A-19 did not require a right of first refusal, and that the highway commissioner had to obtain the highest and best price for the property. On appeal, the court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the prospective buyer, because the highway commissioner had the right to decide whether the property would be useful in the present or foreseeable future, and once that decision was made, he had to first offer the property to the abutting landowners for FMV. Moreover, he had determined the FMV in an unbiased manner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting summary judgment in favor of the prospective buyer in his action to prevent the highway commissioner's subdivision of property. The court ordered that a judgment be entered consistent with its opinion.

 

110 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. State Bd. of Educ. v. Gainer


No. 22549


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 417; 452 S.E.2d 733; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 268


November 29, 1994, Submitted  
December 21, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissenting Opinion Dated December 21, 1994.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original action, relator, the State Board of Education, sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, the State Auditor and the State Treasurer, to approve a salary increase for the Board's Superintendent. The Board urged that W. Va. Code, 6-7-2a (1989), which set the salaries of numerous executive officers, unconstitutionally fixed the salary of the Superintendent, the Board's appointee.


OVERVIEW: The Board contended that, under its constitutional authority generally to supervise public education, it, rather than the Legislature, was entitled to fix the salary of its appointee, the Superintendent, and that, therefore, the Legislature's attempt to set the Superintendent's salary in W. Va. Code, 6-7-2a (1989), was unconstitutional. The court noted that § 2 of Article XII of the West Virginia Constitution empowered the Board to select the Superintendent but that § 2 did not authorize the Board to set the Superintendent's salary. Section 8 of Article IV of the West Virginia Constitution vested authority to set the salaries of all state officers, including the Superintendent, in the West Virginia Legislature. The court rejected the Board's equitable argument that it was difficult to attract top-notch candidates to the Superintendent's position because the Legislature had set the salary at a substantially lower level than salaries paid to many county superintendents. The Legislature's having delegated to the Board the power to set the Superintendent's salary from 1958-1989 was not a permanent abdication of legislative authority to set salaries for state officials.


OUTCOME: The court denied the Board's petition for a writ of mandamus.

State ex rel. Hamrick v. LCS Servs.


No. 21958


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


193 W. Va. 111; 454 S.E.2d 405; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 260


October 4, 1994, Submitted  
December 16, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Berkeley County. Honorable Christopher C. Wilkes, Judge. Civil Action No. 90-C-366 & 90-C-711.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, IN PART, REVERSED, IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Berkeley County (West Virginia) enjoined appellant property owners from accepting waste at their landfill until the landfill received site approval from appellee county waste authority. The property owners challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The property owners were granted a permit to operate a solid waste facility prior to enactment of W. Va. Code § 20-9-12a (1989), which required a person to obtain a solid waste permit from the county waste authority. The property owners were enjoined from operating a landfill because they did not obtain the approval under a siting plan from the county authority. The court affirmed in part and reversed the judgment enjoining the property owners from operating the facility. The property owners applied for and received a permit to operate the landfill prior to the passage of § 20-9-12a. That section recognized that existing solid waste facilities that held valid permits could continue to operate. The statute operated only prospectively because the intent that it should operate retroactively was not clearly expressed by its terms or implied from the language of the statute. Finally, the property owners had a reasonable expectation to rely on the issued permit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in part and reversed the judgment in part as to the requirement that the property owners obtain a permit from the county waste authority.

State ex rel. Board of Educ. v. Bailey


No. 22167


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 534; 453 S.E.2d 368; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 263


September 27, 1994, Submitted  
December 15, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable A. Andrew MacQueen, Chief Judge. Civil Action No. 92-MISC-47.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, county boards of education, appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which denied their request in mandamus to declare W. Va. Code § 18A-4-5, as amended in 1988, unconstitutional. Respondents were the State Treasurer, the State Auditor, the West Virginia Board of Education, and the State Superintendent of Schools.


OVERVIEW: The county boards of education complained because the calculation of their annual state equity pay salary supplements were calculated taking into consideration "excess levies" that were in effect on January 1, but were not renewed by the counties, and expired on July 1. The circuit court determined that the 1988 amendments to W. Va. Code § 18A-4-5 (1985) were not unconstitutional, and refused the boards' request. On appeal, the court reversed the circuit court. The amendments to the statute were an unconstitutional violation of equal protection principles, and as such, failed to correct the defects noted by the court when it determined that the earlier version of the statute was unconstitutional. Determination of salary supplements based on whether the county could maintain its excess levy did not bear a relation to educational needs and treated counties that had no excess levies differently than those counties who did have excess levies that the voters did not renew.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

113 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Booth v. Sims


No. 22464


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


193 W. Va. 323; 456 S.E.2d 167; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 291


October 12, 1994, Submitted  
December 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Filed As Modified: March 24, 1995.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state police officers under the age of 50 who had over 20 years' service, brought an original mandamus action to challenge the constitutionality of certain amendments to the state's public safety pension plan under the contracts clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners claimed that the pension amendments unconstitutionally impaired the vested rights to which they were entitled before the new legislation. Respondents asserted that petitioners had no vested rights and that the amendments were reasonable because they guaranteed the future solvency of the public safety pension fund. Finding that petitioners clearly had property rights that could not be withdrawn because they were all state employees who had contributed into the fund and substantially relied to their detriment in investing more than half of their working lives with the state, the court held that legitimate expectations of government servants could not be confounded after those servants had partially performed their part of the bargain with the people, relied to their detriment, and foreclosed other career options. In short, the court held that the legislature simply could not alter the pension rights of state employees who had invested a substantial part of their working lives with the state. However, only W. Va. Code § 15-2-27a (1994) (reducing petitioners' cost-of-living adjustment) impaired the obligations of contract under W. Va. Const. art. III, § 4.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioners' writ of mandamus as molded.

 

114 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Lawrence v. Polan


No. 22590


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 629; 453 S.E.2d 612; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 246


November 29, 1994, Submitted  
December 12, 1994, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ Denied


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Commissioner of the Division of Tourism and Parks (commissioner) sought a writ of mandamus, requesting that the court find that respondent Secretary of the West Virginia Department of Administration (secretary) had a duty to process a purchase order regarding certain park development revenue bonds. The secretary questioned the legality of the bonds.


OVERVIEW: In this original proceeding in mandamus, the secretary questioned the legality of revenue bonds that the commissioner wanted to issue pursuant to W. Va. Code § 5B-1-13b (1985). The court found W. Va. Code § 5B-1-13b authorized the commissioner to issue revenue bonds, which were to be liquidated from a special fund derived from revenues from the park recreational facilities. However, the court held that such revenue bonds would violate W. Va. Const. art. X, § 4 if the park facilities operated at a net deficit and the only source of funds to liquidate the bonds was the general revenue fund of the legislature. As a result of the court's finding that the funding mechanism for repayment of the park revenue bonds violated the West Virginia Constitution, there was no duty on the secretary's part to act. Therefore the court held that there was no basis for issuing a writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ for mandamus sought by the commissioner to compel the secretary to process the purchase order for park development revenue bonds.

State ex rel. Lambert v. County Comm'n


No. 22371


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 448; 452 S.E.2d 906; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 208


September 14, 1994, Submitted  
December 9, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Mandamus.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Director of the Public Employees Insurance Agency (director) sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent litigants, who were various city or county government authorities or non-profit corporations, who elected to not participate in the Public Employees Insurance Agency (PEIA) to contribute to the cost of coverage for their retired employee who elected PEIA coverage. All the litigants elected to not participate in PEIA.


OVERVIEW: All the litigants elected to participate in the Public Employees Retirement System (PERS). Their participation was voluntary. One of the benefits accorded the litigants, because of their participation in PERS, was that the litigants' employees were eligible to elect PEIA coverage upon their retirement pursuant to the West Virginia Public Employees Insurance Act (Act), W. Va. Code 5-16-1 et seq. Thus, employers who elected to participate in PEIA were having to bear the cost of medical coverage for the retired employees of the litigants who elected PEIA as well as their own. The director requested the court issue a writ of mandamus compelling the litigants to make the contribution required under W. Va. Code § 5-16-22 (1992) because it was the litigants' participation in PERS which made their retired employee eligible for PEIA benefits. The court issued the writ, holding that: (1) the statutes governing PERS should be read in pari materia with the PEIA statutes; (2) § 5-16-22 did not violated the equal protection clause; and (3) § 5-16-22 was not preempted by the Employee Retirement Income Security Act of 1974, 29 U.S.C.S. § 1001 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court granted the director's request for a writ of mandamus to require the litigants to contribute to PEIA.

Stewart v. SMC, Inc.


No. 22163


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 441; 452 S.E.2d 899; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 212


September 27, 1994, Submitted  
December 9, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County Honorable John Hey, Judge. Civil Action No. 91-C-4231.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant real estate owners challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee good faith purchaser, holding that the purchaser had valid title to a certain parcel of real estate it purchased from the state at a tax sale. Appellants sought to set aside the tax deed and to have ownership of the real estate restored to them.


OVERVIEW: The owners had title to the real estate through inheritance. The property was listed in the wrong name by the county assessor. The sheriff's office taxed the real estate in the incorrect name, but the property taxes were paid annually. The previous owner died, the decedent died, and the taxes were not paid for a year. The sheriff sent certified mail notice of the delinquency to the last known name and address, and published the notice. The property was offered for sale, no one bid, and the sheriff took the property pursuant to W. Va. Code § 11A-3-6 (1941). The next year, the estate received notice of the delinquency, and paid that tax, but no one notified appellants that the property had been taken by the state, and that they had 18 months to redeem it or it would be sold for the school fund pursuant to W. Va. Code § 11A-4-3 (1947). The property was sold, and the owners filed their action. The circuit court granted summary judgment, and the owners appealed. The court affirmed the circuit court because the owners did not contest the affidavit that notice of the tax sale was sent according to § 11A-3-6, notice was established, and their due process rights were protected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

State ex rel. Frazier v. Meadows


No. 22333


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


193 W. Va. 20; 454 S.E.2d 65; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 231


September 13, 1994, Submitted  
December 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION FOR A WRIT OF MANDAMUS.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator judge sought a writ of mandamus requiring respondents, sheriff and county commission, to provide the judge with a qualified bailiff of the judge's choice who would work under his control and direct supervision.


OVERVIEW: The judge intended to hire a full-time replacement for his retiring bailiff. He informed respondents of his desire. In an effort to amicably conclude the matter, the parties decided that the judge would interview any deputy sheriff that applied, but could hire from the civilian population. Shortly thereafter, the chairperson of the county wage and hour review board denied the judge's request for a civilian bailiff because he believed statutory law and W. Va. Trial Ct. R. VII required denial of the request. The judge petitioned the court for a writ of mandamus requiring respondents to provide him with a qualified bailiff of the judge's choice. The court granted the judge's petition for writ of mandamus, finding the efficient administration of the judicial system was essential to its duty to implement justice. The court held that under the provisions of W. Va. Code § 51-3-5 and Rule VII, the sheriff of a county was charged with the duty of providing bailiffs. Notwithstanding, the court found a substantial, genuine, and irreconcilable conflict which required the court to assert its ultimate responsibility and authority.


OUTCOME: The court granted the judge's petition for a writ of mandamus requiring respondents to provide him with a qualified bailiff of his choice.

Smith v. Board of Educ.


No. 22154


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 321; 452 S.E.2d 412; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 218


September 27, 1994, Submitted  
December 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Paul Zakaib, Jr., Circuit Judge. Civil Action No. 92-AA-276.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) upholding the denial of his grievance before the Education and State Employees Grievance Board (the board) where he sought entitlement to the state equity supplement as a part of his substitute teacher remuneration.


OVERVIEW: The teacher argued that he had been underpaid based on the failure of the county board of education to include the State equity supplement in the calculation of his pay. The issue was whether State equity pay had to be included in the daily rate of pay of substitute teachers who did not teach more than 10 consecutive days in the same position. While the existence of conflicting opinions from two State superintendents raised a question of the precedential value to be accorded the opinions, the court gave great weight to the interpretation of the current superintendent because it was not clearly erroneous. The court concluded that the term "basic salaries" as defined in W. Va. Code § 18A-4-1 only referred to the corresponding amount of salary appearing in the minimum salary schedule amounts within W. Va. Code § 18A-4-2 and did not encompass any additional amounts, such as equity supplements. Therefore, the calculation of the daily amount of remuneration paid to the substitute teacher did not include an amount for the State equity supplement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

Donley v. Bracken


No. 22254


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 383; 452 S.E.2d 699; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 234


September 14, 1994, Submitted  
December 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ohio County. Honorable W. Craig Broadwater, Judge. Civil Action No. 92-C-775.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Ohio County (West Virginia), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, physicians, a medical partnership, and a hospital, in the parents' medical malpractice action for injuries suffered by their daughter during her delivery.


OVERVIEW: The daughter was deprived of oxygen when she was born, suffered brain damage, and developed cerebral palsy. Her parents filed this action asserting a claim on her behalf, together with their own derivative claims, over 20 years after the daughter's birth. The trial court granted summary judgment to the physicians, the medical partnership, and the hospital because the claims were not brought within the 20-year limitations period set forth in W. Va. Code § 55-2-15 (1923). On appeal, the parents contended that § 55-2-15 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment and held that § 55-2-15 was constitutional. The court further held that in order for a permanently incompetent person to maintain a viable and timely action under § 55-2-15, the lawsuit had to be brought within 20 years of the date of the wrongful act and the injury. Furthermore, the 20-year cap was reasonably related to the legislative goal of preventing stale law suits, and the failure to impose a similar cap on competent persons did not adversely discriminate against the mentally disabled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which granted summary judgment to the physicians, the medical partnership, and the hospital.
