State v. Hopkins


No. 22079


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 483; 453 S.E.2d 317; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 226


September 21, 1994, Submitted  
December 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Raleigh County. Honorable Thomas Canterbury, Judge Criminal Case No. 93-F-371.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Raleigh County (West Virginia), which convicted him of shoplifting, did not sever evidence of defendant's prior shoplifting convictions, and imposed a $ 50 fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the circuit court's decision to convict him of shoplifting, arguing that the circuit court improperly used his prior uncounseled shoplifting convictions to enhance his sentence. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because the circuit court was not prohibited from considering defendant's previous valid and uncounseled misdemeanor convictions in sentencing him for the subsequent offense and imposing a fine. The court found that the circuit court's decision that defendant's statements were spontaneous and not the result of an interrogation was not "plainly wrong or clearly against the weight of the evidence." The court determined that evidence of defendant's prior convictions was a necessary element of the crime charged so the evidence was admissible for jury purposes. The court overruled State v. Armstrong, 175 W. Va. 381, 332 S.E.2d 837 (1985), holding that defendant's prior convictions, which were valid because no prison term was imposed, were also valid to enhance punishment. The court did not find error in the record to indicate that defendant's fines were excessive, shocking, violative of fundamental fairness, or disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's conviction of defendant because the circuit court was not prohibited from considering defendant's previous valid and uncounseled misdemeanor convictions in sentencing him for the subsequent offense and imposing a fine. The court determined that evidence of defendant's prior convictions was admissible because such evidence was a necessary element of the crime charged.

State v. Derr


No. 22101


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 165; 451 S.E.2d 731; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 176


September 14, 1994, Submitted  
November 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marshall County. Honorable Steven D. Narick, Judge. Criminal Indictment No. 90-F-59.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Marshall County (West Virginia) sentenced defendant to life without mercy for first degree murder, to not less than 2 nor more than 10 years for malicious assault, and to 2 sentences of not less than 15 nor more than 25 years for 2 counts of first degree sexual assault, all to run consecutive to each other. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, malicious assault, and two counts of first degree sexual assault in a highly publicized case. He appealed, asserting, inter alia, that the trial court erred 1) by denying his request for a change of venue, 2) by failing to individually voir dire jurors who showed potential bias and prejudice, 3) by permitting the prosecution to introduce two autopsy photographs of the deceased victim, and 4) by permitting Fred Zain to testify concerning DNA tests performed by another person. The court held 1) a change of venue was not needed because the jurors only indicated mere knowledge of the case, but stated that they could judge impartially the defendant's guilt or innocence, 2) individual voir dire was not necessary where defense counsel failed to renew his request to conduct individual voir dire after learning all the jurors were familiar with the case, 3) the gruesome photograph rule of State v. Rowe was overruled for failing to comply with the West Virginia Rules of Evidence, 4) the photographs were admissible because they were in no way unfairly prejudicial, and 5) defendant's Zain challenge was properly made in a habeas corpus petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the final order, noting that defendant could seek post-conviction habeas corpus relief with regard to false evidence submitted against him.

In re Hey


No. 21676


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 221; 452 S.E.2d 24; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 191


September 13, 1994, Submitted  
November 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Disciplinary Proceeding.



DISPOSITION: COMPLAINT DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Special Judicial Hearing Board (West Virginia), recommended the dismissal of the Judicial Investigation Commission finding that probable cause existed to file a complaint against a judge based upon purported violations of W. Va. Judicial Code of Ethics Canons 1, 2A, 3A(6). The judge argued that any adverse decision against him would have violated his rights under U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: The judge was publicly censured for discussing a pending case on television. On the day following his censure, the judge appeared on a local radio station and discussed his own disciplinary proceeding, criticized a member of his investigative panel, and stated his intention to take some reactive measure. The Judicial Investigation Commission determined that probable cause existed to file a complaint against the judge based upon alleged violations of W. Va. Judicial Code of Ethics Canons 1, 2A, 3A(6). The Special Judicial Hearing Board however, determined that the evidence was insufficient to support the complaint. The court held that, consistent with U.S. Const. amend. I and W. Va. art. III, § 7, the general prohibitions in Canons 1, 2, 3 could not be used to punish judges for their public remarks that did not concern a pending or impending matter and that did not violate the law or a specific prohibition. The court stated there was no persuasive evidence which showed the judge's comments conveyed a physical or otherwise improper threat. The judge's conduct did not rise to the level of being deceptive, illegal, or a flagrant abuse of power.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the complaint filed against the judge for alleged ethical violations.

 

123 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. State Farm Fire & Casualty Co. v. Madden


No. 22350, No. 22351


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 155; 451 S.E.2d 721; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 157


September 13, 1994, Submitted  
October 28, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] WRITS OF PROHIBITION.



DISPOSITION: WRITS GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Marshall County (West Virginia) allowed an individual to amend his personal injury complaint and join claims against petitioners, insurer and adjuster, for bad faith and unfair insurance practices, denied petitioner insured's motion to bifurcate claims based on the underlying claim's investigation and adjustment, and issued discovery orders and sanctions. The restaurant, insurer, and adjuster sought writs of prohibition.


OVERVIEW: The court held that amendment was proper under W. Va. R. Civ. P. 15, because an insurer could be joined as a defendant by an injured plaintiff alleging claims of bad faith and unfair insurance practices, W. Va. R. Civ. P. 18(b); however, the prejudice to the insured inherent in allowing the claims to be tried together required that proceedings and discovery on the insurance practices claims be stayed. Prejudice also required a separate trial for claims against the insured arising out of the investigation and adjustment of the underlying claim. W. Va. R. Civ. P. 42(c). The court held that the sanctions ordered by the circuit court after it found that the investigator contacted the individual without permission, in violation of W. Va. R. Prof. Conduct 4.2, 5.3, and engaged in illegal and unethical surveillance, were too broad. The court held that the circuit court abused its discretion by foreclosing cross-examination of the individual regarding activities that the investigator legally observed because even illegally obtained evidence was admissible for impeachment purposes and by barring the investigator's testimony about events that he legally and ethically observed.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writs of prohibition as modified. The court held that the amendment was properly granted, stayed proceedings and discovery regarding the bad faith and unfair practices claim, ordered a bifurcated trial and prohibited discovery on claims against the insured arising out of the investigation and adjustment of the underlying claim, and held that sanctions imposed for illegal and unethical surveillance were overly broad.

Kyriazis v. University of W. Va.


No. 22086


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 60; 450 S.E.2d 649; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 161


October 4, 1994, Submitted  
October 28, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Monongalia County. Honorable Larry V. Starcher, Judge. Civil Action No. 92-C-328.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party sought review of the summary judgment awarded by the Circuit Court of Monongalia County (West Virginia) in favor of defendant state university on the basis that an anticipatory release signed by plaintiff was an absolute bar to his claim for injuries sustained while playing rugby.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured party joined defendant state university's rugby club. Plaintiff signed an anticipatory release. After plaintiff was injured while playing rugby, he sought recovery of damages from defendant. The trial court held that the anticipatory release was an absolute bar to plaintiff's claim and granted summary judgment to defendant. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case. The court held that the anticipatory release violated public policy because defendant qualified as a public service and possessed a decisive bargaining advantage over plaintiff when he executed the release. By conditioning student participation in certain clubs upon execution of the anticipatory release, without demanding the same from students involved in other activities, defendant treated similarly situated persons differently. Thus, the release violated the West Virginia Constitution Equal Protection Clause and it also impermissibly interfered with plaintiff's right to a "certain remedy" pursuant to W. Va. Const. art. III, § 17.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment awarded by the trial court to defendant state university on plaintiff injured party's action for personal injuries suffered while playing rugby. The anticipatory release signed by plaintiff did not bar recovery because it violated public policy, equal protection rights, and "certain remedy" principles.

McGraw v. Caperton


No. 22011


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 528; 446 S.E.2d 921; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 54


March 1, 1994, Submitted  
July 21, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 6, 1994. Opinion Modified July 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable John Hey, Judge. Civil Action No. 93-C-5106



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Attorney General of West Virginia, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) that dismissed his declaratory judgment action finding that he, in his official capacity, was not empowered under the state constitution or the state statutes to institute a declaratory judgment action as a plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: The Attorney General filed a declaratory judgment against appellees, state officials, pursuant to W. Va. Code § 55-13-1 et seq. (1993). He sought a determination of his rights and responsibilities under W. Va. Code § 5A-3-13, which required that he approve state contracts as to form. He also sought a ruling as to the constitutionality of two computer contracts. He later appealed from the dismissal of his action. The court affirmed. It held that the Attorney General, acting in his official capacity, did not come within the parameters of the definition of "person" set forth in W. Va. Code § 55-13-13 and was not entitled to bring a declaratory judgment action pursuant to W. Va. Code § 55-13-2. Although the case was otherwise moot, the court decided the constitutional issue, which was whether certain one-year contracts with nine options to renew were constitutional. The court held that a one-year contract with multiple renewals did not violate constitutional or statutory provisions as they did not create the type of debt prohibited in W.Va. Const. Art. X, § 4 or W. Va. Code § 12-3-17. As such, there was no need to rebid the contract every time a renewal occurred.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and remanded in the Attorney General's action for a declaratory judgment.

Write-In Pritt Campaign v. Hechler


No. 22394


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 677; 447 S.E.2d 612; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 137


July 20, 1994, Submitted  
July 21, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Refused August 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certified Questions.



DISPOSITION: QUESTIONS ANSWERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) certified two questions as to whether a duly organized political action committee (PAC) was an affiliation of voters pursuant to West Virginia Code § 3-1-8 (1994) and whether respondent, the West Virginia Secretary of State, was required by law to recognize an affiliation of voters as an independent political party.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, the co-chairmen of a write-in campaign for a gubernatorial candidate, instituted a declaratory judgment action in the circuit court for determining whether the write-in campaign, in its capacity as a PAC, was a political party that fell within § 3-1-8. The candidate, who was a member of a major political party, had received 7.4 percent of the votes in a general election. The circuit court certified two questions to the court: 1) whether a PAC was an affiliation of voters as that term was used in § 3-1-8 and 2) whether the Secretary was required to recognize it as an independent political party. The court answered both questions in the negative. The court found that the State had a legitimate interest in overseeing the elective process to ensure that it functioned smoothly. It also noted that the candidate was taking great pains to disassociate herself from petitioners and that she had never authorized the write-in campaign to take any action on her behalf. No evidence suggested that the persons voting for the candidate wished to be affiliated with the write-in campaign's efforts. Nothing suggested that those votes intended to become members of a new party.


OUTCOME: The court answered the two certified questions in the negative, holding that a PAC did not qualify as an affiliation of voters representing any principle or organization. The court then dismissed the case.

State ex rel. Lambert v. West Va. State Bd. of Educ.


No. 22225


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 700; 447 S.E.2d 901; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 142


June 28, 1994, Submitted  
July 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Mandamus.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED IN PART;

DENIED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a student and her parents, sought a writ of mandamus against respondents, the West Virginia State Board of Education (Board) and the West Virginia Secondary School Activities Commission (SSAC), to compel the Board to exercise authority over extracurricular activities, to declare W. Va. Code § 18-2-25 (1994) unconstitutional, to provide a signer for the student, and to schedule girls' basketball in the traditional winter season.


OVERVIEW: The student, who had been deaf since birth, had a signer for her basic courses but was not provided a signer for her extracurricular activities. The parents asked the student's basketball coach about providing a signer but did not make that request to the director of special education for the county. The court held that, when a student had a disability requiring special assistance or services to enable participation in school-sanctioned extracurricular activities, a request for assistance or services could be made on the student's behalf to any school official familiar with the student's needs. That school official then had the responsibility to inform the county board of education's director of special education of the request so that appropriate action could be taken. Second, the scheduling of girls' basketball in the nontraditional season constituted a "mere superficial equivalency" to the boys' team and served no important governmental objective. Thus, it was unconstitutional as it violated the equal protection clause set forth in Article III, § 10 of the West Virginia Constitution. Finally, the court held that W.Va. Code § 18-2-25 (1994) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ sought by the student and her parents with regard to the signer and the girls' basketball season; however, the court denied the writ as it related to the constitutionality of W. Va. Code § 18-2-25 (1994). The court directed the Board to submit to the court its plan to change the girls' basketball season to the winter and to provide the student with a signer.

State ex rel. Holmes v. Gainer


No. 22226


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 686; 447 S.E.2d 887; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 140


June 7, 1994, Submitted  
July 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissenting Opinion Dated July 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writs of Mandamus and Prohibition.



DISPOSITION: WRITS GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator clerks of the West Virginia legislature petitioned for a writ of mandamus against respondent auditor of West Virginia to issue warrants for the payment of legislators' salaries and expenses pursuant to W.Va. Const. art. VI, § 33 and W.Va. H. Bill 4031 (bill), and for a writ of prohibition against respondent judge to refrain from hearing a declaratory judgment action pending in the circuit court that involved the same matters.


OVERVIEW: In 1994, the Citizens Legislative Compensation Commission submitted a resolution to the Vest Virginia Legislature to increase the legislators' compensation and expense allowances pursuant to W.Va. Const. art. VI, § 33. The resolution was enacted in the bill, which amended W. Va. Code § 4-2A-1 et seq., and the governor signed the bill into law. The auditor of West Virginia and intervenor citizens argued that the requirements for setting legislative compensation and expense allowances under W.Va. Const. art. VI, § 33 were not properly followed and that contact by legislators with members of the commission violated due process. The court granted the writs of mandamus and prohibition and held that although the commission and the Legislature failed to follow the provisions of § 33, which provided that a resolution to change compensation was only properly submitted to the Legislature every four years, the court refused to apply its interpretation of § 33 retroactively in light of an attorney general opinion to the contrary. The court also refused to impose a judicial prohibition fashioned under a due process rubric on ex parte communications to informal administrative proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus and directed the auditor to process the legislative compensation and expense allowances in accordance with the terms contained in the bill. The court also issued a writ of prohibition against the judge and directed the judge to proceed no further with the declaratory judgment action involving the same issues resolved in the court's opinion.

State v. Lewis


No. 21835


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 635; 447 S.E.2d 570; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 149


January 12, 1994, Submitted  
July 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Mercer County. Honorable John R. Frazier, Circuit Judge. Criminal Action No. 91-FE-169.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Mercer County (West Virginia) entered judgment convicting defendant of third offense shoplifting and sentenced defendant to an indeterminate term of not less than one nor more than ten years in the penitentiary and fined $ 500 pursuant to W. Va. Code § 61-3A-3(c). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed placing pork products and a spice into her purse while she was shopping in a supermarket. While she paid for the items she placed in her cart at the checkout counter, she did not remove or pay for the pork and the spice. At the time, defendant was on probation for second offense shoplifting. She was later indicted for the felony of third offense shoplifting. On appeal of defendant's subsequent conviction on that charge, she asserted the circuit court failed to accept a proffered plea agreement, failed to reduce the charges from third offense to second offense on the grounds that some of her prior convictions were uncounseled, and failed to permit alternate sentencing in view of her health conditions and the nonviolent nature of the offense. The court reversed the sentence imposed because § 61-3A-3(c) violated the cruel and unusual proscription of the Eighth Amendment and W. Va. Const. Art. III, § 5 by imposing a disproportionate sentence to the crime committed by expressly prohibiting probation and implicitly prohibiting alternative sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the sentence imposed upon defendant and remand the case for consideration by the circuit court of the alternative sentencing requested by defendant.

State v. Day


No. 21884


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 641; 447 S.E.2d 576; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 153


June 7, 1994, Submitted  
July 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Raleigh County. Honorable John C. Ashworth, Judge. Criminal Case Nos. 92-F-344, 92-AP-4269, and 4270.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Raleigh County (West Virginia), which convicted him of five counts of third offense shoplifting and one count of obstructing an officer. Defendant also challenged the trial court's decision to impose fines as part of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of five counts of third offense shoplifting and one count of obstructing an officer. Defendant was sentenced to terms of 1 to 10 years and was ordered to pay fines. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found that an out-of-court-identification of defendant was properly admitted even though the witness was shown an off-centered photographic lineup where the record indicated the witnesses' out-of court and in-court identifications were not based on the off-centered photographs and there was sufficient evidence the identifications were reliable. The court held that the trial court did not error by admitting videotapes of the shoplifting incidents into evidence because there was sufficient evidence the videotapes had not been altered or changed. The court determined that a prior conviction of defendant's was appropriately used for enhancement purposes where defendant admitted to an earlier shoplifting offense and defendant failed to show that his prior conviction was unlawfully obtained. The court concluded a mandatory fine imposed against defendant under W. Va. Code § 61-3A-3(d) (1981) was not unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of five counts of third offense shoplifting and one count of obstructing an officer.

State ex rel. Clarksburg Mun. Bldg. Comm'n v. Spelsberg


No. 22312


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 553; 447 S.E.2d 16; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 146


June 28, 1994, Submitted  
July 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] WRIT OF MANDAMUS.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, Clarksburg Municipal Building Commission (commission) and City Council of the City of Clarksburg (council), sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent secretary of the commission, to execute, on behalf of the City of Clarksburg, an agreement and lease (agreement), between the city and the commission, which would have enabled the city to have financing to build a new city hall and municipal building.


OVERVIEW: The council determined that the existing city hall and municipal building, which were over 100 years old, were obsolete and not economically repairable, and that new buildings were in the public interest. The commission secured a financing commitment and sought to issue bonds. The agreement sought by petitioners specified that the city would make monthly rental payments to the commission for use of the new buildings. This money was to be used by the commission to retire the bonds. Petitioners filed for a writ of mandamus to compel the secretary to execute the agreement, arguing that that the agreement was necessary to finance the new buildings. The secretary refused to execute the agreement until the court determined whether the agreement created an unconstitutional debt in violation of the W. Va. Const. art. X, § 8, or in violation of W. Va. Code § 11-8-26 (1963). The court granted the writ of mandamus sought by petitioners, concluding that the bonds at issue did not violate the Virginia Constitution or § 11-8-26. The court found that the agreement posed no threat to the future indebtedness of the state or the city, and it offered a way to finance a much needed project.


OUTCOME: The court granted to petitioners a writ of mandamus to compel the secretary to execute the agreement.

 

132 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Harrison v. Town of Eleanor


No. 21886


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 611; 447 S.E.2d 546; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 130


January 12, 1994, Submitted  
July 15, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Putnam County. Honorable Clarence L. Watt, Circuit Judge. Civil Action No. 87-C-100.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Putnam County (West Virginia), which denied its motion for a new trial or judgment notwithstanding the verdict after appellee landowner was awarded damages in a dispute involving the revocation of building permits under an ordinance. The landowner filed a declaratory judgment action and amended his complaint to include a damages claim. The declaratory judgment action was not resolved.


OVERVIEW: The town revoked the landowner's building permits because he had not complied with Town of Eleanor, W. Va., Ordinance No. 75-2, which required a 20 foot setback from the street and abutting properties for construction of residential dwellings. The landowner filed a declaratory judgment action regarding the validity of the ordinance. He amended his complaint to include a claim for money damages. The jury awarded damages to the landowner, but the declaratory judgment claim was never resolved. The town's motion for a new trial or judgment notwithstanding the verdict was denied. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded and concluded that the trial court erroneously allowed questions of law to be decided by the jury and failed to resolve the questions of law as to whether the disputed ordinance was either a building ordinance or a zoning ordinances. The court concluded that it was a building ordinance, which had been properly enacted. The original issuance of the permits to the landowner was in violation of the ordinance, and, thus, those permits were void. The town was not bound by the original issuance; thus, the landowner could not maintain a contractual theory of liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order, which had denied the town's motion for new trial or judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The court concluded that the trial court erred in allowing questions of law to be decided by the jury, and in failing to resolve the questions of law as to whether the disputed ordinance was either a building ordinance or a zoning ordinances.

 

133 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Putnam County Fire Serv. Bd. v. Kelly


No. 22044


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


192 W. Va. 37; 449 S.E.2d 508; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 109


May 11, 1994, Submitted  
July 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certified Question from the Circuit Court of Putnam County. Civil Action No.'s 90-C-849; 90-C-774; 90-C-775; 90-C-772; 90-C-766; 90-C-721; 90-C-784; 90-C-786; 90-C-785; 90-C-773; 90-C-763 CERTIFIED QUESTION ANSWERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Putnam County Fire Service Board instituted civil suits to collect delinquent fire service fees owed by defendant realty owners pursuant to the Putnam County Fire Service User Fee Ordinance and West Virginia Code § 7-17-12 (1984). Defendants subsequently removed the cases to the Circuit Court of Putnam County and challenged the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the fifteen-day limitation period formerly established by § 7-17-12 for opponents of a fire service fee ordinance to file petitions in protest of the ordinance in order to obtain ballot access was constitutional. The circuit court certified a question as to the constitutionality of the ordinance and answered it in the affirmative, finding the ordinance unconstitutional. Plaintiff sought review. Plaintiff argued that the fifteen-day limitation period mandated by West Virginia Code § 7-17-12 was clear, unambiguous, imperative and constitutional. Plaintiff also maintained that the circuit court's ruling that the limitation period was unduly restrictive was arbitrary, capricious and plainly wrong. Defendants contended that the limitation period burdened the right of individuals to associate and to have access to the ballot box. The court found that § 7-17-12 was deliberately designed to make the initiation of a fire service fee ordinance comparatively simple, while at the same time making it difficult for taxpayers to call for a referendum. The limitation period for filing did not infringe on a fundamental right requiring a compelling state interest be shown.


OUTCOME: The certified question was answered and the case was dismissed.

 

134 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Robb v. Caperton


No. 22310


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 492; 446 S.E.2d 714; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 107


June 28, 1994, Submitted  
July 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Mandamus.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator state political party chairman brought an original action in the nature of a petition for writ of mandamus to compel respondent state governor to issue a directive to schedule an election for a vacant judicial office.


OVERVIEW: The chairman brought an action in mandamus to compel the governor to issue a directive causing a vacancy in the office of a circuit judge to be filled by election. The chairman argued that the governor was required to have the vacancy filled at the next general election by virtue of W. Va. Const. art. IV, §§ 7 and 8, which generally provided for vacancies on the seats of state and county officers to be filled in the interim by appointment, and thereafter at the next general election. The governor argued that he was permitted, if he so chose, to wait for two years before scheduling such election, by virtue of W. Va. Const. art. VIII, § 7, which specifically provided for the filling of vacancies in the office of, inter alia, circuit judge. The court held that the governor's position prevailed, because under principles of constitutional construction, just as with statutory construction, where provisions were in conflict, the provision with greater specificity prevailed over the more general provision. Thus, the governor was not required to fill the judicial office at the next general election.


OUTCOME: The court denied the chairman's petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the governor to schedule the judicial election.

 

135 of 754 DOCUMENTS


In re Maple Meadow Mining Co.


No. 21900


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 519; 446 S.E.2d 912; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 104


May 11, 1994, Submitted  
July 8, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissenting Opinion Dated July 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Raleigh County. Honorable John C. Ashworth, Judge. Civil Action No. 92-AD-361-A.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Raleigh County (West Virginia), which affirmed the tax assessment of appellee county assessor against the taxpayer's real property, which consisted of coal reserves. The taxpayer sought a reduction of the assessment under the Fair and Equitable Property Valuation Act, W. Va. Code § 11-1C-1, et seq.


OVERVIEW: The Act recognized that a sufficient amount of real property and personal property was undervalued for tax purposes, and sought to remedy the problem by the imposition of a requirement that all taxable property be reassessed. The Act required that all property was to be assessed at 60 percent of its value by the end of a three year period, W. Va. Code § 11-1C-1(d) (1990). The Act allowed assessor to gradually implement the percentage, W. Va. Code § 11-1C-7(d). The taxpayer's natural resource property was assessed at 60 percent prior to the implementation of the Act. The taxpayer asserted that the county valuation plans permitted by the Act, § 11-1C-7(d), violated his right to equal protection under W. Va. Const. art. X, § 2 and uniform taxation under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 because it allowed other county property to be assessed at lesser percentage of value. The taxpayer asserted that it was entitled to a reduced rate. On appeal of the affirmance of the assessment, the court held that the assessor was not required to make a downward adjustment to the value of taxpayer's property. The assessor had properly followed the legislative mandates from the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's affirmance of the assessor's refusal to reduce the tax assessment against the taxpayer.

Dyke v. City of Parkersburg


No. 21871


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 418; 446 S.E.2d 506; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 93


May 11, 1994, Submitted  
June 16, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wood County. Honorable George W. Hill, Judge. Civil Action No. 91-C-1164



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Wood County (West Virginia), which granted the motion to dismiss that was filed by appellee city, pursuant to W.Va. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6), in the officer's action that sought reimbursement for expenses associated with his defense when the officer was found not guilty of the charge of sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: After the officer was found not guilty of a charge of sexual assault while on duty, the officer requested that the city reimburse him for the expenses of his defense. The city refused the officer's request, and the officer filed an action against the city seeking reimbursement. The trial court dismissed the officer's action, pursuant to W.Va. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6), and the officer sought review. On appeal, the city contended that the Governmental Tort Claims and Insurance Reform Act (Act), W.Va. Code § 29- 12A-1 et seq. (1992), did not provide for reimbursement of attorneys' fees in criminal proceedings, and that, even if it did, the charge against the officer was manifestly outside the scope of employment. The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the Act did not apply in a criminal proceeding. However, the court reversed the dismissal of the officer's action, holding that the officer was entitled to indemnification if the sexual assault charge developed from a discharge of his official duty, if the officer acted in good faith, and if the city had the authority to indemnify the employee. The court remanded for a determination of whether the officer met these requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that dismissed the officer's action that sought reimbursement by the city for the expenses of his defense that resulted in a finding of not guilty of the charge of sexual assault while on duty. The court remanded the matter for a hearing to be held before the police civil service commission for a determination of whether the officer's attorneys' fees should be reimbursed.

 

137 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Hunter v. Christian


No. 21895


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 390; 446 S.E.2d 177; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 97


May 11, 1994, Submitted  
June 16, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Logan County. Honorable Eric O'Briant, Judge. Civil Action No. 92-C-450



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Logan County (West Virginia) that granted appellee father one-half of the net proceeds collected in the wrongful death action filed by the mother on behalf of the estate of her daughter after it determined that the father was the biological parent.


OVERVIEW: After the mother gave birth to the daughter, the father extended neither emotional or financial support to the daughter during her lifetime. When the daughter was killed in an automobile accident, the mother filed a wrongful death action on her behalf, and the father, who had previously denied that he was the parent to avoid the legal obligation of paying child support and whose paternity had never been judicially determined, filed a motion to intervene. The results of testing established that he was the biological father, and the trial court granted the father's motion for summary judgment and awarded him one-half of the net proceeds of the wrongful death settlement. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the father was equitably estopped from asserting his paternity and from reaping the financial benefits from the daughter's death. Although the court found that estoppel should be applied cautiously, it concluded that this was clearly a case where it should be applied due to the father's disavowal of paternity in order to escape legal and financial responsibility during the daughter's lifetime.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that granted the father one-half of the net proceeds collected in the wrongful death action filed by the mother on behalf of the estate of her daughter.

State ex rel. Marockie v. Wagoner


No. 22214


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 458; 446 S.E.2d 680; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 90


May 11, 1994, Submitted  
June 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] WRIT GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State Superintendent of Schools and President of the a West Virginia School Building Authority (superintendent) sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent Secretary of the West Virginia School Board (secretary) to provide notice of a special meeting of the school board.


OVERVIEW: The superintendent sought a writ of mandamus to compel the secretary to provide notice of a special meeting of the school board called by the superintendent for the purpose of acting upon resolutions authorizing the issuance of the revenue bonds authorized in a state senate bill. The court held that the superintendent had the authority to call a special meeting under By-Laws of the School Building Authority of West Virginia, art. III, § 5 (1991) and that the secretary had a ministerial duty to give notice of any regular or special meeting under By-Laws of the School Building Authority of West Virginia, art. III, § 6 (1991). The court found that the writ of mandamus was adequate a remedy to compel the secretary to give notice of the special meeting and that because the secretary had a duty to comply with the superintendent's request, mandamus was the proper remedy, and the writ was granted.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus.

State v. Walls


No. 21691


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 332; 445 S.E.2d 515; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 80


January 19, 1994, Submitted  
May 27, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Logan County Honorable Eric H. O'Briant, Judge Criminal. Indictment No. 91-F-63.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Logan County (West Virginia), which convicted him of murder and malicious assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and malicious assault in the death of his stepfather. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that based upon the testimony of a psychiatrist who stated that defendant did not suffer from schizophrenia, and the testimony of lay witnesses who indicated that defendant appeared normal to them, there was sufficient evidence adduced at trial by which the jury could have found that defendant was sane at the time that he committed the murder. The court found that although there was testimony from three doctors who believed that defendant was not criminally responsible, the evidence produced by the state was sufficient to prove that defendant was sane at the time of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and malicious assault.

State ex rel. Shamblin v. Collier


No. 22008


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 349; 445 S.E.2d 736; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 73


January 11, 1994, Submitted  
May 23, 1994, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner elderly father sought a writ of habeas corpus to dissolve the committee appointment of respondent daughter, following a determination of his incompetency by respondent Jackson County Commission (commission) pursuant to W. Va. Code § 27-11-1 (1992). He alleged that his right to liberty under W. Va. Const. art. III, § 10 was violated, as well as his due process rights.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to W. Va. Code § 27-11-1 (1992), the commissioner made a determination of incompetency and appointed the elderly father's daughter as committee. The elderly father sought a writ of habeas corpus to dissolve the appointment, and argued that his constitutional rights to liberty and due process had been violated. The court granted the writ, and concluded that the evidence was insufficient to support the commission's determination. The elderly father had not been present at the determination hearing. The court held that commitment determination could not have been summarily made, but must have been established through clear and convincing evidence. Advanced age and past physical problems did not meet the statutory requirements for incompetency. The incompetency laws had been revised subsequent to the commission's determination, and W. Va. Code. ch. 44, the West Virginia Guardianship and Conservatorship Act, provided for more appropriate procedures. The case was remanded to the circuit court for a proper determination of the elderly father's incompetency.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of habeas corpus to permit the case to be remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings regarding a determination of petitioner's incompetency. The court concluded that the evidence was insufficient to support the commission's incompetency determination.

Skaff v. West Va. Human Rights Comm'n


No. 21869


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 161; 444 S.E.2d 39; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 50


March 8, 1994, Submitted  
April 20, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Human Rights Commission.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Secretary of the West Virginia Department of Public Safety and correctional officers, sought review of the decision of appellee West Virginia Human Rights Commission (HRC), which determined that it had jurisdiction to accept complaints of racial discrimination by appellee inmates in the state's penal institutions.


OVERVIEW: The basis for the HRC's assumption of jurisdiction of complaints of racial discrimination by inmates was its belief that the state's penal institutions were places of public accommodations, as defined in W. Va. Code § 5-11-3(j) (1992). The HRC reasoned that under W. Va. Code § 5-11-9(6)(A) (1992) racial discrimination was not permitted. The inmates, two black men imprisoned at the Huttonsville Correctional Center, alleged in the underlying complaint that the prison administration did not protect black inmates from physical violence inflicted by white inmates who belonged to a supremacist group called the Aryan Brotherhood. On appeal, the court held that the state's penal institutions were not places of public accommodations for prisoners housed therein. Therefore, the inmates' claims of discrimination were not under the jurisdiction of the HRC. However, the court pointed out that the inmates would have other relief available to them. The inmates had a right to request relief by writ of habeas corpus under the Eighth and Fourteenth amendments. The court also noted that state courts had concurrent jurisdiction to handle suits by prison inmates under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Human Rights Commission accepting jurisdiction of the complaints of racial discrimination by the inmates. The court also pointed out the relief available to the inmates by habeas corpus under the Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.

 

142 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jenkins


No. 21775


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 87; 443 S.E.2d 244; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 40


January 12, 1994, Submitted  
March 25, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lincoln County. The Honorable W. Jack Stevens, Judge. Criminal Indictment No. 90-F-44.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Lincoln County (West Virginia), which denied his motion to set aside a jury verdict finding him guilty of first degree murder without a recommendation of mercy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder without a recommendation of mercy. The court reversed, holding that a jury instruction in a first degree murder case that informed the jury that malice need not be shown on the part of defendant against the deceased was erroneous. The court also held that it was erroneous in a first degree murder case to instruct the jury that if defendant killed the deceased with the use of a deadly weapon, then intent, malice, willfulness, deliberation, and premeditation could be inferred from that fact where there was evidence that defendant's actions were based on some legal excuse, justification, or provocation. The trial court also erred in refusing defendant's request to advise the jury as to the consequences of a recommendation of mercy. The court held that there was no error in refusing to permit defendant to impeach a prosecution witness with the witness's prior conviction of receiving stolen property because the crime was a misdemeanor punishable by imprisonment for a term not to exceed one year and was not based on facts showing deceitfulness or falsification; thus, the conviction was not admissible under W. Va. R. Evid. 609(a)(2)(A).


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for first degree murder because the trial court committed reversible error with regard to its instruction to the jury on the issue of malice toward the deceased and on the effect of the use of a deadly weapon in establishing the elements of the offense, and in refusing defendant's request to advise the jury as to the consequences of a recommendation of mercy. The court remanded for a new trial.

Brown v. Mierke


No. 21923


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 120; 443 S.E.2d 462; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 34; 18 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1782


January 25, 1994, Submitted  
March 24, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Andrew A. MacQueen, Judge. Civil Action No. 90-C-3341.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff military retirees' declaratory judgment action against defendant state tax commissioner, the tax commissioner appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which held that a West Virginia tax scheme that taxed federal military pensions while exempting certain state retirement benefits discriminated against military retirees in violation of 4 U.S.C.S. § 111.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the military retirees had failed to demonstrate that their job descriptions during any substantial part of their active service corresponded to the job descriptions of the exempted state employees. The court held that there was no intent in the West Virginia scheme to discriminate against federal retirees; rather, the intent was to give a benefit to a very narrow class of former state and local employees. The court specifically found that retired military personnel were treated more favorably than West Virginians who had retired from civilian occupations, that retired military personnel were treated equally with all persons retired from the West Virginia Public Employees Retirement System and the West Virginia Teachers Retirement System, and that military retirees were treated substantially more favorably than persons retired from the West Virginia Judicial Retirement System. Therefore, the court found it extraordinarily difficult to infer that any of the pernicious dynamics that either the ancient doctrine of intergovernmental tax immunity or 4 U.S.C.S. § 111 were designed to remedy was implicated in the state tax scheme.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

144 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Council of Charleston v. Hall


No. 22067


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


190 W. Va. 665; 441 S.E.2d 386; 1994 W. Va. LEXIS 5


January 11, 1994, Submitted  
February 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Mandamus



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a city council and a waste services company, sought mandamus relief against respondent mayor to compel the mayor to sign a waste disposal agreement with the company. The mayor refused to sign the agreement until the court determined whether such agreement would have created an unconstitutional debt in violation of W. Va. Const. art. X, § 8 or W. Va. Code § 11-8-26 (1963).


OVERVIEW: The city contracted with a company to provide waste disposal services. The contract provided that the city would buy back the company's improvements if the agreement was prematurely terminated for specified reasons. The city mayor refused to sign the agreement due to a concern that it would create an unlawful debt in violation of W. Va. Const. art. X, § 8 or W. Va. Code § 11-8-26 (1963). The city council sought mandamus to compel the mayor to sign the agreement. The court granted mandamus relief, holding that the agreement did not violate the constitution or statute. The contract only created an obligation that matured periodically as each installment came due. Therefore, the contract would not be illegal so long as the first year's payment could be paid from either current revenue or a special fund, and since a special fund was created for the purpose, the contract was not illegal. Neither was it illegal to enter into the buyback agreement because the city controlled when the agreement would come into being. Finally, mandamus lay against the mayor because he, as a public officer, could be compelled to perform a ministerial act such as signing the contract in question.


OUTCOME: The court granted mandamus relief, ordering the mayor to sign the contract with the waste management company. The court held that the contract violated neither the constitutional provision nor the statute in question.

Women's Health Ctr. v. Panepinto


No. 21924, No. 21925, No. 21926


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


191 W. Va. 436; 446 S.E.2d 658; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 228


November 30, 1993, Submitted  
December 17, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissenting Opinion Dated July 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable John Hey, Circuit Judge. Civil Action No. 93--4721



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants health groups and individuals on behalf of all Medicaid eligible women in West Virginia sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which upheld the constitutionality of W. Va. Code § 9-2-11 (Supp. 1993), which bans the use of state Medicaid funds for abortions except in limited circumstances, in favor of appellee organization.


OVERVIEW: Appellants brought an action seeking to have that portion of Senate Bill 2, which became W. Va. Code § 9-2-11, declared unconstitutional. The trial court declared the challenged portion constitutional and the appellants sought review. The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the case. The court held that § 9-2-11 constituted a discriminatory funding scheme which violated an indigent woman's constitutional rights. The court found that because there was a federally-created right of privacy that the court was required to enforce in a non-discriminatory manner, it was inconsequential that no prior decision of the court expressly determined the existence of an analogous right. The court held that when the state government sought to act for the common benefit, protection, and security of the people in providing medical care for the poor, it had an obligation to do so in a neutral manner so as not to infringe upon the constitutional rights of its citizens. The court found that the provisions of § 9-2-11 constituted undue government interference with the exercise of the federally-protected right to terminate a pregnancy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which upheld the constitutionality of a statute that banned the use of state Medicaid funds for abortions except in limited circumstances.

 

146 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Billy Ray C. v. Skaff


No. 21894


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


190 W. Va. 504; 438 S.E.2d 847; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 223


November 2, 1993, Submitted  
December 15, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Mandamus.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, a juvenile, petitioned the court for a writ of mandamus against respondents, state officials, compelling them to hear his allegations of physical brutality against a state police officer. The juvenile also alleged that the state officials failed to create an adequate procedure to identify potential liability claims, pursuant to W. Va. Code § 29-12-5 (1986).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile alleged that he was the victim of an unwarranted physical attack by a state police officer. He claimed that the officer investigating his allegations threatened him and took no action against the abusive officer. The juvenile filed a petition seeking a writ of mandamus ordering the state officials to create a system whereby allegations of misconduct would be impartially investigated and compelling them to issue rules and regulations under W. Va. Code § 29-12-5 (1986) apprising the state board of risk with information relating to incidents that exposed the state to liability. The court granted the writ. The court held that: (1) the juvenile had a right under W. Va. Code § 15-2-21 (1977) to bring the use of excessive force by a police officer to the attention of the state superintendent of public safety and the superintendent was required to investigate the complaint; (2) the superintendent's duties required that he promulgate formal, written investigation procedures; and (3) the state board of risk was required to promulgate rules for state agencies to follow to notify the board of incidents that could create liability under the state's liability insurance policy.


OUTCOME: The court granted the juvenile's petition for writ of mandamus compelling the state officials to hear his allegations of physical brutality against a state police officer and to create adequate procedures for investigating such incidents and reporting potential liability claims to the state board of risk.

 

147 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Blair


No. 21558


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


190 W. Va. 425; 438 S.E.2d 605; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 209


September 21, 1993, Submitted  
December 14, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McDowell County. Honorable Booker T. Stephens, Judge. Civil Action Nos. AP-89-M-180; AP-89-M-181; AP-89-M-182; AP-89-M-183; AP-89-M-184; AP-89-M-185; AP-89-M-186.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the president of a water company, appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of McDowell County (West Virginia), which, upon a jury verdict, found him guilty on seven criminal misdemeanor warrants for violating W. Va. Code, 24-3-1 (1923) for failing to provide safe water to customers.


OVERVIEW: The water company was a private corporation, regulated by the Public Service Commission. The warrants brought against defendant by customers of the water company charged that defendant failed to establish and maintain adequate and suitable facilities for customers, in violation of Chapter 24-3-1 of the West Virginia Code. The water company was put into involuntary receivership. Defendant stated that he was financially unable to fix the problem since the banks would not lend him the money and the Public Service Commission had put on hold his request for a rate increase. The witnesses all stated that the water was not safe to drink. An engineer stated that the only way to take care of the problem would be to put a new system in which would cost two to three million dollars. The court addressed defendant's contention that his convictions under W. Va. Code, 24-3-1 (1923) should be reversed on the ground that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court agreed. It found that the statute did not provide any standard by which a jury could determine what was safe and adequate water service and the jury's subjective knowledge of ordinary commercial knowledge would vary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction.

State ex rel. Marockie v. Wagoner

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Mandamus.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator superintendent filed a petition for a writ of mandamus to determine the validity of certain revenue bonds.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the state legislature could dedicate taxes that historically had gone into the general revenue fund to create a separate fund to retire school building authority revenue bonds. The court denied the writ. The court believed that the legislature could not dedicate taxes in such a way without violating the debt strictures of W. Va. Const. art. X, § 4. The court found that no special fund was created except that which already existed in the general revenue fund. The court concluded, therefore, that that the bonds that were to be liquidated by dedicating a portion of the existing consumer sales tax, which was a general revenue fund tax, created new debt and violated art. X, § 4.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of mandamus.

Whitlow v. Board of Educ.


No. 21362


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


190 W. Va. 223; 438 S.E.2d 15; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 169


September 22, 1993, Submitted  
November 23, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Paul Zakaib, Jr., Judge. Civil Action No. 88-C-186



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which dismissed the injured party's personal injury action against defendant education board as time barred by W. Va. Code § 29-12A-6(b).


OVERVIEW: The injured party was 15 when she was severely injured by falling bleachers at her school. The injured party did not bring an action against the education board for over three years after the incident. The trial court determined that the injured party's action was time barred, pursuant to § 29-12A-6(b), but the court reversed and remanded the case. The court determined that § 29-12A-6(b) violated the Equal Protection Clause found in W. Va. Const. art. X, § III to the extent that it denied to minors the benefit of the statute of limitations provided in the general tolling statute, W. Va. Code § 55-2-15. The court held that the classification found in W. Va. Code § 29-12A-6(b) was subject to the rational basis test to determine if it violated the Equal Protection Clause. The court found that the classification was not rational based on social, economic, historic, or geographic factors. Further, the classification did not bear a reasonable relationship to the alleged governmental purpose of obtaining reasonable insurance rates. The court noted that minors were selected for disparate and more severe treatment than the insane, who were also covered under W. Va. Code § 55-2-15.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that the injured party's personal injury case against the education board was time barred. The case was remanded to the trial court.

Williams v. Brown


No. 21816


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


190 W. Va. 202; 437 S.E.2d 775; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 170


September 22, 1993, Submitted  
November 23, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certified Questions from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable John Hey, Judge. Civil Action No. 87-C-186



DISPOSITION: ANSWERED AND DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee brought an action in the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) against defendant attorney general, alleging breach of contract and breach of the duty of good faith and fair dealing. The trial court denied the attorney general summary judgment but certified the issue to the court, W. Va. Code § 58-5-2 (1967).


OVERVIEW: The public employee was employed by the state for 28 years. His employment as a state assistant attorney general was terminated by the newly-elected attorney general. No reason was given. W. Va. Code § 5-3-3 (1961) stated that assistant attorneys general served "at the pleasure of" the attorney general. The court held that § 5-3-3 indicated the legislature's intent to give the attorney general unfettered control over the hiring and firing of his assistants. Even if the statute did not contain the aforementioned phrase, the employment would still have been at-will because at-will removal power was implied when the employer had the power of appointment and the office carried no fixed term. The removal power could not have been contracted away. The attorney general did not owe his assistants a duty of good faith and fair dealing with regard to their employment.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified questions and dismissed the case.

 

152 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Mountaineer Park v. Polan


No. 21767


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


190 W. Va. 276; 438 S.E.2d 308; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 230


September 14, 1993, Submitted  
October 28, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITIONS FOR WRITS OF MANDAMUS



DISPOSITION: WRITS DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, West Virginia Lottery Commission (commission) and track owner, filed petitions for writs of mandamus to compel defendant state officials to approve a contract amendment and extension agreement with regard to video lottery terminals in the track owner's establishment pursuant to the State Lottery Act, W. Va. Code, §§ 29-22-1 to 29-22-28.


OVERVIEW: The lottery commission and track owner filed a writ of mandamus against the state officials arising out of a contract for the operation of video lottery machines by the track owner under the State Lottery Act. The machines were owned by a third party. The state officials' argued that the state had to own the terminals pursuant to W. Va. Const. art VI, § 36. The court held that art. VI, § 36 was clear and unambiguous, and it authorized the legislature to establish a state-run lottery and to prescribe laws for the regulation, control, ownership, and operation of the lotteries. However, the legislature failed to define what an electronic video lottery was or to authorize it. It was also unclear whether an electronic video lottery fell within the definition of a lottery in the State Lottery Act or art. VI, § 36 or whether it was the type of gambling prohibited in the state anti-gambling statutes. When the lottery commission expanded the lottery into video lottery machines it was acting without constitutional or statutory authority because such authority had not been delegated to it by the legislature. The court held that plaintiffs were clearly not entitled to the relief sought.


OUTCOME: The court denied the commission and track owner's petition for a writ of mandamus to compel approval of a contract amendment and contract agreement by the state officials.

 

153 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Public Serv. Comm'n v. Gainer


No. 21852


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


190 W. Va. 151; 437 S.E.2d 589; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 181



October 19, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of Mandamus



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, various state agencies and statutory administrators, filed a writ of mandamus against respondents, the West Virginia State's Auditor and the Treasurer, seeking to have W. Va. House Bill 2120 declared unconstitutional on the ground that it contained more than one subject, neither of which was related to the other.


OVERVIEW: The Bill contained three amendments to the West Virginia Code. One of the amendments was to West Virginia Code § 6-7-2a, which provided for the appointment, qualifications, and salaries of numerous state officers. It was amended to increase the salary of the West Virginia Commissioner of the Department of Motor Vehicles. The administrators were not being compensated pursuant to that statute, but their salaries were set forth at higher amounts in portions of the Code that addressed their powers and duties. Before § 6-7-2a was enacted, the administrators received salaries higher than those set by § 6-7-2a. The effect of the amendments on § 6-7-2a was to reduce their salaries. The court held that W. Va. Const. art VI, § 30 provided that no act could embrace more than one object and that was to be expressed in the title. The State Auditor and the Treasurer admitted that the Bill violated the "one subject" rule and requested that the court nullify the part that decreased the administrators' salaries. The court held that where the title included two subjects of legislation, the whole act fell because it was improper for the court to choose between the two.


OUTCOME: The court granted the requested writ of mandamus and declared W. Va. House Bill 2120 void in toto.

 

154 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Goines v. James


No. 21363


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


189 W. Va. 634; 433 S.E.2d 572; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 136


January 26, 1993, Submitted  
July 22, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wood County. Honorable Arthur N. Gustke, Circuit Judge. Civil Action No. 88-C-656



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant arrestees sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court Of Wood County (West Virginia) that entered judgment in favor of appellee officer and police department, finding they were immune from civil liability for effecting a warrantless arrest.


OVERVIEW: The arrestees challenged their arrest and argued that their Fourth Amendments rights were violated. Defendants contended the warrantless search of an officer to effect the arrest of defendants was unconstitutional. The issue before the court was whether the officers were entitled to qualified immunity in a civil claim. The court engaged in a lengthy review of cases involving warrantless arrests. The court affirmed and stated that a police officer could effect a warrantless arrest for the serious misdemeanor of driving under the influence by following the misdemeanant into his own home in hot pursuit, without a warrant. The court held that under the doctrine of qualified immunity, a police officer was absolved from civil liability for following a misdemeanant in hot pursuit into the residence of a third party, with neither a warrant nor the permission of the third party, in order to effect a warrantless arrest of the misdemeanant, so long as such entry violated no clearly established statutory or constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, finding that the officers did not have any civil liability for effecting a warrantless arrest.

State v. Nelson


No. 21273


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


189 W. Va. 778; 434 S.E.2d 697; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 138

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cabell County (West Virginia), which was entered upon a jury verdict finding her guilty of fraudulently secreting a public record in violation of W. Va. Code § 61-5-23 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was employed as a records clerk by the police department. While under surveillance in a drug investigation, defendant agreed to clean the felony convictions out of a confidential informant's record and not disclose the informant's entire criminal record to a potential employer. Defendant was convicted of fraudulently secreting a public record. On appeal, the court affirmed. Defendant was not a public officer. She was properly charged and tried pursuant to W. Va. Even if defendant presented some evidence of entrapment, the State rebutted the evidence by proving defendant's predisposition to commit the crime charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for fraudulently secreting a public record.

State ex rel. Walls v. Noland


No. 21495


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


189 W. Va. 603; 433 S.E.2d 541; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 117


May 11, 1993, Submitted  
July 16, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Thomas W. Steptoe, Jr., Judge. Civil Action No. 92-P-21



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant magistrate challenged a writ of prohibition granted by the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (West Virginia), which ordered her to halt proceedings against appellee check writer on four pending worthless check charges in violation of W.Va. Code § 61-3-39a et seq. The issue was whether the statute was unconstitutional because it permitted issuance of a warrant of arrest based on an information or complaint before a non-judicial officer.


OVERVIEW: The lower court ordered that the warrants be dismissed and concluded that the statute permitted issuance of an arrest warrant which was merely conclusory in nature and set forth only the statutory elements of the offense. The court agreed that the lower court erroneously concluded that the statutory complaint form allowed worthless check arrest warrants to be issued on inadequate information. The court opined that the check writer engaged in the kind of hypertechnical overanalysis that was unnecessary to establish probable cause. The four bad checks in question were attached to the complaint. The checks supplemented the complaint by explaining what transpired, providing an additional informational basis on which a magistrate could find probable cause. The information in the complaint, along with the four attached dishonored checks, provided a sufficient basis for the answer to the hypothetical question, "What makes you think that a defendant committed the offense charged?" The statutory complaint form was constitutionally sound.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's writ of prohibition and remanded the cause.

 

158 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Paige v. Canady


No. 21573


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


189 W. Va. 650; 434 S.E.2d 10; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 123


March 2, 1993, Submitted  
July 15, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] WRIT OF PROHIBITION



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State sought a writ of prohibition to prevent respondent Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) from entertaining a declaratory judgment action to settle a dispute between respondent oil company and the State's tax department.


OVERVIEW: In an earlier case, a wholesale gross receipts tax that was imposed against the oil company was declared unconstitutional. It was also determined that the decision invalidating the tax had to be applied retroactively. In accord with a State administrative notice, the tax department scheduled a hearing on the oil company's refund claim. Instead of proceeding with the hearing, the oil company sought a writ of mandamus from the circuit court. The circuit changed the case to a declaratory judgment action on the issue of whether the administrative notice was enforceable. On appeal, the court granted the State's request for a writ of prohibition preventing the declaratory judgment action. The court found that W. Va. Code § 11-10-14 (1978) and W. Va. Code § 11-10-14b (1992) provided judicial review of tax refund matters only after the tax department made its ruling on the refund. Furthermore, W. Va. Code § 11-10-14(1) (1978) explicitly prohibited declaratory judgments in refund cases. The administrative notice did not prescribe a specific result; it merely provided a procedure for obtaining a refund.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of prohibition requested by the State preventing the circuit court from entertaining a declaratory judgment action to settle a dispute between the oil company and the State's tax department.
