Kincaid v. Mangum


No. 21505


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


189 W. Va. 404; 432 S.E.2d 74; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 81


March 9, 1993, Submitted  
June 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certified Question from the United States District Court for the Southern District of West Virginia. Honorable Elizabeth V. Hallanan, Judge. Civil Action No. S:91-0721



DISPOSITION: CERTIFIED QUESTIONS ANSWERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action, defendants, sheriff, chief correctional officer, and county commissioners, challenged a preliminary injunction from the United States District Court for the Southern District of West Virginia, which was granted in favor of plaintiff inmates, who contended that confinement conditions were unconstitutional. The district court certified a question to the court regarding the omnibus bill that included jail standards.


OVERVIEW: In reviewing a class action involving plaintiff inmates and defendants, sheriff, chief correctional officer, and county commissioners, the court considered a certified question examining whether an omnibus bill authorizing the rules of many different agencies including the Minimum Jail Standards, 1988 W. Va. Acts 64-2-31(20)(9), violated the one-subject rule. The court held that it did. The court found that legislators did not have the actual rule before them when voting on the omnibus bill. The court held that if there was a reasonable basis for the grouping of various matters in a legislative bill, and if the grouping did not lead to logrolling or other deceiving tactics, then the one-object rule in W. Va. Const. art. VI, § 30 was not violated, but the use of an omnibus bill could lead to those problems. The court reformulated the certified question to explore whether its holding that an omnibus bill was unconstitutional should be applied prospectively and asserted that because its interpretation was not foreshadowed, prospective application was favored, as retroactivity would invalidate hundreds of rules and create too great a burden. The certified question was deemed answered.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question, holding that the omnibus bill was unconstitutional in violating the one-object rule. Recognizing the potential burden on the legislature, the court made its holding prospective and not retroactive. The case was remanded for further proceedings on the issues remaining between plaintiff inmates and defendants, sheriff, chief correctional officer, and county commissioners, consistent with this opinion.

 

160 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Foster v. City of Morgantown


No. 21671


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


189 W. Va. 433; 432 S.E.2d 195; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 78


May 4, 1993, Submitted  
June 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Mandamus



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner voters commenced a mandamus action, which sought to compel respondent, the City of Morgantown (city), to either repeal a zoning ordinance amendment that it had adopted or to submit the matter to a city-wide referendum.


OVERVIEW: The city amended its zoning ordinance. The voters circulated a petition requesting reconsideration of the amendment. They obtained enough signatures to satisfy the requirements of the city's charter. The city council rejected the petition. The voters then commenced a mandamus action. They maintained that the city was required to either repeal the amended ordinance or to hold a referendum on the matter. The court denied the voters' petition. Morgantown W. Va., City Charter § 8.01(b) required a referendum when the city council refused to repeal an ordinance in response to a petition. The court noted that the Zoning Enabling Act, specifically W. Va. Code § 8-24-23 (1969), did not authorize a public referendum on an amendment to a zoning ordinance. Furthermore, § 8-24-23, which was enacted after W. Va. Code § 8-12-4 (1969), superceded the referendum powers granted to home rule cities by § 8-12-4 with regard to amending zoning ordinances. Therefore, the amendment was not subject to a referendum and Morgantown W. Va., City Charter § 8.01(b) was inconsistent with W. Va. Code § 8-24-23 (1969) with regard to the amendment of the city's zoning ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court denied the voters' petition for a writ of mandamus, which would have compelled the city to either repeal a zoning ordinance amendment that it had adopted or to submit the matter to a city-wide referendum.

 

161 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rummer


No. 21095


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


189 W. Va. 369; 432 S.E.2d 39; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 71


January 26, 1993, Submitted  
May 25, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissenting Opinion filed May 28, 1993. Concurring Opinion filed May 28, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wood County. The Honorable Arthur N. Gustke, Judge. Criminal Indictment No. 90-F-133



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Wood County (West Virginia), which sentenced him to two concurrent terms of imprisonment upon his conviction of two counts of sexual abuse in the first degree. Defendant argued that both sentences arose from the same transaction and that they constituted unconstitutional double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: A young woman walking at night noticed a car following her at a slow rate of speed. Shortly after, she saw that a man was following her on foot. He grabbed her, put his hand up her skirt, and grabbed her breasts through her shirt. He fell on top of her and roughly fondled her breasts. Defendant argued that his two convictions were improper for one offense and violated the Double Jeopardy clause of both the state and federal constitutions. On appeal, the court noted that simply because two criminal statutes were construed to proscribe the same conduct did not mean that the Double Jeopardy Clause precluded the imposition of cumulative punishments pursuant to those statutes. The first step in the double jeopardy analysis was to determine whether the legislature intended that each violation be a separate offense. The term "sexual contact" defined in W. Va. Code § 61-8B-1(6) identified different acts that constituted sexual contact. Each act required proof of a fact that the other did not. The court held that defendant, who committed two separate acts of sexual contact on his victim, was convicted of each act without violating double jeopardy principles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Layton

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Andrew Frye, Jr. Judge. Criminal Action No. 90-F-8



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (West Virginia) convicting defendant of aggravated armed robbery and sentencing defendant to 47 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another individual robbed a dairy store; defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery and sentenced to forty-seven years in the state penitentiary. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel and the right to testify meaningfully on his on behalf. The trial court determined that defendant was disposed to perjury and instructed defense counsel not to participate in the questioning of defendant if he took the stand; defendant contented this caused defendant to take the stand without understanding he had the right not to do so. The court ruled that the trial court's instruction to counsel was proper. The court further held that defendant, who walked away from a bench conference, was not denied the right to be present at that critical stage of his trial and that the indictment was not defective. The court further ruled that the sentencing process in which defendant waived his right to file posttrial motions was not violative of defendant's due process rights and the sentence imposed was not based on any impermissible factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of aggravated robbery and assessing a sentence of 47 years in the state penitentiary.

Contractors Ass'n v. West Va. Dep't of Pub. Safety, Div. of Pub. Safety


No. 21519

189 W. Va. 685; 434 S.E.2d 357; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 43; 36 A.L.R.5th 909


February 2, 1993, Submitted  
March 25, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Paul Zakaib, Jr., Judge. Civil Action No. 91-C-315



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, IN PART; REVERSED, IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the West Virginia Department of Public Safety, sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which granted the motion for summary judgment of appellees, a corporation and an unincorporated association, in an action involving the diversion of funds from highways.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was in the business of constructing and repairing state highways and filed a declaratory action to determine whether the reimbursements to the Department violated W. Va. Const. art. VI, § 52, which prevented the diversion of funds from highways or whether the reimbursements exceeded the scope of W. Va. Code Ann. § 15-2-12(i), which authorized reimbursements to the Department for services relating to the duties of the Division of Motor Vehicles. There were six statutes under consideration. The court held that §§ 15-2-12(i), 17A-3-3(a)(7), 17B-1D-7, 17A-4-10(c) and 17A-6B-3(b) were constitutional under art. VI, § 52 since they all involved the cost of administering the duties of the Division of Motor Vehicles. However, § 17C-16-5 violated art. VI, § 52 to the extent it authorized the use of revenue collected from motor vehicles to operate or repair police barracks. Furthermore, the court found that the reimbursements by the Division to the Department for activities described as road patrol, traffic, operator examinations, and assisting with administrative functions did not exceed the scope § 15-12-2(i). The court affirmed the judgment in part, and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in part, and reversed in part in an action involving the diversion of funds from highways.

State ex rel. Paige v. Canady


No. 21573


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


1993 W. Va. LEXIS 35

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: WRIT OF PROHIBITION



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner tax department sought a writ of prohibition to prevent respondent Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) from entertaining a declaratory judgment action to settle a dispute between respondent corporation and the tax department.


OVERVIEW: The corporation asked the trial court to declare an administrative notice, which described the procedure that the corporation had to follow to obtain a tax refund, unconstitutional. The court awarded the writ. The court determined that W. Va. Code § 11-10-14 (1978) required the tax department first to rule on the amount of the refund, and then provided judicial review. The court explained that W. Va. Code § 11-10-14(i) (1978) made that the exclusive remedy for procuring a tax refund. The court noted that a declaratory judgment action was inappropriate because such an action would be intervention in the tax refund case not allowed by statute. The court concluded that an administrative notice put out by the tax department was not a regulation within the contemplation of the Administrative Procedure Act, W. Va. Code ch. 29A. The court determined that the burden of proof had to rest on the State to show by clear and convincing evidence the amount of tax passed on to consumers that did not affect the corporation's market performance if the State intended to reduce the refund by some amount based on the pass-on theory.


OUTCOME: The court awarded the writ of prohibition prayed for.

 

165 of 754 DOCUMENTS


E.H. v. Matin


NO. 21467


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


189 W. Va. 102; 428 S.E.2d 523; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 24


January 19, 1993, Submitted  
February 25, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable A. Andrew MacQueen, Judge. Civil Action No. 81-MISC-585



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMAND DELAYED FOR THIRTY DAYS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Acting Director of the West Virginia Department of Health And Human Resources, sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which enjoined the Department's plan to build a 150-bed mental health facility after appellee advocates filed a motion to prevent that construction in a long running mental health care case.


OVERVIEW: The trial court enjoined the Department from building a 150 bed mental health facility in a case that arose out of an earlier decision in which the court held that the State must comply with the provisions of W. Va. Code § 27-5-9 (1977) that concerned the treatment of mental patients. After a remand from that the decision the Department and the advocates sought and obtained funding for a new hospital. Revenue bonds were issued and site preparation had started when the advocates filed a motion to enjoin the construction on the ground that there were better ways to spend the money. The trial court stayed its order pending appeal. The court reversed because the trial court and the advocates had no authority to challenge the project. The court noted that under the principle of separation of powers found in W. Va. Const. art. V, § 1 the legislature and not the courts had the responsibility for economic decisions. The court noted that there was no constitutional objection to the project and that the advocates had impermissibly asserted a different position in the case. The court delayed the remand in order to obtain a report as to the need for further judicial supervision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court order and delayed remand for 30 days in order to obtain a report from the parties about the need for further judicial monitoring.

State v. Davis


No. 21111


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


189 W. Va. 59; 427 S.E.2d 754; 1993 W. Va. LEXIS 19


January 26, 1993, Submitted  
February 24, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wood County. Honorable George W. Hill, Judge. Criminal Action No. 89-F-26



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Wood County (West Virginia), which sentenced him to life imprisonment as a recidivist. The issue was whether the State's recidivist statute, W. Va. Code § 61-11-18, violated the proportionality principle implicit in the cruel and unusual punishment clause of the Eighth Amendment and W. Va. Const. art. III, § 5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of committing a burglary to an unoccupied building and stealing a total of $ 10. At his sentencing, because he had two previous felony convictions, the trial court imposed a life sentence under the recidivist or "three-strike" statute. On appeal, defendant argued that the statute imposed an unconstitutionally disproportionate sentence and violated the cruel and unusual clauses of both the state and federal constitutions. The court held that even under the statute, the trial court was required to consider the circumstances of the latest and earlier offenses, with particular consideration as to whether they were violent crimes or only property crimes. The court held that defendant's crimes, while felonies, were not violent, involved only crimes against property, and that defendant evidenced no tendency toward violence. Therefore, imposing a life sentence violated the proportionality principle. The court held that the five-year enhancement under the statute was the more appropriate sentence.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the trial court that imposed a life sentence on defendant and remanded for resentencing consistent with the court's opinion.

OVERVIEW: The former superintendent was transferred from his position as Wayne County Maintenance Superintendent to Area Maintenance Manager position at the District Two Headquarters, and although he had no specific duties assigned to him in his new position, he continued to receive the same salary. Thereafter, a democrat was appointed to replace the former superintendent in his former position. The former superintendent filed an action seeking to be reinstated to his former position and to have W. Va. Code § 29-6-4(d) declared unconstitutional. The trial court held that § 29-6-4(d) was unconstitutional insofar as it applied to the former superintendent's position and ordered the former superintendent reinstated to his former position. Judy v. White


No. 21324


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA

October 6, 1992, Submitted  
December 16, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Mandamus



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney sought a writ of mandamus against respondent judge ordering the judge to accept and approve for payment a fee voucher submitted by the attorney for services rendered to an indigent criminal client.


OVERVIEW: The attorney represented a client in a criminal action in which the client was convicted of four counts of involuntary manslaughter. He also represented the client on appeal. The attorney filed a voucher for the trial, which was paid, and for the appeal, which was reduced by the trial court. The attorney sought a writ of mandamus to force the trial court to approve the appellate fee voucher in its entirety. He argued that although the voucher was in excess of the amount permitted under W. Va. Code 29-21-13(a) (1990), it should have been approved because the client's four convictions should have been considered separate actions. The court noted that approval of the fee was within the trial court's discretion. The court ruled that single appeals, regardless of the number of convictions, constituted a single proceeding. The court further held that the trial court's reduction of the attorney's appellate fee to an amount less than the maximum for an appeal was not an abuse of discretion. In the future, the court advised the trial court to provide a brief explanation for reducing the fee amount claimed by court-appointed counsel.


OUTCOME: The court denied the attorney's petition for a writ of mandamus.

Town of Burnsville v. Cline


No. 21227


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


188 W. Va. 510; 425 S.E.2d 186; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 267


September 8, 1992, Submitted  
December 14, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Prohibition



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner town filed an action against respondent corporations seeking to collect business and occupational taxes from them. The corporations claimed that the town was selectively enforcing the tax provisions. Respondent judge, in the Circuit Court of Braxton County (West Virginia), granted the corporations' motion for inspection of the town's tax records. The town filed a writ of prohibition petition to prevent the disclosure of its records.


OVERVIEW: To support their claim that the town was attempting to selectively enforce the tax laws against them, the corporations successfully filed a motion for production and inspection, seeking disclosure of information relating to business and occupational tax returns that had been filed with the town. Information about the filing taxpayers was also sought. The town filed the petition after the judge granted the discovery motion. The court issued the requested writ, holding that W. Va. Code § 11-10-5d(a) (1987) was enacted to preserve taxpayer privacy and preserved the confidentiality of the contents of all tax returns, including business and occupation tax returns. The Equal Protection Clause, however, required the town to tax the corporations similarly to other taxpayers in their tax classification. In order to prove that they were being taxed at a different rate, or that the town had not taxed similarly situated businesses at all, the corporations needed some access to the town's tax returns. Making available a list of taxpayers who paid the tax to the town would not violate the confidentiality provisions of § 11-10-5d(a).


OUTCOME: The court granted the requested writ, but ordered that the corporations could review a list of the names of taxpayers who filed business and occupational tax returns with the town.

 

171 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Lufft v. Lufft


No. 20918


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


188 W. Va. 339; 424 S.E.2d 266; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 226


September 8, 1992, Submitted  
November 25, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ohio County. Honorable George L. Spillers, Judge. Civil Action No. 90-C-842



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Ohio County (West Virginia), which granted appellee father's request that a minor's last name be changed under W. Va. Code § 48-5-1 et seq. (1992) from the mother's last name to the father's last name. The father argued that the name change was required in order to protect the minor from the stigma of illegitimacy.


OVERVIEW: After the minor was born out of wedlock, the mother and father married, but later divorced. Thereafter, the mother gained custody, and the minor, in accordance with the birth certificate, retained the mother's last name. During a subsequent hearing, the father requested the minor's last name be changed to the father's. The request was granted. Accordingly, review was sought, and the court reversed. The court rejected the contention that a name change would protect against illegitimacy's stigma because: (1) there was no longer a legal stigma surrounding illegitimacy, (2) the marriage had legitimized the minor under W. Va. Code § 42-1-6, and (3) the divorce had not affected the legitimacy under W. Va. Code § 42-1-7. The court also held the trial court had failed to follow the procedures for a name change pursuant to W. Va. Code § 48-5-1 et seq. (1992). Moreover, the court held that because the name change involved a minor, proof that the change was in the minor's best interests was necessary over and above what W. Va. Code § 48-5-1 et seq. required. Finally, the court noted that the father had failed to change the minor's name at birth, pursuant to W. Va. Code § 16-5-24(d) (1992).


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment granting the father's request that a minor's last name be changed from the mother's last name to the father's last name.

O'Dell v. Town of Gauley Bridge


NO. 20741, NO. 21112, NO. 21260


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


188 W. Va. 596; 425 S.E.2d 551; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 229


September 16, 1992, Submitted  
November 24, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fayette County. Honorable John W. Hatcher, Jr., Judge. Civil Action No. 90-C-814

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Braxton County. Honorable Danny O. Cline, Judge. Civil Action No. 91-C-58

Certified Questions from the Circuit Court of Logan County. Honorable Eric H. O'Briant, Judge. Civil Action No. 90-C-506



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. ANSWERED AND DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of the separate decisions by the Circuit Courts of Fayette County, of Braxton County, and of Logan County (West Virginia), that W. Va. Code § 29-12A-5(a)(11) conferred immunity from suit upon political subdivisions in the state in personal injury cases where the claim or loss resulted from a claim covered by workers' compensation or employer's liability laws. Plaintiffs' three cases were consolidated for decision.


OVERVIEW: The plaintiffs suffered personal injuries that occurred during their course of employment. Each received workers' compensation benefits. Each subsequently brought lawsuits against their respective local political subdivision, alleging their injuries arose because of the actions or inactions of the public entities. The trial courts in two of the cases granted summary judgment for the political subdivisions. The third trial court certified certain questions relating to W. Va. Code § 29-12A-5(a)(11). On appeal, the court consolidated the three cases because they presented similar issues regarding the West Virginia Governmental Tort Claims and Insurance Reform Act, W. Va. Code § 29-12A-1 et seq. The court determined W. Va. Code § 29-12A-5(a) was designed to make liability insurance more affordable to political subdivisions by reducing the number of tort cases filed against them. The court held § 29-12A-5(a)(11) did not violate the equal protection principles of the state's constitution. The court ruled § 29-12A-5(a)(11) provided immunity to a political subdivision for all damages arising from a tortious injury, not merely for those compensated by workers' compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions of the two trial courts that granted summary judgments in favor of the political subdivisions. The court affirmed the rulings of the remaining trial court on the certified questions presented.

State ex rel. Smith v. Skaff


No. 21127


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


187 W. Va. 651; 420 S.E.2d 922; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 134


May 6, 1992, Submitted  
July 23, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified. Opinion Filed July 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: WRIT OF HABEAS CORPUS



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed suit to obtain a writ of habeas corpus, claiming that he was unlawfully confined in a regional jail and that he had effectively been denied parole. Respondents, the parole board, the division of corrections, and other public officials, answered the writ.


OVERVIEW: After pleading guilty to uttering, the inmate was sentenced to a term of one to 10 years in a state prison facility. He served about 13 months in a regional jail before he was transferred to a state facility, as a result of filing suit. Though the parole board scheduled the inmate for parole consideration on a certain date, the scheduling did not occur until after he was transferred. In granting the writ, the court held that under W. Va. Code §§ 25-1-15, 62-13-5, the division of corrections had a nondiscretionary duty to incarcerate inmates sentenced to prison to a state penal facility operated by the division. The division was prohibited from lodging inmates in a regional facility, absent the availability of space, once the inmates were sentenced to a division of corrections facility. Moreover, the parole board had a mandatory duty to consider an inmate for parole once he was eligible and to conduct a parole hearing, if necessary, in any facility where the inmate was being lodged, whether it was one within the division of corrections or a regional jail. Thus, the parole board violated W. Va. Code § 62-12-13 by refusing to consider the inmate for parole until after his transfer.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ and directed the division to comply with Dodrill by developing a plan within the next six months to provide a temporary arrangement to meet its obligation to house and detain all those lawfully sentenced to a state penal facility until the new prison was completed. The court also directed the parole board to conduct appropriate hearings for inmates eligible for parole.

Adkins v. Miller


No. 20273


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


187 W. Va. 774; 421 S.E.2d 682; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 159


January 28, 1992, Submitted  
July 23, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified. OpinionFiled July 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County. Honorable E. Lee Schlaegel, Jr., Judge. Civil Action No. 89-C-229.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employees sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Boone County (West Virginia), which dismissed their complaint against appellee Sheriff of Boone County (sheriff).


OVERVIEW: The former employees were hired by the sheriff's predecessor in office. When the sheriff took office, he replaced them with "his own people." The former employees filed a complaint against the sheriff, alleging that he fired them in violation of their constitutional rights. The trial court dismissed the complaint based on its interpretation of W. Va. Code § 7-7-7 (1982), which stated that sheriffs could "appoint and employ, to assist them in the discharge of their official duties for and during their respective terms of office, assistants, deputies and employees." On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that dismissals of non-civil service protected employees were improper and violative of First Amendment rights when made for political patronage reasons. The court noted that even if the legislature had intended to codify patronage dismissals by enacting § 7-7-7, such codification inherently violated the former employees' freedom to associate pursuant to both the First Amendment to the United States Constitution and W. Va. Const. art. III, § 7. The court thus interpreted the statute as not allowing the sheriff to make employment decisions based solely upon political reasons.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court dismissing the former employees' complaint and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Brown


No. 20472


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


188 W. Va. 12; 422 S.E.2d 489; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 138


January 22, 1992, Submitted  
July 10, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. Honorable J. Zane Summerfield, Circuit Judge. Civil Action No. 90-F-113



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Marion County (West Virginia), which dismissed 17 felony embezzlement counts against appellee former county prosecutor.


OVERVIEW: The former county prosecutor was charged with 17 felony embezzlement counts. The former county prosecutor filed a motion to dismiss the indictment on the grounds that W. Va. Code § 61-3-20 (1989) required proof of specific intent to convict a public official of embezzlement. The trial court agreed, and dismissed the indictment. The state sought review. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that: (1) the crime of embezzlement by a public official, as that offense was set forth in W. Va. Code § 61-3-20, was not a specific intent crime; (2) while proof of intent to steal or misappropriate was not required, proof that the public official intended to do the act or acts that resulted in the embezzlement was necessary to convict a public official of embezzlement pursuant to the second paragraph of W. Va. Code § 61-3-20; and (3) because the requisite intent might have been present in the instant case, the indictments were reinstated and the case was remanded to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and reinstated the 17 felony embezzlement counts against the former county prosecutor.

State v. Harding


No. 20847


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


188 W. Va. 52; 422 S.E.2d 619; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 120


April 28, 1992, Submitted  
July 10, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wood County. Honorable Daniel B. Douglass, Circuit Judge. Criminal Action No. 91-F-32



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction, after a jury trial was held in the Circuit Court, Wood County (West Virginia), for failure to appear, in violation of W. Va. Code § 62-1C-17b(a) (1989). Defendant argued the circuit court erred by admitting evidence regarding the revocation of his personal recognizance bond. He also claimed § 62-1C-17b(a) did not apply because after his bond was revoked, he was not released upon his personal recognizance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with burglary and larceny. After a mistrial was declared, he was placed on a personal recognizance bond pending trial and was directed to make weekly contacts with his probation officer and attend all court appearances. Defendant was notified that trial was scheduled for a certain date. Less than a month later, the probation officer informed the prosecutor that defendant failed to appear for two consecutive weeks. The circuit court then allowed the State's motion to revoke bond. After defendant failed to appear on the date scheduled for trial, he was indicted under § 62-1C-17b. On appeal, the court held that there was no merit to defendant's assertion that the circuit court erred by admitting testimony regarding his bond revocation on the ground that it was irrelevant. Defendant did not object to the testimony and in fact had introduced it himself through cross-examination of two state witnesses. Section 62-1C-17b applied to persons who, after having been released on personal recognizance, failed to appear. The intervening event of bond revocation did not render the statute inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

177 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lewis


No. 20930


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


188 W. Va. 85; 422 S.E.2d 807; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 124


April 29, 1992, Submitted  
July 6, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certified Questions from the Circuit Court of Greenbrier County. Honorable J. Zane Summerfield, Special Judge. Criminal Action No. 91-F-76



DISPOSITION: CASE DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Greenbrier County (West Virginia) certified questions arising out of a first-degree murder case, which resulted in a mistrial. The certification was made pursuant to W. Va. Code § 58-5-2 and W. Va. R. App. P. 13. The court granted the case to determine whether the state could obtain review of a ruling made in a criminal case by certified question under W. Va. Code § 58-5-2 (1967) or by writ of prohibition.


OVERVIEW: The first certified question asked whether the trial court properly admitted against defendant the confession of an alleged co-defendant who did not testify at trial. The second certified question asked: If the confession was improperly admitted, was a retrial of defendant barred by double jeopardy? The court dismissed the case as improvidently awarded and held that W. Va. Code § 58-5-2 was for certifying questions in civil cases. The state's right to appeal in a criminal case was contained in W. Va. Code § 58-5-30 and confined to those cases where a circuit court held an indictment bad or insufficient. The state was, however, entitled to a limited right to seek a writ of prohibition in a criminal case where the trial court acted outside of its jurisdiction. The state would have to demonstrate that the trial court's action was so flagrant that it was deprived of its right to prosecute the case or deprived of a valid conviction, and the prohibition proceeding could offend neither the Double Jeopardy Clause nor defendant's right to a speedy trial. Even if the issue were before the court in prohibition, however, the lack of a factual record foreclosed consideration of it.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the case as improvidently awarded.

State v. Jones


No. 20657


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


187 W. Va. 600; 420 S.E.2d 736; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 167

June 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Summary judgment granted by Jones v. Painter, 140 F. Supp. 2d 677, 2001 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 20905 (N.D. W. Va., 2001)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Jones v. Waid, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 128094 (N.D. W. Va., Mar. 4, 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at McGurgan v. Fox, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 154969 (N.D. W. Va., Sept. 29, 2011)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Jones v. Fox, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 49283 (N.D. W. Va., Jan. 17, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Morgan County. Honorable Thomas W. Steptoe, Jr., Judge. Criminal Indictment No. 90-F-3



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his life sentence under West Virginia's habitual criminal statute, W.Va. Code § 61-11-18 (1943), entered by the Circuit Court of Morgan County (West Virginia) after his conviction for making threats to kidnap and demand ransom under W.Va. Code § 61-2-14c.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from an incident, in which he held a repairman at gunpoint because the repairman was unable to fix defendant's stove. After the jury verdict, the State filed a habitual offender information, citing four prior convictions for crimes committed under a different name. These separate crimes included convictions for possession of a firearm by a felon, grand larceny, and burglary. The jury found that defendant was the person who was convicted of the prior crimes and sentenced him to life imprisonment as a habitual offender. Defendant argued that a conviction that occurred 15 years earlier was too remote in time to serve as the basis for the recidivist sentence. The court held that the deterrent purpose of W.Va. Code § 61-11-18 was not served if earlier felony convictions were excluded because of their ages. The court further held that that under W.Va. Code § 61-11-18, the State was not required to utilize its five-year enhancement proceeding before a life recidivist proceeding was invoked. Additionally, the court held that the imposition of the life recidivist sentence did not violate the proportionality doctrine under W.Va. Const. art. III, § 5.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

179 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. State Line Sparkler v. Teach


No. 20908


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


187 W. Va. 271; 418 S.E.2d 585; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 75


April 29, 1992, Submitted  
May 15, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Refused June 24, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Berkeley County. Honorable Patrick G. Henry, III, Judge. Civil Action No. 91-C-404



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a corporation and its principals, filed a writ of prohibition that sought to prevent respondents, the county building code enforcement officer, and county magistrates, from obtaining and from issuing criminal warrants to enforce provisions of the county building code. The Circuit Court of Berkeley County (West Virginia) ruled that the county ordinance that imposed such sanctions was unconstitutional. The county officials appealed.


OVERVIEW: The building code enforcement officer issued notices of building code violations to the corporation, and its principals, posted a stop-work notice, and filed criminal complaints that charged them with continuing to operate their business without required permits, and the principals and several employees were arrested. The principals filed a petition for a writ of prohibition that sought to prevent the officer and magistrates from obtaining, issuing, or enforcing warrants against them for alleged violations of the county building code. The circuit court determined that the county ordinance adopting the building code was unconstitutional insofar as it permitted imposition of penalties. On appeal, the court reversed the circuit court because, although there was no direct statutory authorization for the county to impose penalties, a grant of the police power to a local government necessarily included the right to carry it into effect and empowered the governing body to use proper means to enforce its ordinances. The power to punish by a pecuniary fine or penalty was implied from the delegation by the legislature of the right to enforce a particular police power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment that granted the corporation and its principals a writ of prohibition, which prevented the county from imposition of penalties for a violation of the county building code, and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

180 of 754 DOCUMENTS


In re Grubb


No. 20978


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


187 W. Va. 228; 417 S.E.2d 919; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 36


April 7, 1992, Submitted  
May 7, 1992, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] SUSPENDED WITHOUT PAY


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the West Virginia Judicial Investigation Commission, filed an action against respondent judge and sought the judge's temporary suspension without pay, pending the final disposition of criminal charges filed against the judge and the completion of the judicial disciplinary proceeding initiated by the Commission.


OVERVIEW: In a federal court proceeding, the judge was convicted of bribery, mail fraud, conspiracy, witness tampering, obstruction of justice, fraud, and racketeering activity. The Commission initiated an action to temporarily suspend the judge, without pay, pending the final disposition of the criminal charges against the judge, as well as the completion of the judicial disciplinary proceedings initiated by the Commission. The court granted the relief requested by the Commission. The court found that W. Va. Const. art. VIII, §§ 3 and 8 authorized the court to suspend the judge without pay, pending final disposition of the criminal charges against him or until the completion of the underlying disciplinary proceedings. The court held that, based on the facts of the case, temporary suspension without pay was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court rendered judgment in favor of the Commission and ordered the judge's temporary suspension without pay, pending the final disposition of the criminal charges filed against the judge and the completion of the judicial disciplinary proceeding initiated by the Commission.

 

181 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hensler


No. 20210


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


187 W. Va. 81; 415 S.E.2d 885; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 79


January 15, 1992, Submitted  
March 20, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Brooke County. Honorable W. Craig Broadwater, Judge. Criminal Action No. 89-F-94.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Brooke County (West Virginia), which sentenced him to two concurrent terms of from one-to-five years in the state penitentiary for two convictions of first-degree sexual abuse degree in violation of W.Va. Code, 618B-7 and for two other concurrent terms of from one-to-five years for two additional convictions of first-degree sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a minister who operated a private school in the basement of his home. A 14-year-old student accused defendant of four separate sexual assaults during the 1985-86 school year. The circuit court instructed the jury to consider whether the sexual assault resulted from "forcible compulsion" in accord with W.Va. Code, 61-8B-1(c) (effective July 1, 1986), which augmented the W.Va. Code, 61-8B-1(1)(a)-(b) definitions of such compulsion to include fear by a child under 16 years of age caused by intimidation, expressed or implied, by another person 4 years older than the victim. Because the effective date of 61-8B-1(c) was after the dates of the charged crimes, the court on appeal held that defendant was entitled to a new trial because his convictions violated prohibitions against ex post facto laws set forth in Article I, § 10, clause 1 of the United States Constitution and West Virginia Constitution, Article III, § 4. The court reasoned that W.Va. Code, 61-8B-1(c) was an ex post facto law that impermissibly altered the legal rules of evidence, and received less or different testimony than the law required at the commission of the offense, in order to convict defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

182 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Hamrick v. LCS Serv.


No. 20127


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 702; 414 S.E.2d 620; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 12


September 11, 1991, Submitted  
February 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 14, 1992. As Modified February 14, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Berkeley County. Honorable Patrick G. Henry III, Judge. Civil Actions No. 90-C-366 and 90-C-711



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant West Virginia Division of Natural Resources (DNR) sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Berkeley County (West Virginia), which denied the DNR's attempt to enforce W. Va. Code § 20-9-12b and W. Va. Code § 20-9-12c against appellee corporations in the DNR's action seeking a declaration that the corporations were operating a landfill without a certificate of site approval.


OVERVIEW: The DNR sought a declaration that the corporations were operating a landfill without a certificate of site approval in violation of W. Va. Code § 20-9-12b. The DNR sought a preliminary injunction. The trial court denied the DNR's attempt to enforce W. Va. Code § 20-9-12b and W. Va. Code § 20-9-12c against the corporations. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the trial court committed error by applying the doctrines of res judicata and collateral estoppel to the questions before it. The federal district court did not rule on the merit of the action at hand, which was whether the corporations were entitled to a permit under the law. Rather, the federal district court merely determined which law applied, namely the law in effect on February 3, 1988. Because the issue of the requirement of a certificate of site approval from county or regional solid waste authorities was not litigated in the federal district court, it was error for the trial court to apply principles of res judicata and collateral estoppel to bar litigation seeking to adjudicate the issue in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court, which denied the DNR's attempt to enforce state statutes against the corporations, in the DNR's action seeking a declaration that the corporations were operating a landfill without a certificate of site approval.

 

183 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Committee on Legal Ethics of W. Va. State Bar v. Printz


No. 20665


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


187 W. Va. 182; 416 S.E.2d 720; 1992 W. Va. LEXIS 44



January 14, 1992, Submitted  
March 23, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied May 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Recommendation of The Committee on Legal Ethics. Disciplinary Proceeding. Complaint No. 89-190.



DISPOSITION: CHARGES DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent attorney sought review of a recommendation of The Committee on Legal Ethics of the West Virginia State Bar that recommended that the court publicly reprimand respondent for violation of W. Va. D.R. 7-105(A) of the Code of Professional Responsibility (1978).


OVERVIEW: Respondent attorney assisted his father and a former employee, who had embezzled from the father, in a negotiation whereby the employee was to compensate the father and, in turn, the father agreed to withhold prosecution. A disciplinary proceeding was brought and the Committee on Legal Ethics of the West Virginia State Bar recommended that the court publicly reprimand respondent for violation of W. Va. D.R. 7-105(A) of the Code of Professional Responsibility (1978). After independently examining the record, the court disagreed with the Committee's recommendations and dismissed the complaint against respondent. The court held that W. Va. Code § 61-5-19 (1923), to the extent that it prohibited a victim or his agent from seeking restitution in lieu of a criminal prosecution, was void under the doctrine of desuetude. Because respondent did not have fair notice that he might be subject to prosecution under the statute, he did not act inappropriately and he could not be sanctioned under the disciplinary rule.


OUTCOME: The court disagreed with the ethics committee that recommended that the court publicly reprimand respondent attorney for violation of the Code of Professional Responsibility, holding that the underlying statute that respondent allegedly violated was void under the doctrine of desuetude. Respondent did not have fair notice that he could be prosecuted under the statute and did not act inappropriately.

 

184 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Charleston Area Medical Ctr.


No. 20109


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 720; 414 S.E.2d 877; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 271


September 25, 1991, Submitted  
December 20, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Refused February 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Patrick Casey, Judge. Civil Action No. 88-C-3685. AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia) entered a judgment for the plaintiffs, an infant and his parents, and, holding that the $ 1Million "cap" on noneconomic loss in a medical liability action against the defendant doctor, as set forth in the West Virginia Medical Professional Liability Act of 1986, W. Va. Code §§ 55-7B-1 to 55-7B-11(1986) was unconstitutional, awarded $ 4.5 Million in noneconomic damages. The doctor appealed.


OVERVIEW: A doctor contended that the "cap" on noneconomic loss was constitutional. The parents of the injured infant argued that it violated the equal protection, special legislation, due process, "certain remedy," and jury trial provisions of the West Virginia Constitution. The court held: (1) W. Va. Code § 55-7B-8, as amended, which provided a $ 1 Million limit or "cap" on the amount recoverable for a noneconomic loss in a medical professional liability action was constitutional; and (2) the "cap" applied as one overall limit to the aggregated claims of all plaintiffs against a health care provider, rather than applying to each plaintiff separately. The test for "certain remedy" purposes required the existence of a clear social or economic problem, and that the legislative alteration of a common-law right or remedy must be a reasonable method of eliminating or curtailing it. Because the right to file a lawsuit for tort damages was not a fundamental right, the "rational basis" test for state constitutional equal protection purposes was applicable to statutory limitation on remedies in certain common-law causes of action, such as statutory "caps" on the recoverable amount of damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the injured infant and his parents, but reversed the award of noneconomic damages, and adjusted the noneconomic damages in conformity with its opinion.

 

185 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Maynard


No. 20444


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 421; 412 S.E.2d 822; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 257


November 6, 1991, Submitted  
December 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Prohibition.



DISPOSITION: Writ Granted


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner labor commissioner filed a petition for a writ of prohibition. The commissioner, who was named as a defendant in a declaratory judgment action in the Circuit Court of Mingo County (West Virginia), contended that venue was improper in Mingo County and sought a writ of prohibition against respondent circuit judge, prohibiting further proceedings in the matter.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, judge and bank, conceded that the commissioner was a state agent, but they contended that for the remaining defendants, corporations and private individuals, venue was proper in Mingo County and that once venue was proper for one defendant, it was proper for all other defendants subject to process. What respondents failed to recognize was that the principle did not usually apply when one of the defendants was the governor, any other state officer, or a state agency pursuant to W. Va. Code § 14-2-2(a)(1). Respondents contended that an exception to W. Va. Code § 14-2-2 was carved out because the recovery sought was from private sources rather than public funds. However, that exception was recognized because it did not defeat the manifest purpose of § 14-2-2. The real party in interest in the case was a state officer. The purpose of § 14-2-2 could easily be defeated if every time a state officer were sued, a private citizen or corporation was also sued. The court declined to sanction such a result. The court found that the order dismissing the commissioner's motion exceeded the trial court's lawful jurisdiction, and it issued a writ of prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court granted a writ prohibiting the judge from acting further in the declaratory judgment action by a bank against the commissioner, the corporations, and private individuals.

 

186 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Tsapis


No. 20477


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 642; 413 S.E.2d 699; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 270


November 6, 1991, Submitted  
December 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Refused February 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Prohibition



DISPOSITION: Writ Denied


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Circuit Court of Brooke County (West Virginia) denied their motion to suppress certain evidence, petitioner employees filed a petition for a writ of prohibition against respondents, judge and prosecutor, to prevent further criminal proceedings against them. The employees argued that the evidence was obtained by a nonresident private investigator in violation of W. Va. Code § 61-6-11 (1923).


OVERVIEW: The employees were charged with delivery of marijuana, a controlled substance, after their employer hired an out-of-state investigator. The employees' motion to suppress the investigator's evidence was denied by the trial court and in an original proceeding in the court, they sought a writ of prohibition on the ground that the evidence was obtained in violation of § 61-6-11. The court denied the writ and dismissed the rule to show cause, concluding that § 61-6-11 discriminated against nonresident investigators. No law prevented the use of resident investigators. In addition, the ability to pursue employment in another state was a fundamental right which was protected by the Privileges and Immunities Clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, cl. 1. The reason for § 61-6-11, a nonresident's presumed unfamiliarity with state laws, did not satisfy the substantiality test so as to justify excluding nonresident investigators from employment. Section 61-6-11 violated the Privileges and Immunities Clause insofar as it applied to nonresident private investigators, and it did not provide a basis for excluding evidence gathered by any nonresident investigators pursuing their livelihood in the state.


OUTCOME: The court denied the employees' petition for a writ of prohibition and it dismissed the rule to show cause that was previously issued.

Mullett v. Huntington Police Pension Bd.


No. 20277


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 488; 413 S.E.2d 143; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 264


September 17, 1991, Submitted  
December 18, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the Circuit Court of Cabell County. Honorable Dan O'Hanlan, Circuit Judge. Civil Action No. 90-C-952.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pension board sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cabell County (West Virginia), which found that appellee policeman was eligible for early pension benefits.


OVERVIEW: The policeman began working for the department in 1968. He enlisted in the National Guard while working for the department. His service in the Guard included weekend drills, annual summer camp, and various other duty assignments. He was never called to active duty. In 1990, the policeman applied for a pension pursuant to W. Va. Code §§ 8-22-25 and 8-22-7 (1985), asserting that his service in the Guard, in total, amounted to more than the one year required service. The board denied the application for benefits, holding that his employment had not been "interrupted" by Guard service. The policeman appealed to the trial court, which ordered the pension board to reconvene and reconsider the application based on the statutes in effect in 1968 on his date of hire. The board again denied benefits. The trial court reversed upon the policeman's appeal. The board sought review. The court held that the statute in place at the time the policeman's interest in his pension became vested controlled his receipt of benefits. The year of service required for eligibility for early pension was a consecutive year; the policeman's intermittent Guard service did not qualify.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

State ex rel. Dadisman v. Caperton


No. 20419


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 627; 413 S.E.2d 684; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 276


November 6, 1991, Submitted  
December 17, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Refused February 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Mandamus. WRIT DENIED



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state and state agencies, filed an application for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent public officials requesting relief concerning the under funding of state employer contributions to the then state division of the retirement system and that the amendment to W. Va. Code § 5-10-28 (1990) was an unconstitutional impairment of the contractual rights.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed a writ of mandamus. The two primary issues in the case invoking the original jurisdiction of the court were: (1) whether there had been compliance with the particular mandate of the court concerning the under funding of state employer contributions to the then state division of the retirement system for four fiscal years and (2) whether the amendment to § 5-10-28 eliminating, for most accounting purposes, the two divisions of the retirement system (the state division and the public employer division for non state public employees) was an unconstitutional impairment of the contract between the system and the non state employees. The court concluded that the petitioners had failed to show their entitlement to the requested mandamus relief. The court denied the writ, holding that the 1990 amendment to § 5-10-28 did not constitute an unconstitutional impairment of the contractual rights of the former public employer division's beneficiaries or retirees for the system had always owned all of the assets.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioners' application for a writ of mandamus to compel respondents requesting relief concerning the under funding of state employer contributions to the then state division of the retirement system and that the amendment to the enabling statute was an unconstitutional impairment of the contractual rights.

 

189 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Benedict v. Polan


NO. 20116


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 452; 413 S.E.2d 107; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 234


October 1, 1991, Submitted  
December 13, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County. Honorable Patrick Casey, Circuit Judge. Civil Action Number 90-Misc. 297



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART AFFIRMED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, secretary, Department of Administration; Commissioner, Division of Finance and Administration; Auditor; and Treasurer, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which denied mandamus to compel appellees, Commissioner of Agriculture, State taxpayers, and the Board of Osteopathy, to comply with House Bill No. 4456 (1990) (West Virginia) because the bill was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court found that the bill unconstitutionally transferred monies from three special revenue accounts for the benefit of the Division of Human Services, Department of Health and Human Resources (DHS). Specifically, the circuit court found that the bill violated § 30 of Article VI of the West Virginia Constitution. Upon review, the court found that because the bill clearly enunciated its purpose as a supplementary appropriations bill, it did not violate § 30. However, the court held that the legislature could not amend or violate substantive statutes by passage of a supplemental appropriation bill that required money to be spent and expropriated in a manner contrary to that already provided by statute. Thus, the bill violated West Virginia Code § 12-2-2(j). The court found that the circuit court erred in refusing to recognize the "historical method analysis" as a means of projecting the existence of surplus in a special revenue account and in finding the bill unconstitutional on that basis. There was no prohibition on the use of historical averaging for determining the existence of a surplus when a supplemental appropriation was sought before the end of the fiscal year.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision in part and affirmed the decision in part.

Randall v. Fairmont City Police Dep't


No. 20089


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 336; 412 S.E.2d 737; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 232


September 24, 1991, Submitted  
December 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. Honorable Ronald E. Wilson, Special Judge. Civil Action No. 88-C-505-W



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, estate of decedent and injured victims, appealed from the Circuit Court of Marion County, West Virginia, which dismissed the action against defendants, city, police department and employees, for failure to state a claim in light of the West Virginia Governmental Tort Claims and Insurance Reform Act of 1986 (the Act), W. Va. Code § 29-12A-5(a)(5) (1986) and W. Va. Code § 29-12A-5(b) (1986).


OVERVIEW: The decedent repeatedly requested police protection against a man that was harassing and threatening her. The police took no action, despite that he had seriously injured her and had an outstanding arrest warrant. She was driving when she saw the man following her. She parked directly beside the police station and blew her horn in an unsuccessful attempt at police help. The man shot her and injured a passenger. The court affirmed the circuit court's finding that the qualified tort immunity provisions of the West Virginia Governmental Tort Claims Act were constitutional. The dispositive procedural issue, however, was the propriety of the dismissal. The court found the dismissal was improper due to a material factual issue raised by the complaint of whether a special relationship existed between plaintiffs and defendants. Lacking a clear expression to the contrary, the court found that the Act incorporated the common-law special duty rule and did not immunize a breach of a special duty to provide, or the method of providing, such protection to a particular individual. If proved, such a relationship created duties not covered by the immunity provisions of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that the qualified tort immunity provisions of the governmental tort claim act was constitutional. On the other hand, the court reversed the circuit court's dismissal for failure to state a claim because the decedent's estate and the injured passengers raised a factual issue of whether they had a special relationship with the city. Therefore, the court remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

191 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Pritchard v. Arvon


No. 20202


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 445; 413 S.E.2d 100; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 241


September 18, 1991, Submitted  
December 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certified Questions from the Circuit Court of Boone County. Honorable W. Jack Stevens, Judge. Civil Action No. 90-C-205



DISPOSITION: CERTIFIED QUESTIONS ANSWERED; CASE DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant superintendent sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Boone County (West Virginia), which denied his motion to strike his name from the pleadings based on the statutory immunity in W. Va. Code § 29-12A-5(b) (1986) of the Governmental Tort Claims and Insurance Reform Act (the Act) in an action brought by plaintiff injured child's mother.


OVERVIEW: The superintendent filed a motion to strike his name from the pleadings on the ground that he was immune from liability under the Act. The lower court denied his motion and held that the Act was unconstitutional and the court reversed. The court found that the Act did not extinguish causes of action against governmental agencies, but merely removed individuals as defendants. The court concluded that the Act was reasonable for the purpose in which it was enacted, to limit liability insurance costs for political subdivisions. The court held that the Act's provisions, which provided immunity for an employee of a political subdivision under some circumstances, did not violate the certain remedy provision of W. Va. Const. art. III, §17, nor did it violate the equal protection principles contained in the W. Va. Const. art. III, § 10. The court held that §29-12A-16(d) of the Act, which provided that the purchase of liability insurance did not constitute a waiver of any immunity or defense of the political subdivision or its employees did not violate equal protection principles because it was rationally related to the legitimate government purpose.


OUTCOME: The court held that the lower court erred in determining that the provisions of the Act were unconstitutional and the court dismissed the mother's personal injury case.

 

192 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Common Cause v. Tomblin


NO. 20325


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 537; 413 S.E.2d 358; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 218


September 11, 1991, Submitted  
December 9, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for a Writ of Mandamus. WRIT GRANTED AS MOULDED



DISPOSITION: Writ as moulded, awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner activists applied for a writ of mandamus against respondent legislative committee chairman, claiming, inter alia, that a budget digest prepared by them under W. Va. Code § 4-1-18 differed significantly from the actual budget bill and that it violated the separation of powers doctrine pertaining to legislative vetoes.


OVERVIEW: After the budget bill for 1992 was passed by the West Virginia legislature, the chairmen of the conferees committee on the budget met and prepared a digest of the budget bill, as required by § 4-1-18. Claiming that this process violated an open meetings law and that the budget digest improperly differed from the actual budget bill that passed the legislature, the activists petitioned for mandamus relief. In granting relief in part, the supreme court ruled that, although a budget digest did not have the force and effect of law and § 4-1-18 was therefore not facially a violation of the constitutional separation of powers doctrine, to prevent the statute from being unconstitutional in its application, digests were required to include a disclaimer that they did not have the force and effect of law. Moreover, it was a violation of § 4-1-18 to prepare the digest without the approval of a majority of a quorum of the full conferees committee.


OUTCOME: The activists' petition was granted in part and denied in part and a writ of mandamus, as molded, was awarded. The court further declared that, although a budget digest did not have the force and effect of law, a budget was required to say it did not have that force and effect and it was required to be prepared by a quorum of the entire conferees committee on the budget.

State ex rel. Hayden v. Wyo. County Corr. Officer Civil Serv. Comm'n


No. 20103


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


186 W. Va. 239; 412 S.E.2d 237; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 210


September 18, 1991, Submitted  
December 6, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wyoming County. Honorable John S. Hrko, Judge. Civil Action No. 89-C-473



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, IN PART, AND WRIT, IN PART, VACATED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Wyoming County Correctional Officer Civil Service Commission sought review of an order entered by the Circuit Court of Wyoming County (West Virginia), which ordered the Commission to include appellee's name on a certified list of eligible candidates for a temporary correctional officer position. The Commission was not properly constituted, and that, consequently, all actions taken by the Commission during that time were void.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court also directed the Commission to pay appellee back pay, to award him seniority rights, and to reform itself. The Commission was notified pursuant to W. Va. Code, 7-14B-11 that a position for a temporary correctional officer was available. The Commission was to supply a list of eligible candidates to be certified to the sheriff. One of the members of the Commission changed his political affiliation and the composition of the Commission violated W.Va. Code, 7-14B-3. The Commission certified a list to the sheriff, but appellee's name was not included. He filed a petition for a writ of mandamus. Upon review, the court found that at the time the Commission put together the list, it had a de jure existence, but the appropriate individuals were not occupying de jure positions within the organization. However, the individuals were de facto officers, and they were not precluded from performing valid acts insofar as the public and third persons were concerned. Because it was only the Commission's duty to certify a list of eligible candidates and it had no authority to hire or pay correctional officers, it could not be compelled to award appellee back pay.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portions of the judgment that found the acts of the Commission void and that related to the hiring or back pay of appellee. The writ of mandamus in that regard was declared a nullity. In all other respects, it was upheld.

 

194 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Butler v. Tucker


No. 19998


SUPREME COURT OF APPEALS OF WEST VIRGINIA


187 W. Va. 145; 416 S.E.2d 262; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 281



September 24, 1991, Submitted  
April 2, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied May 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Nicholas County. Honorable James H. Wolverton, Judge. Civil Action No. 90-C-104.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant video rental stores sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court of Nicholas County (West Virginia), which ruled in favor of appellees, county, sheriff and chief of police, and declared an anti-pornography ordinance adopted by the Nicholas County Commission constitutional pursuant to W. Va. Code § 7-1-4 (1990).


OVERVIEW: The stores filed a petition for declaratory judgment challenging the constitutionality of the commission's anti-pornography ordinance. The trial court declared that the ordinance was constitutional. On appeal the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that W. Va. Code § 7-1-4 (1990), defining obscenity allowed each county to decide whether to adopt a local ordinance and was not constitutionally vague. The court stated that the statute met the constitutional standard for obscenity because it embodied the general obscenity test authorized by the United States Supreme Court and incorporated specific examples of obscenity set out by the United States Supreme Court. The court noted that the ordinance's language tracked the statute's and was therefore facially constitutional. The court found that the statute's language was complete and unambiguous and while counties could decide whether and in what form to adopt a pornography ordinance, it could not be made more restrictive that the form already adopted by the legislature. The court noted that the power to adopt the ordinance was delegated to the county and did not constitute usurpation of the legislative function.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court declaring that the statute which authorized county commissions to enact anti-pornography ordinances was not an unconstitutional delegation of power.

 

195 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Deberry


No. 19990


Supreme Court of Appeals of West Virginia


185 W. Va. 512; 408 S.E.2d 91; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 137


May 14, 1991, Submitted  
July 25, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Harrison County; Honorable Daniel L. McCarthy, Judge; Criminal Action No. 90-F-15-1.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Harrison County (West Virginia), which dismissed an indictment returned against defendant on the charge of felonious neglect under W. Va. Code § 61-8D-4(b) (1988).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted after the death of her daughter. The State asserted that defendant committed felonious neglect when she took her daughter to a party where the daughter was encouraged to drink alcohol until she lost consciousness. Defendant then had the girl taken home a put to bed, where she was found dead the next morning. The circuit court dismissed the indictment on the grounds that the term "neglect" as used in § 61-8D-4(b) was unconstitutionally vague. The court reversed holding that the statute passed constitutional muster. The term "neglect" was defined in W. Va. Code § 61-8D-1(6) (1988) and was not itself vague. "Neglect" as defined by § 61-8D-1(6) was the unreasonable failure by a parent to exercise a minimum degree of care to assure a minor child's physical safety or health. W. Va. Code § 61-8D-4(b) was based on a negligence concept and did not require specific intent. Thus, the use of the term "neglect" in § 61-8D-4(b) did not create unconstitutional vagueness because the use of the term gave persons of ordinary intelligence fair notice that his or her contemplated conduct was prohibited and it also provided adequate standards for adjudication.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment.

 

196 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Devrnja v. W. Va. Bd. of Med.


No. 19907


Supreme Court of Appeals of West Virginia


185 W. Va. 594; 408 S.E.2d 346; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 135


May 15, 1991, Submitted  
July 23, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Refused September 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County; Honorable John Hey, Judge; Civil Action No. 89-AA-25.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Kanawha County (West Virginia), which upheld an order of appellee board of medicine revoking the doctor's license to practice medicine and surgery.


OVERVIEW: The board relied upon a decision from the court holding W. Va. Code § 30-14-8a (1987) void and revoked the doctor's license. He had been granted a license previously based upon § 30-14-8a, which provided for the permanent licensure of any resident physician who had held a temporary certificate in West Virginia prior to January 1, 1987. The doctor was otherwise not qualified to practice medicine in West Virginia, having repeatedly failed the Federation of Licensing Boards Examination (FLEX exam). The doctor appealed, contending that the board's decision to void § 30-14-8a should not apply retroactively. The circuit court affirmed the board's decision. On appeal, the court held that: (1) where § 30-14-8a was of recent origin and was a radical departure from prior practice, the doctor did not have any settled expectation arising from a longstanding practice; (2) where § 30-14-8a affected a narrow class of physicians, retroactive application of the ruling was more sustainable; (3) there was a substantial public policy served in requiring doctors to pass the FLEX exam; and (4) therefore, the circuit court was correct in giving retroactive application to the ruling voiding § 30-14-8a.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the circuit court, which affirmed the board's revocation of the doctor's license.

Lewis v. Canaan Valley Resorts


No. 19780


Supreme Court of Appeals of West Virginia


185 W. Va. 684; 408 S.E.2d 634; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 126


March 5, 1991, Submitted  
July 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certified questions from the Circuit Court of Tucker County; Honorable C. Reeves Taylor, Judge; Civil Action No. 89-C-120.



DISPOSITION: CERTIFIED QUESTIONS ANSWERED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the personal injury action of plaintiffs, husband and wife, the Circuit Court of Tucker County (West Virginia) certified questions to the court to determine the constitutionality of the West Virginia Skiing Responsibility Act, W. Va. Code §§ 20-3A-1 to 20-3A-8 (the Act), after the trial court granted a motion to strike defendant ski resort's defense under the Act.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife filed suit against the ski resort for personal injuries sustained while the husband disembarked from a ski lift at the ski resort. The wife sued for loss of spousal consortium. The ski resort contended that the action was barred by the Act. The husband and wife moved to strike the defense that the action was barred by the Act, which limited the ski resort's liability. The trial court eventually granted the motion to strike, based upon its conclusion that the Act was unconstitutional in that it violated equal protection principles of W. Va. Const. art. III, § 10, and U.S. Const. amend. 14, § 1; the "open courts" provision of W. Va. Const. art. III, § 17; and the proscription against special legislation of W. Va. Const. art. VI, § 39. Subsequently, the trial court certified questions to the court regarding the constitutionality of the Act. The court concluded that the Act was constitutional on its face despite the claims that it denied equal protection or constituted impermissible special legislation, or violated the "certain remedy" provision of the state's constitution.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified questions by finding the Act constitutional and remanded to the trial court with instructions to deny the motion of the husband and wife to strike the ski resort's affirmative defense.
