Geibel v. Clark


No. 19743


Supreme Court of Appeals of West Virginia


185 W. Va. 505; 408 S.E.2d 84; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 114


May 8, 1991, Submitted  
July 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wayne County; Honorable Robert G. Chafin, Judge; Civil Action No. 88-C-339.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners under a tax deed challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Wayne County (West Virginia), which voided the tax deed based on the invalidity of W.Va. Code § 11A-3-2(1965) and granted plaintiff, a representative of the prior deceased owners, summary judgment as to the issue of laches in the representative's action to set aside the tax deed and for adverse possession.


OVERVIEW: The representative was the daughter of the prior owners, who were both deceased. About 25 years earlier, the lot was purchased by a sheriff on behalf of West Virginia for nonpayment of ad valorem real property taxes. Pursuant to W. Va. Code § 11A-3-2 (1965), advance notice of the sheriff's tax sale was not required to be mailed to the prior owners. Three years later, a tax deed was delivered to the landowners. However, the representative and her parents, the prior owners, continued to reside at the property. When the prior owners died, the representative learned that the landowners owned the lot and she sought to void the tax deed to the landowners. The court held that a holding that § 11A-3-2 was invalid because it permitted the sale of real property without personal notice to affected owners and others having an interest in the property was not to be applied retroactively. The court explained that such a general retroactive application had a severe disruptive effect on land titles in West Virginia. The court further held that there were issues of fact remaining as to the representative's allegations of laches and adverse possession and that summary judgment was improper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that the tax sale was void, vacated the summary judgment as to laches, and remanded for further proceedings on a related issue of adverse possession raised in the pleadings.

 

199 of 754 DOCUMENTS


Tony P. Sellitti Constr. Co. v. Caryl


No. 19918


Supreme Court of Appeals of West Virginia


185 W. Va. 584; 408 S.E.2d 336; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 117


May 7, 1991, Submitted  
July 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Hancock County; Honorable Callie Tsapis, Judge; Civil Action No. 87-P-121W.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State Department of Tax and Revenue (department) sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Hancock County (West Virginia), which vacated plaintiff taxpayer's past-due tax, additions to tax, and penalties, and held that the taxpayer was considered to be in the business of contracting for purposes of the consumers sales and service and use tax exemptions for the purchase of things used in the business of contracting.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a speculative builder, challenged the taxes assessed by the department. The trial court granted judgment for the taxpayer. The court reversed, in part, and affirmed, in part, the trial court's decision. The court held that speculative builders were not considered as engaged in the business of contracting for purposes of the consumers sales and service tax exemption and use tax exemption, for purchases of things directly used or consumed in the business of contracting. Speculative builders were engaged in the business activity of constructing improvements to real property that they owned with the intent of selling the improved realty to other persons. It was not an equal protection violation for the department to treat actual contractors differently from speculative builders because there was a rational basis for treating the two classes differently. Speculative builders were essentially engaged in sales of their own improved realty, whereas contractors worked under contracts for the owners of real estate. Because the taxpayer had a good faith belief that his position was legal, the court affirmed the trial court's order vacating his additions to tax and penalties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision vacating the taxpayer's additions to tax and penalties. The court reversed the trial court's decision vacating the taxpayer's past-due tax and holding that the taxpayer was considered to be in the business of contracting for purposes of the consumers sales and service tax exemption and the use tax exemption.

 

200 of 754 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hayes


No. 19783


Supreme Court of Appeals of West Virginia


185 W. Va. 664; 408 S.E.2d 614; 1991 W. Va. LEXIS 99


May 8, 1991, Submitted  
July 12, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Mercer County; Honorable John R. Frazier, Judge; Criminal Action No. 89-F-130.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED FOR PROPER SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Mercer County (West Virginia), which convicted defendant of violating W.Va. Code § 61-3-39 (1977), which related to the issuance of a worthless check in exchange for property or a thing of value.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction but remanded for a new sentence. The court found that W.Va. Code § 61-3-39 (1977) and W. Va. Code § 61-3-39(a) (1977) were not constitutionally vague and were clear in their use of terms. The court held that defendant obtained an interest in a commercial lease when he issued a worthless check for a security deposit and that the lease represented a thing of value under W. Va. Code § 61-3-39. The court concluded that defendant was not entitled to a lesser included offense instruction because the statutes considered completely different crimes. The court also found that the trial judge based his sentencing decision on the total circumstances not the limits of W. Va. Code § 61-3-39(a) (1977). The court also held that defendant was not prejudiced by the prosecutor's remarks during his arguments in closing statements. Finally, the court found that defendant was sentenced to a prison term of 1 to 10 years, but the maximum under law was only 1 to 5 years for his crime, and the court remanded the case for a sentence correction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant' conviction of the issuance of a worthless check in exchange for property or a thing of value and remanded back to the trial court for the imposition of a proper sentence.
